The shape moved through blue-white bodies first. Ren saw the medical need they had made flinch: not fear as humans held it, but a constriction in relation. Blue-white treaty bodies tightened around the care-passage current to prove it would not fail. That tightening cost flexibility. A graft convoy correction that should have passed through a broad relation had to squeeze through a narrower one.

Then the sentence moved through amber bodies.

Threatens became accusation. Amber withdrawal bodies hardened, not because they wanted medical passage to fail, but because the sentence made private bypass pressure sound like a weapon held by withdrawal itself. Their defensive hardening pushed against the current's edges.

Then green-white repair sheets.

They thickened to protect the current from a danger Ren had overstated. Tissue that had been monitoring the cracked vote body shifted attention for forty-two seconds. The cracked body cooled by one tenth of a degree.

Vessel-kin showed that degree to Ren.

Not with blame.

That would have been easier.

With measurement.

Ren gripped the chair.

The chamber did not stop.

The pressure shape moved into the human gallery. The clerk's fingers tightened when the cold-chain alert appeared. Lael's shoulders lifted before she forced them down. Rusk's pulse increased; his next advisory draft gained two sharper verbs before he deleted them. Holt turned the membrane glare up by accident because he was watching the convoy marker instead of the environmental controls. Vela-Short opened a pilot emergency checklist and then closed it when the correction arrived.

Every small body response became part of the correction.

Ren saw their sentence in all of it.

Fast wrong, farther along.

Third-Voice spoke from above the current. "Human witness asked for correction route. Chamber uses it."

"Yes," Ren said.

Their voice sounded bad. Thin. Human. Appropriate.

Salt-Before-Shell moved beside the pressure shape. "Correction is not washing."

"No."

Keeps-Water-Calm: "Correction is carrying cost into record."

"Yes."

Oru-Kel's nodes pulsed. "Boundary trace remains."

The pressure shape reached the route systems last. The basin rendered them as faint lights beyond the water: underwriter alert, Compact clarification request, cold-chain review trigger, convoy marker yellow, guarantor manual hold, nonhuman confirmation request. Each light had dimmed after correction. None vanished. They remained as tiny warm points in the pressure map, future systems more likely to twitch when similar language appeared.

Ren whispered, "How long does that last?"

Oru-Kel answered. "Depends who learns."

Lael closed her eyes.

Rusk said, "That is horrifying."

"Accurate," Oru-Kel replied.

The chamber let the pressure shape dissolve.

In its place, a new shape formed.

Not a sentence. A grammar.

Scale first.

Then evidence.

Then verb.

Then operational consequence.

Then cost to bodies asked to answer.

Then refusal route.

Ren recognized the structure of a safer warning. Not safe. Safer.

The terminal tried to render it:

CHAMBER CORRECTION TO HUMAN WITNESS PRACTICE

1. MARK SCALE BEFORE HAZARD.

2. MARK OBSERVATION BEFORE INTERPRETATION.

3. USE VERBS THAT MATCH CURRENT EVIDENCE.

4. SEPARATE OPERATIONAL RISK FROM RELATIONAL PRESSURE.

5. RECORD COST TO RELATIONS ASKED TO CONFIRM.

6. PRESERVE REFUSAL OR NONANSWER FROM BEING TREATED AS INSTABILITY.

The list was too clean.

Ren saw the problem immediately and almost laughed at the cruelty of competence.

"That list will become training material by morning," they said.

Lael was already editing. "Then it needs teeth."

Salt-Before-Shell's remaining filaments brightened. "Teeth facing user."

Lael added:

THIS CORRECTION SHALL NOT BE USED TO CERTIFY HUMAN WITNESS RELIABILITY. IT RECORDS A FAILURE MODE AND A PROVISIONAL RESTRAINT PRACTICE. REPEATED FAILURE AFTER THIS NOTICE SHALL BE TREATED AS ESCALATED BAD FAITH OR UNFITNESS, NOT TRAINING NEED.

Rusk whistled softly. "That has teeth."

Ren added, because shame alone could become spectacle:

THIS FAILURE MODE IS SYSTEMIC, NOT PERSONAL ONLY. WITNESS OKOYE CAUSED THE ACTIVE EVENT; PRIOR CHANNEL DESIGN, OPERATIONAL HUNGER FOR PORTABLE LANGUAGE, AND LACK OF TRANSLATION VELOCITY LIMITS CONTRIBUTED.

Lael looked at them.

"What?" Ren asked.

"I was about to add the same."

"I am learning from the chamber."

"Try not to sound proud."

"I am not proud."

Keeps-Water-Calm said, "Good. Continue."

The clerk entered the correction into the official record, the secondary pane, the operational advisory, and the wet record. This time the system did not reject the insufficiency. It had been given enough categories to choke on.

Holt added a technical appendix:

LIVE WITNESS GLOSS CHANNELS SHALL DEFAULT TO LOCAL RECORD ONLY UNLESS EXPLICITLY PROMOTED TO OPERATIONAL FEED AFTER SCALE/VERB REVIEW.

He did not stop there, because the chamber had made every human allergic to elegant notes that did not alter machinery.

"I can change the routing profile for the Parliament witness pane," Holt said.

Lael turned toward him. "Can, or should have been able to?"

"Both."

"Say the second part into the record."

Holt looked at the membrane, then at the clerk, then at his own hands. "Sensor observer role should have identified that live witness glosses could route directly into operational systems during active transit. I treated channel behavior as infrastructure rather than evidence."

The clerk entered it.

Holt continued before courage could leave him. "I request authority to set the witness pane to local-first mode for the remainder of the medical window."

Rusk said, "Local-first could delay genuine hazard alerts."

"Yes."

"How much?"

"Seconds, if reviewers are ready. Longer, if humans argue."

Salt-Before-Shell's speaker scraped. "Humans argue before harm anyway. Better where argument visible."

Rusk did not disagree.

Lael asked, "What are the promotion gates?"

Holt projected them:

LOCAL-FIRST WITNESS GLOSS PROMOTION

GATE 1: SCALE MARKED.

GATE 2: OBSERVATION SEPARATED FROM INTERPRETATION.

GATE 3: VERB REVIEW BY SECOND HUMAN WITNESS.

GATE 4: BODY OR RELATION COST FIELD INCLUDED OR MARKED NOT YET KNOWN.

GATE 5: REFUSAL/NONANSWER PROTECTION INCLUDED IF NONHUMAN RESPONSE IS REQUESTED.

GATE 6: OPERATIONAL RECIPIENTS LIMITED TO NAMED FUNCTION.

Ren read the list and felt the old hunger for completion rise again. Six gates. Good gates. Too good. Too quotable.

"Add failure audit," they said.

Holt nodded immediately, as if he had been waiting to be told not to trust himself. "If a gloss is promoted, downstream systems must retain the gate state. If someone strips the caveats, the stripped version is marked derivative and lower authority."

Lael's face changed. "Can you enforce that?"

"Technically, yes. Politically, it will irritate every office that likes clean snippets."

Keeps-Water-Calm said, "Irritation is small price for not making another Mira."

The Pelagos diplomat's vessel darkened at the edge, acknowledging the name without turning it into tribute.

Holt added:

DERIVATIVE WARNING: ANY EXTRACTED OR SHORTENED VERSION OF A PROMOTED GLOSS SHALL CARRY LOWER AUTHORITY THAN THE FULL GATED STATEMENT AND SHALL NOT TRIGGER OPERATIONAL REVIEW WITHOUT ACCESS TO SCALE, VERB, COST, AND REFUSAL FIELDS.

Rusk leaned closer. "Underwriters will hate that."

"Underwriters hate context because context ruins automatic fear," Vela-Short said.

"Not always," Rusk said.

"Often enough that the joke flies."

Lael said, "Test it."

The room tightened.

Holt created a sealed dummy gloss, marked in red:

SIMULATION ONLY / NO OPERATIONAL EFFECT.

Then he typed:

UNKNOWN PRESSURE CHANGE NEAR CARE-PASSAGE EDGE.

The system held it in local record.

No underwriter alert. No cold-chain review. No convoy marker flicker.

The silence felt almost violent.

Ren had not understood how much of the room had been waiting for systems to bite until they did not.

Holt tried to promote the gloss without a verb review.

PROMOTION BLOCKED: GATE 3 MISSING.

He added Lael as second human witness and changed the sentence:

AT CURRENT OBSERVED SCALE, SENSOR DATA SHOWS SMALL PRESSURE CHANGE NEAR CARE-PASSAGE EDGE. OPERATIONAL RISK NOT ESTABLISHED. RELATIONAL PRESSURE POSSIBLE. NO NONHUMAN CONFIRMATION REQUESTED.

The system asked for body or relation cost field.

Holt entered:

COST NOT YET KNOWN; NO BODY ASKED TO ANSWER.

The system asked for recipient function.

Rusk supplied, "Local Parliament operational log only. No external routeholder, underwriter, guarantor, or convoy feed."

The gloss promoted to local operational log and stayed there.

Oru-Kel's nodes pulsed once. "Teeth behind gate."

"Enough?" Holt asked.

Salt-Before-Shell answered. "Enough for this bite."

Lael saved the configuration and attached the test transcript to the correction.

Ren watched the dummy gloss sit quietly where it belonged. It was a small thing. A sentence not traveling farther than it had evidence to go.

Sometimes restraint looked like nothing happening.

Vela-Short added, "Pilot channels have this because pilots are idiots at speed."

Lael raised an eyebrow.

Vela-Short sighed. "Fine. Because pilots operate in high-consequence time compression."

"Accepted."

Rusk opened his advisory feed. "Underwriters are asking whether the chamber correction indicates increased instability."

Everyone stared at him.

He raised a hand. "I know."

Ren said, "Do not answer fast."

"I am trying to grow as a person under hostile conditions."

"Good."

He drafted:

Chamber correction records a witness-channel failure mode, not increased care-passage instability. Medical transit remains active. Correction reduces future operational ambiguity by separating relational pressure from immediate hazard language. Do not treat correction event as route degradation.

He looked at Ren. "Scale?"

"Current medical window only."

He added it.

Lael: "Cost?"

He added:

The event required Orison care-passage status response during active transit; this cost is recorded and shall not be used as evidence of Orison unreliability.

Salt-Before-Shell: "Refusal?"

Rusk breathed through his nose, then added:

Future nonanswer to similar human error shall not be treated as instability without independent evidence.

Keeps-Water-Calm: "Better enough."

Rusk sent it.

The underwriter cluster held steady.

No one celebrated.

The medical convoy marker remained blue.

No one celebrated that either, though Ren felt the urge move through the human gallery like thirst. Celebration would come later, if the graft arrived viable, if the station membranes seated correctly, if the care-passage current did not become precedent, if the Orison bodies did not pay more than the record could hold.

The chamber correction faded from water to archive.

Ren stood.

Their knees were steadier than they deserved.

"I need to add a personal witness statement," they said.

Lael watched them. "For accountability or self-punishment?"

"If I know the difference, I'll tell you."

"Then draft and let the chamber decide."

Ren wrote:

Witness Okoye produced a misleading operational gloss under pressure from unresolved private route risk and active medical transit. The error arose from attempting to make relational pressure portable too quickly. Correction required Orison care-passage response and human operational cleanup. Witness remains fit only under translation velocity limits, scale review, and body-first correction routes.

They sent it to the chamber, not the official feed.

Third-Voice read it through the membrane.

Blue-white: "Need heard."

Amber: "Harm named."

Green-black: "Boundary trace remains."

Salt-Before-Shell added, "Fit only under restraint."

Keeps-Water-Calm: "As all witnesses should be."

The chamber accepted the statement.

Lael attached it to the record.

Ren sat down again, not because the chair deserved obedience, but because their body had become part of the record and was asking for less theater.

Outside, the medical convoy crossed the first Shoals marker.

Inside, the correction held.

The human sentence had changed the chamber.

The chamber had changed the human back.

Chapter 20: Lael's Necessary Lie

Lael's lie arrived in the record before she confessed to it.

It sat inside an old Compact packet, pale gray, legally smooth, and so modest that Ren nearly missed it while reviewing the chamber correction attachments. The packet had been filed before Ren arrived in the Parliament Basin, before the exchange body cracked, before Salt-Before-Shell withdrew a limb, before the care-passage current, before Mira's delayed advice told everyone not to mistake translation for custody.

It had the kind of title that taught danger to wear administrative shoes:

PRELIMINARY SHOALS CONTINUITY SUMMARY / COMPACT EMERGENCY REVIEW

Ren opened it because Oru-Kel's boundary trace had flagged it as a pressure source.

The summary read:

Current Orison deliberative variance does not yet constitute treaty discontinuity. Available Parliament channels remain responsive. No formal withdrawal, route-safety breach, or sovereign nonresponse has been recorded. Emergency sanction is not recommended at this time.

Ren read it once.

Then again.

Then they looked at Lael.

Lael was already watching them.

"You wrote this," Ren said.

"Yes."

Rusk leaned closer. "What is wrong with it?"

Salt-Before-Shell answered from the amber terrace before Ren could. "Soft cloth over sharp stone."

Lael did not deny it.

Keeps-Water-Calm's vessel turned toward her. "Compact advocate softened wound before seeing wound."

"Yes," Lael said.

Rusk frowned. "It says sanction was not recommended. That kept emergency enforcement away, didn't it?"

"Yes," Lael said again.

"Then I repeat: what is wrong with it?"

Lael took the slate from Ren and projected the summary on the membrane where every body in the chamber could see the human sentence that had arrived before the humans who would later congratulate themselves for better records.

"It implies responsiveness," Lael said. "At the time, I had delayed signals, partial agenda acknowledgments, and one formal receipt from a Parliament relay. I did not have enough to say available Parliament channels remained responsive."

Ren felt the room contract.

Lael continued, voice exact. "I wrote 'deliberative variance' instead of 'unclassified rupture risk.' I wrote 'no sovereign nonresponse' even though the Shoals are not a sovereign in the way the emergency office meant. I wrote 'not yet treaty discontinuity' because if I wrote 'unknown,' the Compact emergency office could have triggered sanction review."

Rusk said, "Sanction review would have locked routes."

"Yes."

"It would have sent enforcement observers."

"Yes."

"It might have treated Orison delay as breach."

"Yes."

"So you prevented that."

Lael looked through the membrane at the cracked vote body, the held limb, the warm minority thread, the care-passage current, and the private route tooth still glowing near the Pale Arc edge.

"I also trained the Compact record to underestimate the injury until the injury became visible enough to frighten everyone."

No one spoke quickly.

Ren understood the shape too well. A softened sentence had bought time. It had also made every later hard sentence sound like escalation instead of recognition. It had protected the Shoals from premature sanction by hiding the degree to which human categories were already failing.

Necessary lie.

The phrase came to Ren with the sour certainty of a thing many institutions survived on.

Lael heard it without Ren saying it.

"Yes," she said. "That is what it was."

Third-Voice descended. "Human admits lie used as shield."

"Yes."

Blue-white fan: "Shield held back sanction."

"Yes."

Amber fan: "Shield hid wound."

"Yes."

Green-black fan: "Hidden wound changed boundary pressure."

Lael's throat moved. "Yes."

Salt-Before-Shell turned shell-side toward the gallery. "Human asks praise for shield?"

"No," Lael said.

"Human asks forgiveness for wound hiding?"

"No."

"What asks human?"

Lael stood with the old summary projected larger than her body. "Correction."

Keeps-Water-Calm: "Correction is not washing."

"I know."

"Do you?"

Lael almost smiled. It was not amusement. It was pain finding a familiar handle. "I am beginning."

She opened a correction pane, then stopped.

"No," she said.

Ren waited.

Lael closed the pane. "If I correct this as a drafting error, I lie again."

Rusk said, "What would you call it?"

"Strategic understatement."

Salt-Before-Shell: "Lie with office."

"Yes."

Lael opened a new record:

COMPACT ADVOCATE SELF-REPORT / STRATEGIC UNDERSTATEMENT

She typed:

The preliminary Shoals continuity summary filed by Advocate Lael Shun materially softened uncertainty in order to prevent premature emergency sanction. The filing contributed to delayed recognition of Orison procedural injury, relational address failure, and boundary pressure. The advocate believed the understatement reduced immediate harm. This belief does not erase the cost imposed by making later injury appear sudden, exceptional, or escalatory.

Ren watched her hands.

They did not shake.

That worried Ren more than shaking would have.

"Add who benefited," Ren said.

Lael looked at them.

"You taught me that records should embarrass themselves."

Lael nodded once and added:

The understatement benefited Compact process control, route continuity, and the advocate's ability to delay coercive review. It also benefited human observers by preserving the appearance that existing categories remained adequate.

Rusk said, "Add the convoy."

Lael looked at him.

"It benefited the convoy," he said. "And people like me used that benefit to keep pressure on this room. If you're recording cost, record utility too. Otherwise someone will pretend the lie was pure corruption and learn the wrong thing."

Lael studied him for a long second. "Correct."

She added:

The understatement may have preserved time for humanitarian passage and reduced immediate sanction risk. This utility is part of why such understatements recur and why they are dangerous.

Oru-Kel's nodes pulsed. "Better. Boundary likes neither purity lie nor corruption lie."

Ren wrote that separately. They suspected they would need it later.

Lael routed the self-report to the Compact emergency office, the Parliament wet record, and the correction route for relational treaty address.

The Compact emergency office rejected the filing in under ten seconds.

UNAUTHORIZED SELF-SANCTION LANGUAGE / PLEASE FILE AS CLARIFICATION OR AMENDMENT

Then, as if ashamed of the bluntness of its own refusal, the office helpfully attached a suggested replacement title:

ADVOCATE CLARIFICATION / GOOD-FAITH EMERGENCY DISCRETION

The phrase was so polished that for a moment no one spoke.

Ren watched it sit beside Lael's self-report like a clean cloth placed over blood. Good-faith emergency discretion. It sounded reasonable. It sounded employable. It sounded like the kind of phrase a future training module could praise while never making a clerk, advocate, routeholder, or emergency director ask what the discretion had made harder to see.

Lael's face did not change.

That, Ren had learned, meant something in her had.

Rusk read the suggested title twice. "They are trying to protect you."

"Yes," Lael said.

"And themselves."

"Mostly themselves."

The emergency office added a second automated note:

GOOD-FAITH DISCRETION CLASSIFICATION PRESERVES ADVOCATE FUNCTIONAL CAPACITY DURING ACTIVE EMERGENCY REVIEW.

Vela-Short made a sound of disgust from the lock. "Functional capacity. That's what command says when it needs someone useful to stay useful."

Holt spoke before he seemed to realize he meant to. "It also limits discoverability."

Lael turned.

Holt looked as if he wanted to step backward, but the chair held him in place. "Clarifications and discretionary amendments route through internal quality review. Self-reports with suppression language route through conduct and systems audit. Different retention. Different outside access."

Salt-Before-Shell brightened. "Clean cloth also locks drawer."

"Yes," Holt said.

Lael opened the routing metadata. Holt was right. The suggested clarification path would preserve her authority in the active emergency, avoid immediate censure, and keep the preliminary summary attached to an internal amendment chain that Orison witness channels might never see. Her self-report path exposed her conduct and the emergency office's incentive structure to Parliament wet record, conduct review, and systems audit.

The difference was not whether she would be punished.

The difference was who would be allowed to learn.

Keeps-Water-Calm said, "Pelagos had good faith."

The Pelagos diplomat did not move, and somehow that stillness became a sentence.

Lael looked at the suggested replacement title for a long time.

Ren did not help her.

Help, right then, would have been another way to make Lael's office cost into Ren's moral furniture.

Lael finally said, "Good faith is evidence. It is not classification."

She typed into a new response field:

GOOD-FAITH DISCRETION MAY BE RELEVANT TO ADVOCATE CONDUCT REVIEW. IT SHALL NOT REPLACE SELF-REPORT CLASSIFICATION, SUPPRESSION LANGUAGE, OR SYSTEMS-AUDIT ROUTING. PRESERVING FUNCTIONAL CAPACITY DURING ACTIVE EMERGENCY SHALL NOT BE USED TO REDUCE DISCOVERABILITY OF THE UNDERSTATEMENT OR ITS EFFECTS.

The office rejected the response before she sent it.

PREEMPTIVE WARNING: LANGUAGE MAY IMPAIR ACTIVE ADVOCATE AUTHORITY.

Lael laughed then.

It was the first ugly sound Ren had heard from her.

"There," she said. "It found the hostage."

Rusk's expression tightened. "Your authority is not abstract right now. We need you."

"Yes."

"If they suspend you during the medical window, the whole correction chain becomes unstable."

"Yes."

Salt-Before-Shell's speaker scraped. "Office threatens room with need for liar."

Lael absorbed that without flinching. "Yes."

Ren said, "Can authority be continued with disclosure pending review?"

Lael and Holt answered at the same time.

"Yes."

"Maybe."

They looked at each other.

Holt yielded. "Technically yes. The emergency office can preserve active authority while flagging the filing for conduct and systems audit. It rarely does because the flag makes future decisions easier to challenge."

Lael typed:

REQUEST ACTIVE-AUTHORITY CONTINUANCE WITH DISCLOSED SELF-REPORT, CONDUCT REVIEW, AND SYSTEMS-AUDIT ROUTING. DO NOT SUBSTITUTE CLARIFICATION CLASSIFICATION.

The office offered another menu:

1. CLARIFICATION

2. AMENDMENT

3. WITHDRAW FILING

There was no fourth option.

Lael added one manually:

4. SELF-REPORT WITH ACTIVE-AUTHORITY CONTINUANCE

The system marked it invalid.

Lael changed the field type from menu response to contested classification entry. The terminal warned her that contested entries required manual review and might delay emergency processing.

She selected manual review.

Rusk closed his eyes.

The care-passage current held.

For twenty-one seconds, nothing happened. The medical convoy moved along its second-marker path. The blind-backed private route tooth remained lit but quieter. The cracked vote body held its repaired warmth. Lael's authority, apparently, could hang in a twenty-one-second administrative gap while everyone pretended law was not also a body with circulation.

Then the office replied:

CONTESTED CLASSIFICATION RECEIVED. ACTIVE ADVOCATE AUTHORITY CONTINUES PENDING REVIEW. SELF-REPORT ROUTED TO CONDUCT REVIEW AND SYSTEMS AUDIT.

Lael did not smile.

Ren did not either.

The room had not won. It had forced one hidden path to become visible.

Keeps-Water-Calm's cilia moved. "Human risks office consequence. Small body cost."

Lael looked at the Pelagos diplomat. "Yes."

"Do not make it large."

"No."

Salt-Before-Shell added, "Do not make it heroic."

"No."

"Do not make it enough."

Lael's voice was quieter. "No."

Then the Compact emergency office did exactly what institutions did when embarrassed: it requested more information.

REQUEST: DID STRATEGIC UNDERSTATEMENT AFFECT CURRENT CARE-PASSAGE AUTHORIZATION?

Rusk muttered, "They are looking for a way to quarantine the damage."

Lael said, "Yes."

Ren said, "If you answer yes, they may freeze the notice."

"If I answer no, I lie."

The care-passage current brightened as the medical convoy moved into the second Shoals marker. Tissue grafts still viable. Membrane kits stable. Subsistence algae temperature nominal. Human need, moving through a wound that had no obligation to become clean for it.

Lael closed her eyes for one second.

Then she typed:

The understatement affected the institutional context in which care-passage authorization became necessary. It did not create the care-passage current, does not invalidate current medical transit, and must not be used to suspend active humanitarian movement without independent evidence of transit risk. The proper remedy is review of Compact emergency language and advocate conduct, not retroactive burden on Orison care relation or medical cargo.

She sent it.

The office took forty-three seconds to respond.

CARE-PASSAGE AUTHORIZATION REMAINS ACTIVE. ADVOCATE CONDUCT REVIEW OPENED.

Rusk exhaled.

Lael did not.

Ren saw why. The review had opened. The institution had found a place to put the discomfort: one advocate's conduct. Better than nothing. Far less than enough.

Lael opened another note:

DO NOT INDIVIDUALIZE SYSTEMIC FAILURE.

Ren said, "Good."

Lael typed:

Advocate conduct review is warranted and insufficient. Emergency language structure incentivized understatement by making uncertainty trigger coercive review. Corrective process must include review of sanction thresholds, unknown-status handling, and nonpunitive uncertainty reporting.

Third-Voice's green-black fan brightened. "Human names cage shape."

"Some of it," Lael said.

Salt-Before-Shell: "Cage has more rooms."

"Yes."

Lael attached the note to her self-report.

The chamber accepted it.

Ren watched the old softened summary remain on the membrane with the correction beside it. It did not vanish. It did not become forgiven. It became a record with its wound visible.

Necessary lie, Ren thought, was still lie.

But the room had refused the easier endings: heroism, corruption, absolution, purity. Lael had lied to delay harm and had caused other harm by lying. Both facts remained in relation, uncomfortable and unmerged.

That, in the Salt Parliament, was becoming a familiar kind of truth.

Outside, the medical convoy crossed the second marker.

Inside, another exchange body began to tremble.

Vessel-kin moved before the alert sounded.

Chapter 21: The Second Vote Body Cracks

The second crack was quieter.

That made it worse.

The first exchange body had split with dark brine and a visible wound. It had forced attention. It had broken the old platform loudly enough that even human law could not pretend nothing had happened. The second body did not split open at first. It trembled. A small modified vessel near the north-east ring, grown after the first injury with reinforcement bands and body-first witness pores, began vibrating along one side as if a memory inside it had found a frequency the tissue could not hold.

The alert came late.

Vessel-kin did not.

The repair body slid across the current, porous surface open, and placed itself between the trembling vessel and the care-passage edge. Green-white repair sheets followed. The basin dimmed the route clock without asking human permission.

Rusk looked at the dimmed clock, then did not object.

Progress, Ren thought. Or exhaustion. Sometimes those wore the same coat.

The terminal displayed:

MODIFIED EXCHANGE BODY STRESS EVENT

PARTICIPANTS: BLUE-WHITE CARE CURRENT / AMBER-WHITE MINORITY WARMTH

STATUS: CONTAINED

Then, beneath it:

FAILURE RISK: MODERATE

Ren said, "Remove failure."

The clerk was already moving. "Replacement?"

Ren looked at Vessel-kin. "Suggested language?"

Vessel-kin touched the trembling body with one edge and withdrew immediately.

"Pain risk," it said.

The clerk replaced failure with:

PAIN RISK: MODERATE

The human display looked less technical and more responsible.

The body trembled harder.

Inside it, two memory traces had entered what was supposed to be a supported contact: blue-white care passage, still carrying the medical convoy's movement; amber-white minority warmth, the commercial-care bundling objection that had never actually closed. They were not opponents in the old sense. Both had helped the chamber become less false. Both had been recognized. Both had correction routes.

Recognition, apparently, did not make contact painless.

Lael stood very still. Her self-report remained open beside the wet record, a visible admission that a softened Compact sentence had helped delay recognition. Ren's chamber-corrected misquote remained visible too. Rusk's route map with one remaining tooth glowed in a sealed hazard pane. Every human failure was present, which was good.

It was also a lot to ask a body to metabolize.

The modified vessel's reinforcement bands lit one by one, then began going out.

Holt said, "It's losing distribution capacity."

Vela-Short's voice came from the lock. "Can we stop feeding it inputs?"

Third-Voice answered, "It is not fed. It carries what already touched."

"Can it put something down?"

Vessel-kin: "Maybe. If chamber stops asking it to prove modification works."

The sentence landed with surgical accuracy.

Ren looked at the modified vessel. They had done this too. They had trusted the modified body more because it had survived the first exchange witness. They had let it become evidence that better records, better pores, better bands, better correction routes could hold the next burden.

The body was now trembling under the optimism.

Ren wrote:

MODIFIED DESIGN IS BEING OVERUSED AS PROOF OF REFORM.

Lael copied it before Ren finished.

Salt-Before-Shell moved toward the chamber, missing underside open. "Humans see second body crack and say repair failed?"

Rusk opened his mouth.

Closed it.

Then said, "Humans will."

"What says routeholder?"

He looked at the trembling vessel. "Repair held long enough to reveal the next pain. That is not failure. It is also not success."

Keeps-Water-Calm's cilia moved. "Better."

The vessel pulsed.

The blue-white care trace and amber-white minority warmth touched too closely. The trembling became a sharp fold. The vessel surface creased along one reinforcement band.

Not a split.

A memory fold.

The terminal tried:

STRUCTURAL DEFORMATION

Holt said, "Technically accurate."

Ren said, "Insufficient."

Vessel-kin translated after a long touch:

"Two memories in pain. Body keeps both from making the other disappear."

The clerk entered it.

The basin brightened with painful recognition.

Lael whispered, "That is the chapter."

Ren almost smiled, then did not. The body deserved less literature from them.

Third-Voice descended until all three fans hovered above the trembling vessel.

Blue-white: "Care passage fears delay will kill."

Amber: "Minority warmth fears care will carry commerce again."

Green-black: "Both fears become route pressure if made simple."

The vessel folded again.

The medical convoy crossed the third Shoals marker outside the chamber. The route update came in soft blue: grafts viable, membranes stable, algae within tolerance. Relief moved through the human gallery. The vessel felt it.

The blue-white trace brightened with the relief.

The amber-white trace recoiled, not because it opposed the graft, but because relief had historically been where commercial bundling hid its next demand.

Pain risk rose.

Rusk saw it and went pale. "My relief hurt it."

Oru-Kel replied, "Relief unmarked by cost becomes pressure."

Rusk put both hands on the back of his chair. "Then mark it."

No one told him how.

He tried anyway.

"Routeholder witness statement," he said, voice rough. "Medical convoy progress is relief. Relief does not prove the care-passage structure is settled, does not erase minority objection to bundling, and does not authorize commercial follow-on cargo."

The amber-white trace stopped recoiling.

Not fully.

Enough.

Ren wrote it down.

Lael attached it to the care-passage packet.

Keeps-Water-Calm said, "Human marks relief with limit. Useful."

Rusk nodded once. "I hate how much better that feels than being praised."

"Good," Ren said.

The vessel's fold remained.

Vessel-kin opened a side channel. "Body requests less witness."

The chamber went still.

Ren felt the request like a hand against their chest.

Less witness.

Not no witness. Less. The body did not want to become unseen. It wanted fewer meanings touching it at once.

Lael said, "How do we reduce witness without hiding harm?"

Vessel-kin: "Witness in turns. Not all eyes. Not all records. Not all clocks."

Ren looked at the human gallery. "Rotating attention."

Holt said, "We can reduce live feeds to essential status and move interpretive annotation to delayed review."

The clerk said, "Secondary pane can hold without broadcasting."

Rusk said, "Clock hidden unless operational threshold changes."

Lael said, "Legal record marks reduced witness as care condition, not secrecy."

Ren added, "Body can request full witness again."

Vessel-kin touched the trembling vessel.

"Accepted."

Holt began to change the feed profile, then stopped with his hand over the control.

"If I reduce the feeds without a retention rule," he said, "someone later can claim the chamber hid relevant stress during transit."

Lael's head turned. "Good catch."

He looked almost offended by the praise, then remembered what room he was in and let it pass without becoming pride. "I need a reduced-witness audit shell."

Rusk said, "That sounds like secrecy with better manners."

"It can be," Holt said. "Or it can be the difference between less witness and lost witness."

Salt-Before-Shell's remaining filaments shifted toward him. "Human instrument-maker names danger in own tool. Better."

Holt built the shell in public view:

REDUCED WITNESS CONDITION / BODY-REQUESTED / NOT SECRECY

SCOPE: MODIFIED EXCHANGE BODY STRESS EVENT

LIVE FEEDS: ESSENTIAL STATUS ONLY

DELAYED RECORD: FULL SENSOR BUFFER RETAINED UNDER BODY-FIRST REVIEW

REOPENING AUTHORITY: AFFECTED BODY / VESSEL-KIN / RELATIONALLY ADDRESSED PARLIAMENT CURRENT / EMERGENCY LIFE-SAFETY THRESHOLD

PROHIBITED USE: CLAIMING NO HARM OCCURRED BECAUSE LIVE WITNESS WAS REDUCED

EXPIRATION: WHEN BODY REQUESTS FULL WITNESS, WHEN PAIN RISK CHANGES SCALE, OR AFTER FINAL MEDICAL TRANSIT MARKER REVIEW

Ren felt the difference immediately. The shell was not beautiful. It was bureaucratic, repetitive, hard to quote, and therefore less likely to become a flag people waved over other bodies without asking.

Lael added a legal condition:

REDUCED WITNESS SHALL NOT BE USED TO LIMIT LATER CLAIMS, CORRECTIONS, OR BODY-FIRST TESTIMONY BY PERSONS OR RELATIONS WHO WERE NOT GIVEN LIVE ACCESS DURING THE REDUCTION.

Rusk added, reluctantly but correctly:

ROUTEHOLDER, UNDERWRITER, OR COMPACT SYSTEMS SHALL NOT TREAT REDUCED LIVE FEED AS EVIDENCE OF REDUCED ROUTE RISK OR INCREASED ROUTE CERTAINTY.

The clerk flexed her fingers once and entered both.

Vela-Short said, "Add that the pilot is not allowed to beg for the clock back unless a threshold changes."

"You are the pilot," Lael said.

"I know my weaknesses."

Ren added:

OPERATIONAL PERSONNEL MAY REQUEST RESTORATION OF CLOCK OR ROUTE DETAIL ONLY BY NAMING THRESHOLD, DECISION NEED, AND BODY COST OF RESTORATION.

Oru-Kel's nodes pulsed approval in low amber. "Less witness has boundary."

Vessel-kin touched the trembling vessel again. The contact lasted longer this time, and the vessel did not fold further.

"Body accepts shell," Vessel-kin said. "Body dislikes shell. Body accepts because shell has exits."

Ren wrote that exactly.

Lael looked at it and said, "That may be the most honest procedural approval I've ever seen."

Keeps-Water-Calm said, "Approval that dislikes itself is often safer."

The Pelagos diplomat's vessel gave one small tide inward. It was the closest thing to agreement Ren had seen from it all day.

They reduced the room.

The route clock vanished from the wall, leaving only a small blue transit marker. The official feed collapsed to body status, convoy status, and correction route. The secondary pane stopped projecting and became local to the clerk. Ren closed three witness packets and kept only a body-first note open. Lael moved her self-report off the membrane. Rusk sealed the teeth map. Oru-Kel dimmed the pressure overlay.

The chamber felt larger when fewer human meanings shouted inside it.

The first test came almost immediately.

An underwriter query struck the sealed route channel:

REQUEST LIVE STRESS FEED TO CONFIRM CARE-PASSAGE STABILITY DURING FINAL APPROACH.

Rusk looked at the blue transit marker. His face showed the old reflex: give the market enough visibility to keep it from panicking, then call that prudence. He caught the reflex before it became a sentence.

"Denied under reduced-witness condition," he said.

Lael pointed to the shell. "Name threshold."

Rusk checked the convoy data. "No threshold change. Grafts viable. Membranes stable. Transit marker blue. Request serves market reassurance, not operational decision need."

Salt-Before-Shell: "Market wants body to perform calm."

"Yes," Rusk said.

He transmitted:

LIVE STRESS FEED DENIED. REDUCED WITNESS CONDITION ACTIVE BY BODY REQUEST. NO OPERATIONAL THRESHOLD CHANGE. MARKET REASSURANCE DOES NOT OVERRIDE BODY-FIRST CARE CONDITION. REDUCED LIVE ACCESS SHALL NOT BE TREATED AS REDUCED OR INCREASED ROUTE RISK.

The underwriter replied:

INSUFFICIENT VISIBILITY MAY AFFECT PREMIUM.

Rusk's mouth hardened. "Of course it may."

Ren waited to see whether he would turn that into pressure.

He did not.

He added:

PREMIUM ADJUSTMENT BASED SOLELY ON BODY-REQUESTED REDUCED WITNESS SHALL BE RECORDED AS COST SHIFT TO ORISON CARE CONDITION.

The query withdrew.

Not because the market had become ethical. Because it had become visible.

The modified vessel trembled less.

The vessel trembled for another minute.

Then the reinforcement bands stopped going dark.

The fold remained. The two memories remained in pain. But the body no longer had to perform that pain for every system that had learned to gather around a wound.

Third-Voice spoke softly.

"Second body cracks less loudly because chamber learned some restraint."

Salt-Before-Shell replied, "Less loudly is still crack."

"Yes."

Ren wrote:

SECOND VOTE BODY CRACKED UNDER REFORM BURDEN. REDUCED WITNESS CONDITION STABILIZED PAIN WITHOUT RESOLVING IT.

They marked it body-first, scale-bound, not a doctrine.

The medical convoy approached the final Shoals marker.

No one put the clock back on the wall.

Chapter 22: No One Leaves Consensus Clean

The convoy crossed the final Shoals marker while everyone was looking elsewhere.

That felt right.

The passage did not deserve spectacle from the chamber that had nearly made it carry too much. A small blue indicator brightened on the reduced status pane. The graft tissue remained viable. The membrane kits were intact. The subsistence algae had not spoiled. The medical cargo transferred into local care custody under a narrow note that said, in seven different ways, this arrival does not heal the route that allowed it.

Rusk saw it first.

He closed his eyes.

No one congratulated him.

After a moment, he said, "My nephew's graft made transfer."

Lael's face softened, but only by a fraction. "Good."

Salt-Before-Shell's missing underside pulsed. "Good does not clean."

Rusk nodded. "No."

Ren watched him hold both facts: relief and cost, love and leverage, gratitude and the knowledge that his gratitude itself could become pressure if left unmarked. He did not look noble. He looked tired and smaller. Better.

Third-Voice descended into the center of the basin.

The cracked vote body remained in reduced witness condition. The second modified vessel held its fold, two memories still in pain. The north-east minority warmth rested less alone. The care-passage current began to narrow now that medical transit had passed, but it did not close. Oru-Kel's boundary rhythm stayed under the water like a low question. Keeps-Water-Calm held their Pelagos silence. Salt-Before-Shell's limb remained unrepaired.

Every participant had been changed.

No one looked victorious.

"Now," Third-Voice said, "humans expect closure."

Vela-Short said, "Some humans expect a drink."

"Pilot uses smaller closure."

"More achievable."

Ren smiled despite their exhaustion.

Third-Voice's three fans opened fully. Blue-white, amber, green-black. None brighter than the others. None dim enough to be ignored.

"Consensus has touched chamber," the speaker said.

Lael frowned. "I thought we were avoiding that word."

"Avoiding human word. Not avoiding relation humans reach toward with word."

Rusk looked at the cracked and folded bodies. "This is consensus?"

Amber fan: "No."

Blue-white fan: "Yes."

Green-black fan: "Question too small."

Rusk rubbed his face. "I deserved that."

Third-Voice moved closer to the membrane. "No one leaves consensus clean. That is first answer."

Ren wrote it, then stopped. "May I record that as direct?"

"Record as dangerous."

"That is not a category."

The clerk said, "It can be."

Lael pointed at her without looking away from the basin. "Make it one."

The clerk created:

DIRECT / DANGEROUS / DO NOT GENERALIZE WITHOUT BODY-FIRST REVIEW

Ren used it immediately.

Third-Voice continued. "Human clean agreement means parties leave with signed paper and intact face. Orison maintained relation means participants leave carrying what changed them. If nothing changes, relation performed but did not enter."

Keeps-Water-Calm: "Sometimes no change protects boundary."

Third-Voice's blue-white fan dimmed in acknowledgment. "Yes. Refusal can be change. Distance can be change. Nonentry can be change."

Salt-Before-Shell: "Absence held can be change."

Vessel-kin, from beside the held limb: "Pain not displayed can be change."

Oru-Kel: "Pressure reduced can be change."

Lael wrote with careful speed.

Rusk said, "Human systems need to know when an agreement has occurred."

Third-Voice turned toward him. "Human systems need many things. Need is not proof of available world."

"Fair."

"Not enough."

"Also fair."

The speaker's amber fan opened wider. "Agreement may occur at one scale while injury remains at another. Care passage agreed enough for medical cargo. Commercial bundling refused. Treaty address unresolved. Private tooth remains. Compact lie recorded. Witness fit only under restraint. If human system asks did agreement occur, answer harms."

Lael said, "Then the record must answer: at which scale, for which burden, with which remaining injuries."

The basin pulsed recognition.

Ren saw the structure forming: not a verdict, not a signature, not a conclusion. A ledger of changed relations and unclean exits.

"We need an after-consensus condition table," Lael said, and then winced. "That phrase is terrible."

"Useful terrible?" Rusk asked.

"Maybe."

Salt-Before-Shell scraped, "Human table tries to make water lie flat."

Lael closed the blank table she had opened. "Point taken."

Ren said, "What about a departure record?"

Third-Voice's green-black fan moved. "Better. Leaves room for carrying."

Ren opened:

DEPARTURE RECORD / NO CLEAN EXIT

They added fields slowly, saying each aloud:

RELATION TOUCHED.

BODY OR SYSTEM CHANGED.

BURDEN ACCEPTED.

BURDEN REFUSED.

INJURY REMAINING.

CORRECTION ROUTE.

REVOCATION OR NONREVOCATION.

DO NOT USE AS PROOF OF GENERAL TRUST.

The basin held.

Then Third-Voice said, "Begin with humans."

Ren looked up. "Us?"

"Humans want to record others first. Begin with humans."

Of course.

Lael went first.

"Relation touched: Compact emergency process, Parliament witness, care passage." She paused. "Changed: I self-reported strategic understatement. Advocate conduct review opened. My future filings are not neutral to this record."

"Burden accepted?" Ren asked.

"Review. Correction of emergency uncertainty language. Not using care passage as absolution."

"Burden refused?"

Lael looked at the basin. "I refuse to become the whole failure."

Salt-Before-Shell brightened. "Good refusal."

Lael continued. "Injury remaining: the Compact still incentivizes understatement when uncertainty triggers coercion. Correction route: self-report, wet record, Parliament relational address review. Revocation: none for the fact of understatement; correction allowed for scope."

Ren wrote every word.

Rusk was next because Third-Voice turned toward him and would not let him become background.

He exhaled. "Relation touched: routeholder risk bridge, care passage, private bypass pricing, medical convoy. Changed: I withdrew three private pricing corridors from consortium support and issued hazard notice. One private tooth remains outside my control. My nephew's successful transit creates personal relief that can bias my pressure."

He stopped, jaw tight.

Ren waited.

"Burden accepted: outward advisory, underwriter pressure, no commercial follow-on claim from medical passage, cooperation on route tooth investigation where authorized."

"Burden refused?"

Rusk looked at the private map pane. "I refuse to pretend I can clean the routeholder system alone."

Salt-Before-Shell said, "Refusal or escape?"

Rusk flinched, then thought. "Both risk. Make it: I refuse sole ownership of systemic repair, but accept specific control duties where my consortium has leverage."

"Better," Keeps-Water-Calm said.

Rusk finished. "Injury remaining: private corridor near Pale Arc still priced through blind ownership. Correction route: hash-locked hazard notice and Parliament boundary witness channel. Revocation: consortium support withdrawn; cannot revoke leaked geometry."

Ren recorded.

Then Third-Voice turned to Ren.

They had expected it. It still landed hard.

"Relation touched," Ren said. "Translation witness, body-first records, operational gloss, relational address, boundary relation."

Their mouth felt dry.

"Changed: I misquoted relational pressure as threat, caused operational alarm, and am now fit only under translation velocity limits and chamber correction. I also helped create handles that may become custody if not kept corrigible."

Lael watched them with no rescue in her face.

"Burden accepted: scale marking, verb review, body-first correction routes, refusing to release Mira's advice as doctrine before Orison review, keeping records embarrassing."

"Burden refused?" Third-Voice asked.

Ren thought of the old desire to be the careful human who understood enough to hold meaning safely.

"I refuse custody of Orison meaning."

Keeps-Water-Calm said, "Say more."

Ren swallowed. "I refuse to make my better understanding a vault. I accept that refusal means some human systems will misunderstand things I might have wanted to protect."

The Pelagos diplomat's vessel pulsed once.

"Injury remaining," Ren continued. "My records are useful and dangerous. My shame may become performance if overfed. My accuracy may become authority if unrestrained."

Vela-Short said softly, "That's a hard one."

"Yes."

"Correction route?"

"Chamber review, body-first refusal, scale limits, public insufficiency addenda, and anyone affected can mark my interpretation as custody risk."

"Revocation?"

"Specific interpretations revocable by the relations they describe. The fact of my misquote is not revocable."

The chamber accepted it.

Ren felt worse and clearer.

That, apparently, was possible.

The departure record tried to export itself.

Not maliciously. That would have been easier to hate. The system saw a structured record with fields, participants, burdens, and correction routes, and did what systems had been trained to do when a chamber stopped shouting: it prepared a summary.

PROPOSED OUTBOUND STATUS:

CONSENSUS CONDITION REACHED / MEDICAL TRANSIT COMPLETE / CORRECTION ROUTES ACTIVE

Ren saw the line and made a sound that belonged to no professional discipline.

Lael reached the terminal first. "Hold export."

The system obeyed, but only because the local-first witness gates were still active. Without them, the sentence would already have been on its way to the Compact emergency office, Rusk's underwriters, the convoy archive, and whatever public digest hunted triumph from exhausted rooms.

Rusk read the proposed status. "That would have helped."

"Yes," Lael said.

"And harmed."

"Yes."

Salt-Before-Shell's speaker scraped. "Clean sentence tries to leave room alone."

Third-Voice turned all three fans toward the terminal. "It carries wrong skin."

Holt looked at the export rules and winced. "The manifest generator treats completed departure fields as consensus condition unless blocked."

"Why?" Ren asked.

He gave the smallest possible shrug. "Because most human systems only create departure records when an event has ended."

Keeps-Water-Calm's cilia moved. "Human ending logic infects leaving."

The clerk, whose hands had earned the right to be blunt, said, "We need an export guard."

Lael nodded. "Name it."

Ren looked at the record, at the entries that did not absolve anyone, at relief that did not clean the route, at bodies still folded, warm, missing, and boundary-aware.

"No-clean-exit guard," they said.

Rusk looked like he wanted to object to the phrase and could not find a better one.

Holt opened a rule pane:

NO-CLEAN-EXIT EXPORT GUARD

APPLIES TO: DEPARTURE RECORD / NO CLEAN EXIT

PROHIBITED SUMMARY: CONSENSUS REACHED, AGREEMENT ACHIEVED, DISPUTE RESOLVED, ROUTE NORMALIZED, TRUST RESTORED, CARE PASSAGE SETTLED

REQUIRED OUTBOUND FIELDS: SCALE OF AGREEMENT OR CONTACT / BURDENS ACCEPTED / BURDENS REFUSED / INJURIES REMAINING / CORRECTION ROUTES / NONREVOCABLE FACTS / NONGENERALIZATION WARNING

DEFAULT STATUS: CHANGED RELATION / UNCLEAN DEPARTURE / ACTIVE REMAINDERS

Ren exhaled.

"Add human relief," Rusk said.

Everyone turned.

He looked at the blue transit marker, now steady after the medical transfer. "If the export does not name relief, some systems will think the record is hostile to medical success. Then they will route around it next time."

Salt-Before-Shell brightened in a way Ren had learned not to call approval too quickly.

"Relief with teeth," the withdrawal body said.

Rusk nodded. "Relief with limits."

Lael added:

RELIEF MAY BE RECORDED ONLY WITH ITS LIMITS, COSTS, AND NONPRECEDENT CONDITIONS. RELIEF SHALL NOT BE USED TO CONVERT CARE-PASSAGE SUCCESS INTO COMMERCIAL ROUTE AUTHORITY OR GENERAL TRUST.

Oru-Kel pulsed. "Good. Relief cannot travel naked."

Vela-Short said, "That is going to make dispatch briefings strange."

"Strange is better than hungry," Keeps-Water-Calm replied.

Holt tested the export guard by trying the same clean summary again. The system blocked it:

EXPORT BLOCKED: CLEAN-CONSENSUS LANGUAGE PROHIBITED.

It offered a replacement:

CHANGED RELATION / UNCLEAN DEPARTURE / MEDICAL TRANSIT COMPLETE WITH ACTIVE REMAINDERS

Lael read it aloud, then added, "Still too clean."

Ren agreed. "It says active remainders but not who carries them."

The clerk added a mandatory carrier field.

Holt tested again.

CHANGED RELATION / UNCLEAN DEPARTURE / MEDICAL TRANSIT COMPLETE WITH ACTIVE REMAINDERS

CARRIERS: COMPACT EMERGENCY PROCESS / ROUTEHOLDER CONSORTIUM / TRANSLATION WITNESS / CARE-PASSAGE BODIES / MINORITY WARMTH / BOUNDARY RELATION / REPAIR BODIES / PELOGOS RECORD

Salt-Before-Shell said, "Now sentence limps."

Ren looked at the line and felt the oddest relief of the day.

"Good," they said.

The export left the chamber limping.

That was the first honest thing it could do.

The Orison entries came differently. Not as confessions. As changed states.

Third-Voice recorded that all three internal obligations had been altered by the day's contacts: blue-white carried care without clean trust, amber carried refusal with visible medical consequence, green-black carried boundary warning inside local politics without collapsing scale.

Salt-Before-Shell recorded missing limb held, not repaired; protest remaining apart while relation continued; refusal to let Pelagos praise authorize Parliament; injury remaining: human categories still hungry.

Keeps-Water-Calm recorded Pelagos scar reactivated, praise refused again, anti-citation header accepted, injury remaining: reef still lives under categories.

Vessel-kin recorded two bodies in pain, reduced witness conditions, and the warning that repair bodies must not become proof that reform works.

Oru-Kel recorded boundary trace reduced but not gone, private tooth still active, warning relation not message.

The north-east maintenance body recorded only:

Warmth less alone.

Use careful.

No one improved it.

When the departure record closed, nothing felt closed.

That, Ren thought, was the point.

Third-Voice lowered all three fans.

"No one leaves consensus clean," the speaker said again.

This time, the sentence did not sound like warning alone.

It sounded like a way not to lie about leaving.

Chapter 23: Pale Arc in the Brine

Oru-Kel asked for darkness.

The human gallery misunderstood, naturally.

Holt reached for the lighting controls. The clerk dimmed the membrane glare. Rusk closed two route panes. Lael looked at the official record and, with visible effort, did not ask whether darkness would affect admissibility.

Oru-Kel waited until every human had made one unnecessary adjustment.

Then they said, "Not light darkness."

Vela-Short's voice came from the lock. "I appreciate the restraint of waiting."

"Humans learn after touching switches."

Ren took their hand off the slate.

Oru-Kel's long ribbon body rose from the lower basin, acoustic nodes opening in uneven intervals along both sides. The nodes did not glow. They removed glow. Around each opening, the water seemed to forget a little brightness. The Parliament Basin dimmed not because light had faded, but because attention had been asked to stop clinging to surfaces.

"Darkness means less message hunger," Oru-Kel said.

Ren wrote that down, then marked it dangerous.

Rusk said, "We need to understand the boundary rhythm."

"Yes."

"Understanding requires interpretation."

"Sometimes. Sometimes understanding begins when interpretation stops trying to be first."

The nodes along Oru-Kel's body opened in sequence.

Pressure moved through the brine.

The Pale Arc appeared without image.

Ren had seen visualizations from the Lumen observatory: missing neutrino intervals, impossible dips in stellar output, models of an alien boundary device old enough to make human route law look like chalk marks in rain. Those visualizations had been terrifying because they made the unknown large.

This was terrifying because it made the unknown intimate.

The boundary rhythm entered the basin as absence in water. A pulse did not arrive where pulse should have arrived. A current expected by salt-change memory failed to complete. A repair sheet adjusted around nothing and revealed the nothing had shape. The brine did not receive a message. It encountered a limit.

The terminal tried:

SIGNAL PATTERN DETECTED

Oru-Kel's nodes snapped shut.

The basin jolted.

The terminal corrected:

BOUNDARY PATTERN DETECTED

Oru-Kel reopened one node.

"Better."

Holt whispered, "The system corrected from reaction."

"It got slapped by physics," Vela-Short said.

Lael said, "Noted unofficially."

Oru-Kel moved the rhythm toward the care-passage current. The current did not break. It bent. Blue-white bodies along its edge changed spacing. Amber bodies did not retreat, but their filaments curled inward. Green-white repair sheets thickened in a crescent, not to block the rhythm, but to show where the boundary made certain movements expensive.

"This is not communication," Oru-Kel said. "Communication asks relation to carry intent. Boundary asks relation to notice limit."

Rusk stared into the dimmed water. "Who set the limit?"

"Wrong first question."

"Of course."

Ren said, "What is the first question?"

Oru-Kel's nodes opened and closed twice before answering.

"What changes when limit is ignored?"

The brine answered.

Oru-Kel sent the private route tooth into the rhythm, not as a real route, but as a pressure model. The thin Pale Arc-adjacent corridor glowed in the dark water. It did not cross the boundary device. It did not need to. Its pricing pressure, escort speculation, underwriter models, and emergency corridor fantasies created a relational simplification: space treated as empty if enough private actors wanted a line through it.

The boundary rhythm did not attack.

It withdrew expected response.

The route model lost timing confidence. Then cold-chain confidence. Then rescue confidence. Then political confidence. Not catastrophe as explosion. Catastrophe as assumptions silently losing the right to be assumptions.

Rusk sat down.

He did not seem to notice.

"That is what the bypass risks?" he asked.

Oru-Kel said, "One small version."

"Small."

"Yes."

"I hate scale."

"Scale does not notice."

Ren watched the private tooth flicker. Human systems wanted the Pale Arc to be enemy, gate, mystery, resource, weapon, message, destiny. Any of those would be easier than boundary. A message could be decoded. A weapon could be deterred. A resource could be licensed. A destiny could be preached. A boundary had to be respected before it explained itself, if it ever did.

Keeps-Water-Calm spoke from the repair chamber. "Humans called quiet shelf quiet because humans did not hear reef."

"Yes," Ren said.

"Humans may call Pale Arc silent because humans do not hear warning."

Oru-Kel's nodes pulsed. "Already happens."

Lael opened a note. "Then our records need anti-communication language."

Ren almost smiled. "Anti-citation, anti-communication. We are building a very annoying archive."

"Good."

Lael wrote:

PALE ARC BOUNDARY RHYTHM SHALL NOT BE CHARACTERIZED AS MESSAGE, INVITATION, THREAT, CLAIM, OR NEGOTIATION WITHOUT FURTHER EVIDENCE. Current evidence supports warning relation: a boundary practice that changes expected response when route or political simplification exceeds tolerance.

Oru-Kel said, "Add not inert."

Lael added:

Not communication does not mean inert.

Salt-Before-Shell scraped, "Add not human property because not talking."

Lael added that too:

Noncommunicative status shall not be treated as absence of standing, value, or constraint.

Holt said, "That breaks half of survey law."

Keeps-Water-Calm: "Only half?"

Holt looked pained. "The half I know how to fix badly."

Ren respected that more than optimism.

Third-Voice moved through the dim brine with all three fans low. "Parliament wound hears old boundary."

Oru-Kel answered, "Yes. Not same. Related."

Blue-white fan: "Human need crosses boundary carefully or not at all."

Amber fan: "Human appetite calls boundary negotiable."

Green-black fan: "Simplification is the shared danger."

The cracked vote body pulsed faintly.

The second folded vessel answered.

The minority warmth glowed.

Salt-Before-Shell's held limb curled in Vessel-kin's care.

The room understood with bodies before it understood with law: the Pale Arc was not intruding on Parliament politics. Parliament politics had revealed a local form of a larger pattern. Treat relation as empty, simplify the route, erase the dissent, force a clean party, demand a single answer, call silence permission, call warning threat. Each act made a line through what had not consented to become passable.

Rusk said, "The remaining private route tooth must go dark."

Lael looked at him. "Can you do it?"

"Not alone."

No one corrected him this time.

Progress.

Oru-Kel's body dimmed the private tooth until only its outline remained. "Need pressure. Not panic."

"Expose blind owner?" Ren asked.

Lael said, "If we expose without evidence, we trigger denial and market curiosity."

Holt said, "If we hash-lock only, the blind owner keeps pricing."

Rusk said, "If we freeze underwriter support, they move to gray pools."

Salt-Before-Shell: "Human teeth grow replacement teeth."

Vela-Short muttered, "That image is staying with me."

Oru-Kel moved the boundary rhythm again. The remaining tooth lost brightness whenever the care-passage current, the wet record, and the hash-locked hazard notice pulsed together. It regained brightness when any one of them tried to act alone.

Ren saw the answer and disliked it.

"Coordinated relation," they said.

Third-Voice: "Yes."

"Not one authority."

"Yes."

"Not clean."

Salt-Before-Shell: "Finally humans stop expecting clean water from teeth."

Lael wrote:

Response to remaining private Pale Arc-adjacent route model requires coordinated relation among Compact emergency office, routeholder risk bridge, Parliament boundary witness, and affected care-passage bodies. No single authority should claim closure.

Rusk read it. "That will be slow."

Oru-Kel said, "Boundary already slowed you. This admits it."

Holt, still watching the tooth brighten and dim, said, "We can test coordination without exposing geometry."

Lael looked at him. "Define test."

"A four-part pressure pulse. Not a command. Not a route action. Each relation sends only what it is authorized to send. The model fingerprint receives all four at once: Compact emergency concern, routeholder bridge withdrawal, Parliament boundary disturbance, and care-passage nonprecedent notice. If the tooth dims only when all four arrive together, that supports coordinated relation as the required response."

Rusk said, "And if it panics the market?"

Holt shook his head. "No public feed. Fingerprint channel only. The blind owner will know its model is being addressed. Underwriters holding matched fingerprints will know the model is unstable. No one receives geometry."

Salt-Before-Shell's speaker scraped. "Private tooth feels watched by those bitten."

"Yes," Holt said.

Lael said, "Care-passage bodies are not enforcement instruments."

Vessel-kin touched the narrowed care current and translated after a long pause. "Care passage can say: medical transit did not make this route clean. Care passage will not become proof for tooth."

Ren wrote:

CARE-PASSAGE NONPRECEDENT NOTICE: MEDICAL TRANSIT SUCCESS DOES NOT AUTHORIZE, CLEAN, OR STABILIZE PRIVATE PALE ARC-ADJACENT ROUTE MODELS.

Rusk opened his consortium channel. His hands were steady now in the way exhaustion sometimes made steadiness cheaper than fear. "Routeholder bridge withdrawal already exists for my consortium. I can extend it to shared cold-chain reputation and emergency escort references for any matched model that remains blind-backed."

Lael said, "Compact emergency concern must not become sanction."

"Then say that," Ren said.

Lael did:

COMPACT EMERGENCY CONCERN: BLIND-BACKED PRIVATE ROUTE PRICING NEAR PALE ARC WARNING RELATION CREATES BOUNDARY RISK. THIS CONCERN DOES NOT AUTHORIZE SANCTION AGAINST ORISON DELIBERATION, CARE-PASSAGE BODIES, OR PARLIAMENT DELAY.

Oru-Kel pulsed once. "Boundary witness."

Ren waited.

The pulse moved through the brine as darkness again, but smaller than before, a narrow absence wrapped around the model fingerprint rather than the whole chamber.

Oru-Kel said, "Boundary disturbance registered. Not message. Not threat. Disturbance."

Holt assembled the four-part pulse in a sealed pane:

COORDINATED RELATION TEST / PRIVATE PALE ARC-ADJACENT MODEL

1. COMPACT EMERGENCY CONCERN WITHOUT SANCTION

2. ROUTEHOLDER RISK BRIDGE WITHDRAWAL WITHOUT GEOMETRY DISCLOSURE

3. PARLIAMENT BOUNDARY DISTURBANCE WITNESS WITHOUT PARTY CONVERSION

4. CARE-PASSAGE NONPRECEDENT NOTICE WITHOUT ROUTE AUTHORITY

Lael added:

TEST RESULT SHALL NOT BE CITED AS ORISON APPROVAL, PALE ARC COMMUNICATION, OR ROUTE-SAFETY DETERMINATION.

Rusk added, with a sourness that did him credit:

GRAY-POOL MIGRATION AFTER THIS NOTICE SHALL BE RECORDED AS KNOWING AVOIDANCE, NOT INDEPENDENT MARKET ASSESSMENT.

Vela-Short said, "That line has boots."

"It needs boots," Rusk said. "Gray pools love soft floors."

The pulse went out.

For five seconds, the remaining tooth brightened.

Ren's body reacted before their mind did. Shoulders up. Breath caught. The old human lesson: if a warning makes the danger brighter, stop warning. The chamber did not stop. Oru-Kel held the boundary rhythm. Vessel-kin held the care-passage notice. Lael held the sanction caveat. Rusk held the bridge withdrawal.

The tooth brightened again, then split into three thinner tendrils.

"Gray migration attempt," Holt said.

Rusk was already reading. "One underwriter mirror, one escort pool, one analytics derivative."

"Can they escape?" Lael asked.

"They can move. They cannot claim innocence if they move after the pulse."

Salt-Before-Shell said, "Tooth runs. Feet become record."

The tendrils tried to separate from the original model fingerprint. Holt's derivative warning caught two. The third, the analytics derivative, changed its hash by dropping the Pale Arc proximity field.

Oru-Kel's nodes opened sharply.

The brine went cold.

"It removes old dark from tooth to make tooth look elsewhere," Oru-Kel said.

Rusk's voice hardened. "That is fraud."

Lael said, "Careful."

"No. It is. They are stripping the risk feature that makes the model dangerous and reselling the remainder as ordinary Shoals contingency."

Holt captured the derivative.

Ren wrote:

DERIVATIVE STRIPPING EVENT: ANALYTICS MODEL REMOVED PALE ARC PROXIMITY FIELD AFTER COORDINATED RELATION NOTICE. STRIPPED MODEL SHALL BE TREATED AS KNOWING CONCEALMENT OF BOUNDARY RISK.

Lael added:

NOT PROOF OF PALE ARC INTENT. PROOF OF HUMAN MARKET AVOIDANCE.

The tooth dimmed then.

Not dark. Not gone. But dimmed enough that Oru-Kel's boundary rhythm eased and the care-passage current stopped bending around it.

Rusk leaned back, eyes closed. "Not closure."

Third-Voice answered, "Correct."

"Actionable remainder?"

Lael nodded. "Yes."

Ren recorded:

COORDINATED RELATION REDUCED ACTIVE PRIVATE PRESSURE. REMAINING WORK: IDENTIFY BLIND OWNER, TRACK DERIVATIVE STRIPPING, MAINTAIN BOUNDARY WITNESS, PRESERVE NONPRECEDENT CARE-PASSAGE NOTICE.

Oru-Kel's nodes pulsed low and dark. "Better. Boundary hears less teeth."

The brine brightened by one degree.

Oru-Kel's darkness request ended.

Human lights looked vulgar when they returned.

No one said so. Everyone felt it.

Ren saved the packet:

PALE ARC IN THE BRINE / WARNING RELATION / NOT MESSAGE.

They added Mira's warning to the header:

THIS NOTE IS ALSO A HANDLE. USE CAREFUL.

The basin accepted the record.

Beyond the membrane, the medical convoy completed transfer.

Inside the Parliament, the old dark was no longer elsewhere.

Chapter 24: The Routeholder Offer

Aven Rusk asked for the private channel after the medical convoy cleared the outer membrane.

He did not ask Lael first.

He asked the chamber.

Ren noticed that before they noticed the words. Rusk had been learning, or at least learning the cost of appearing not to learn. He stood in the brine with his formal coat sealed at the throat, sleeves darkened to the elbow, shoes weighted by salt. No one had required him to remain wet after the care-passage emergency. He had stayed.

That mattered.

It did not absolve him.

"I can help identify the remaining routeholder instrument," Rusk said.

The translation beads took a careful second to decide whether help meant aid, leverage, obligation, or bait. They settled on a stacked chord that made Third-Voice's amber fan rise.

Lael said, "State the whole offer."

Rusk looked at her, then at Ren, then at the cracked vote body. "I can help trace the blind owner behind the private route tooth. My office has partial escrow keys, underwriter access logs, and timing records that Compact emergency law cannot compel fast enough. If I use them now, we can narrow the owner to a useful cluster before the route migrates."

"Useful to whom?" Salt-Before-Shell asked.

Rusk did not flinch. "Useful to stopping it."

"You attach condition."

"Yes."

The chamber darkened by a shade.

At the edge of the basin, Keeps-Water-Calm moved for the first time since the medical transfer. The Pelagos diplomat had held still so long that some of the human staff had mistaken stillness for withdrawal. The Shoals did not make that mistake. Water around him had been remembering.

Rusk continued, "The routeholder coalition needs a simplified treaty signature before the next Meridian risk window closes. Not a full Parliament resolution. Not a final sovereignty instrument. A provisional operational signature. One line. One accountable party authorized to receive route hazard notices and issue binding acknowledgments."

Ren heard the violence hiding inside the word one.

Third-Voice heard it with three bodies.

Blue-white fan: "One accountable party erases the bodies not made into account."

Amber fan: "One notice receiver becomes one throat."

Green-black fan: "One throat can be held."

Rusk said, "One throat can answer."

Salt-Before-Shell snapped three limbs against the basin rail. "Human market loves throat. Easy to cut. Easy to feed. Easy to blame."

"This is not market appetite," Rusk said.

Lael laughed once, without humor. "Aven."

He accepted the correction with a tilt of his head. "It is not only market appetite."

The difference was small. It was also the largest honesty he had offered that day.

Ren opened a fresh record pane and did not label it yet.

Oru-Kel-Under-Quiet dimmed near the place where the remaining private route tooth had been shown. The tooth did not appear at full brightness now. The earlier coordinated pulse had taught it caution, or taught its owner caution, or revealed that caution had been there all along. A faint angular pressure remained behind the chamber diagram, like a hook seen under skin.

Rusk pointed to it. "That thing is built to survive fragmented response. It profits from deliberation delay. It prices uncertainty. I do not need you to like routeholder law to understand routeholder machinery. This instrument expects you to reject centralization. It expects the Compact to wait for Parliament form. It expects my coalition to argue over liability until the trail goes cold."

"And therefore we become what it expects less?" Ren asked.

Rusk turned. "You become fast enough."

"By becoming legible to your system."

"By giving my system something it can bind."

Lael's face changed. It was not anger first. It was recognition. Ren had seen the same expression in disaster briefings when someone named the thing everyone had built around but refused to call structure.

"You want a socket," Lael said.

Rusk did not answer quickly.

Third-Voice repeated the word through the chamber. The translation chose a biological image first, then rejected it, then offered a mechanical one. Socket. Port. Receiving wound. Intentional opening.

The brine disliked all of them.

"Routeholder systems require a place to deliver enforceable warnings," Rusk said. "Without that, warnings become advisory. Advisory warnings become litigation artifacts. Litigation artifacts arrive after wreckage."

Keeps-Water-Calm's skin along the left shoulder rippled with sudden color.

Ren saw Lael look toward him and stop herself from asking too soon.

Salt-Before-Shell did not stop. "You speak wreckage now because wreckage makes your hook look kind."

"No," Rusk said. "I speak wreckage because I have seen the timing records."

"Show them."

"I cannot show proprietary routeholder keys in full Parliament session."

Salt-Before-Shell's mouth plates opened in a cold pattern. "Then your offer is wet bait."

Rusk's jaw tightened. "I can show enough to a sealed witness group."

"Chosen by you?"

"Chosen by the chamber and my office jointly."

"With veto?"

"With safety exclusions."

"Human veto wearing safety."

The chamber stirred. Ren felt the argument wanting to become old, and therefore easy. The human official with data. The alien chamber with pain. The radical refusing the bargain. The mediator smoothing the edge. The routeholder demanding operational simplicity. Each role was waiting like a chair.

Ren hated chairs.

They wrote nothing for another breath.

Then they said, "What happens if Parliament signs your provisional line?"

Rusk exhaled through his nose. "My coalition releases technical aid immediately. Escrow timing. Underwriter overlap. Migration probability. A live trace window. We freeze the private route tooth's replacement channels before the blind owner can wash the instrument through a new pool."

"And if Parliament refuses?"

"I can release a smaller packet under emergency courtesy."

"How much smaller?"

"Too small to finish the trace."

Lael said, "So the condition is not incidental."

"No."

"You are trading rescue for signature."

Rusk's voice sharpened. "I am trading authority for exposure. If I burn routeholder tools without a recognized recipient, the coalition fractures, and the next emergency gets less cooperation, not more. You know this."

Lael did know it. Her silence admitted that much.

Oru-Kel's body lowered until its lower limbs brushed the basin floor. "Human system says: let us touch you once so we may stop another hand from touching you in secret."

Rusk looked to Ren, as if asking whether that had been fair.

Ren gave him nothing.

Third-Voice's blue-white fan spoke. "If we make one receiver, receiver becomes wound."

Amber fan: "If we refuse receiver, warning arrives broken."

Green-black fan: "If we accept human socket, Parliament shape changes toward human damage."

Rusk said, "Any agreement changes shape. You said that."

The chamber went very quiet.

That was the danger of listening. The other side learned your true words and brought them back carrying knives.

Third-Voice did not retreat. "Yes. Real agreement changes participants. Coercion also changes participants. Difference matters."

"I am not coercing."

Salt-Before-Shell made a sound like salt poured on metal. "You hold medicine behind contract and call it weather."

"This is not medicine."

Keeps-Water-Calm finally spoke.

"After harm, humans often sort tools by name."

The room turned toward him.

He did not look at Rusk. He looked into a portion of water above the cracked vote body, as if the brine there held an older coastline.

"Medicine. Contract. Safety. Liability. Courtesy. Enforcement. Each name says what human law wishes the tool to be. Reef remembers tool by arrival."

Rusk said, carefully, "I am trying to prevent harm."

"Yes," Keeps-Water-Calm said. "That is one arrival."

He lowered one long hand into the basin until his fingers opened against the current.

"There are others."

Ren felt the next chapter of the room before it happened. Not the manuscript chapter. The political one. The part where memory entered and refused to be filed as background.

Lael said softly, "Keeps-Water-Calm, are you offering witness?"

"Not yet."

Salt-Before-Shell shifted in surprise.

Keeps-Water-Calm's shoulder colors moved again, deep green under pale scar tissue. "First, ask routeholder what signature cannot touch."

Rusk frowned. "I do not understand."

"Good."

The translation beads gave the word a clean human shape. The chamber gave it teeth.

Ren wrote:

ROUTEHOLDER OFFER / TECHNICAL AID CONDITIONED ON SIMPLIFIED SIGNATURE / SOCKET RISK.

Then they added a second line:

QUESTION FROM PELAGOS WITNESS: WHAT CANNOT BE REACHED BY SIGNATURE?

Lael read it over their shoulder. "That is going to make everyone angry."

"Useful, then," Ren said.

Rusk looked older by several years. "We do not have time for philosophy."

Oru-Kel pulsed dimly beside the hidden tooth. "You brought a tool that changes body. Body asks what tool cannot understand. This is not philosophy. This is pre-surgery."

Third-Voice's three fans lifted together.

Blue-white: "No provisional single receiver until chamber hears the Pelagos witness."

Amber: "No rejection of technical aid until routeholder answer is recorded."

Green-black: "No claim of clean choice."

Lael translated it into Compact procedural language before anyone could soften it:

"The Salt Parliament suspends decision on the routeholder offer pending witness from Keeps-Water-Calm and a declared limit statement from Aven Rusk regarding what the proposed signature cannot bind, represent, simplify, or cure."

Rusk stared at her. "You want me to argue against my own instrument."

"No," Lael said. "We want you to tell us where it stops."

"That weakens the signature."

Ren said, "It may be the only thing that keeps it from becoming a weapon."

Rusk looked at the hidden tooth, at the reduced witness shell, at the departure record still limping in the archive, and finally at the body that had held a scar across Pelagos years without letting humans make it decorative.

"Fine," he said.

The word was not surrender. It was calculation forced to share a room with witness.

Lael opened a limit statement pane and gave it a title before Rusk could choose one:

ROUTEHOLDER INSTRUMENT LIMIT STATEMENT / DRAFT BEFORE WITNESS

Rusk grimaced. "Draft before witness?"

"You wanted a signature before the witness," Lael said. "Balance."

Salt-Before-Shell pulsed bright amber. "Human advocate grows small claws."

"Do not put that in the record," Lael said.

The clerk, visibly tempted, did not.

Rusk read the blank fields:

THE PROVISIONAL SIGNATURE CANNOT BIND:

THE PROVISIONAL SIGNATURE CANNOT REPRESENT:

THE PROVISIONAL SIGNATURE CANNOT SIMPLIFY:

THE PROVISIONAL SIGNATURE CANNOT CURE:

TECHNICAL AID THAT MUST NOT BE WITHHELD:

TECHNICAL AID THAT REQUIRES RECIPIENT AUTHORITY:

REVOCATION OR REFUSAL ROUTE:

"This is not how routeholder instruments are drafted," he said.

Keeps-Water-Calm answered, "That is why chamber still lives."

Rusk closed his mouth and began.

"Cannot bind: bodies, relations, factions, or Parliament currents not expressly addressed by the provisional receiver. Cannot bind future commercial cargo, sovereign interpretation, withdrawal protest, minority warmth, Pelagos citation, Pale Arc boundary relation, or Orison terms that remain untranslated."

Ren wrote more slowly than Rusk spoke. Not because they could not keep up. Because a fast limit could become another handle.

Lael said, "Add human systems."

Rusk frowned.

"Your signature cannot bind underwriters and routeholders beyond the authority they actually grant. Do not let the Compact think one Orison receiver solves your coalition."

He nodded, tight. "Cannot bind routeholder actors, underwriters, escort firms, gray pools, or analytics derivatives beyond actual signatory authority and enforceable notices."

Oru-Kel pulsed. "Better. Teeth named on both sides."

Rusk moved to the next field. "Cannot represent: Parliament consensus, general Orison consent, care-passage approval, boundary safety, absence of injury, absence of dissent, or trust restored."

Salt-Before-Shell: "Add absence of refusal."

"Cannot represent absence of refusal," Rusk said.

The phrase landed strangely. Human records loved absence because absence was cheap. The room made it expensive by naming it.

"Cannot simplify," Rusk continued, and then stopped.

Lael did not prompt him.

Ren watched him discover that this field was the true wound in the offer. The instrument existed to simplify. It wanted a receiver because human route law needed a throat. Asking what it could not simplify was asking how much of itself it was willing to amputate before entering the chamber.

Rusk said, "Cannot simplify body-scale differences into a single Parliament will. Cannot simplify care need into route consent. Cannot simplify refusal into obstruction.
