Cannot simplify silence into stability. Cannot simplify warning relation into communication. Cannot simplify technical aid into political acceptance."

Third-Voice's green-black fan opened fully.

"Good," the fan said.

Rusk looked as if praise would have been easier than that single word.

"Cannot cure," he said. "Cannot cure the cracked bodies. Cannot cure the hidden minority warmth. Cannot cure Compact understatement. Cannot cure my coalition's private appetite. Cannot cure Pelagos. Cannot cure the Pale Arc boundary risk. Cannot cure the fact that I brought the offer late and conditioned it on a shape useful to my systems."

The last line cost him. Not as much as the chamber had paid. Enough to be real.

Keeps-Water-Calm's scarred shoulder darkened once.

Lael moved to the aid fields. "Technical aid that must not be withheld."

Rusk inhaled. "Emergency courtesy packet. Hash fingerprints for the remaining tooth. Derivative stripping evidence already observed. Non-geometric timing indicators. Underwriter contact timestamps. Gray-pool migration alerts for the next six hours."

"Six?" Ren asked.

"That is what I can release without recipient authority. More requires account controls and liability transfer."

Salt-Before-Shell scraped. "Human gives crumbs and calls meal."

Rusk turned toward the amber body. "Yes. But the crumbs can still show where the meal is being hidden."

For once, Salt-Before-Shell did not strike back immediately.

Lael entered:

EMERGENCY COURTESY PACKET SHALL BE RELEASED WITHOUT PROVISIONAL SIGNATURE AND SHALL NOT BE TREATED AS CONCESSION, SATISFACTION, OR PARTIAL ACCEPTANCE OF SOCKET INSTRUMENT.

Rusk did not object.

"Technical aid that requires recipient authority," Lael said.

"Escrow key use, account-specific underwriter access logs, live trace into private coalition systems, and liability-bearing freeze orders."

"Revocation or refusal route?"

Rusk's mouth tightened. "The receiver, if created, can refuse scope expansion, revoke technical receipt authority, or require body-first review before any warning is converted into route consent. Nonreceiver bodies retain objection channels. No failure to answer the receiver shall be treated as Orison-wide nonresponse."

Ren looked at Lael.

Lael looked at the basin.

Third-Voice spoke with all three fans overlapping.

"Now offer has edges."

Oru-Kel answered, "Edges still cut."

"Yes," Third-Voice said.

Keeps-Water-Calm lifted his hand from the basin. Water streamed from his fingers. "Now scar can speak to tool."

Beyond the chamber membrane, distant equipment knocked once as the medical convoy sealed its outer lock. The sound traveled through water as a small blunt fact.

The private route tooth flickered.

Not gone.

Not triumphant.

Waiting.

Keeps-Water-Calm turned his marked shoulder into the basin light.

"Then I will show the scar," he said.

Chapter 25: Keeps-Water-Calm Shows the Scar

Pelagos bodies did not scar like human bodies.

Ren knew that as a biological fact and then knew, watching Keeps-Water-Calm turn under the basin light, that fact was the least important part.

The pale ridge along his shoulder was not only damaged tissue. It was arranged memory. Fine green lines crossed the old injury in branching paths, each line entering and leaving the scar at a different angle. Some faded before they reached its center. Some stopped abruptly at the boundary and did not cross. One dark line vanished beneath the pale ridge and emerged on the other side thinner, as if the injury had translated it into less.

The chamber made room without being asked.

Not physical room. Political room. Sound fell away. Bodies lowered. The cracked vote body dimmed until its pain remained present but did not occupy the front of the water. Even Salt-Before-Shell withdrew the sharpest posture from his limbs.

Rusk looked uncomfortable in the way of a man who had requested evidence and found himself facing witness.

Keeps-Water-Calm touched two fingers to the scar. "This is from Beryl Shoal."

Lael's eyes closed for one breath.

Ren knew the name from treaty school, where it had been presented as a minor early-contact incident in the southern Pelagos drift corridor. The lesson file had emphasized failures of sensor alignment, delayed notice, cross-cultural evacuation challenges, and the eventual creation of the Beryl Compensation Framework. It had included a map, casualty ranges, and a cheerful note that the framework became a model for later aquatic transit agreements.

No file had mentioned a shoulder.

"The law file says navigation accident," Rusk said before he could stop himself.

Lael opened her eyes.

Keeps-Water-Calm did not look offended. That made it worse.

"Yes," he said. "Human law arrived and named accident."

The basin translated his skin color poorly at first. The beads tried grief, rejected it, tried contempt, rejected that too, then produced a chord Ren felt in the back of the teeth: remembered pressure.

"Before the accident name," Keeps-Water-Calm said, "there was a survey promise. Human survey craft requested passage above juvenile reef. They said no contact. They said no extraction. They said remote scan only."

Rusk's mouth tightened. "That was before current routeholder standards."

"Yes. Before standards. After promise."

No one spoke.

Keeps-Water-Calm drew one finger along the first green branch. "The reef accepted because the human craft did not ask to touch. The craft carried a calibration drone too small to be called vessel in human law. Too small to be declared. Too small to require reef consent."

Ren saw where this was going and wished, uselessly, for it not to.

"The drone descended when current changed. It used anchor needles to hold position. Human file calls micro-contact. Reef calls bite. Juvenile reef opened defense chemistry. Survey craft misread defense as storm bloom. It increased scan heat."

Salt-Before-Shell whispered, "Heat on young reef."

Keeps-Water-Calm touched the dark line that entered the scar and emerged thin. "One brood line survived with memory damage. One brood line fused wrong. One brood line stopped making future."

Rusk said, very quietly, "I am sorry."

"Yes," Keeps-Water-Calm said again. "That came later."

It did not reject the apology. It placed it in order.

Ren's record pane remained open. Their hands hovered over it, useless.

The Pelagos diplomat continued, "After harm, human law arrived with names. Accident. Liability. Compensation. Corrective standard. Non-repetition clause. Joint review. Human law asked who represented the injured reef."

He lifted his scarred shoulder higher.

"The reef could not answer in one body. The harmed brood had changed relation. Some memory remained in living tissue. Some remained in chemical absence. Some remained in water that no longer carried future larvae. Human law needed a party."

Lael said, "So it made one."

"It invited one."

The distinction cut differently.

"My predecessor accepted," Keeps-Water-Calm said. "Not because the shape was true. Because the hatchery needed filters, the surviving brood needed mineral correction, and the human survey consortium would not release full remedy without authorized receipt."

Rusk looked down.

The private route tooth flickered once behind the chamber diagram.

Oru-Kel pulsed faint dark around it, not enough to expose, enough to remind the room that pressure had listeners.

Keeps-Water-Calm said, "Signature brought aid. Signature also taught human systems that reef could be made into answer after harm. Every later file found the answer easier. Every later request arrived with a place already carved."

He touched the pale ridge.

"This is the place."

Third-Voice's blue-white fan folded in.

Amber fan: "Aid became shape memory."

Green-black fan: "Shape memory became future demand."

Salt-Before-Shell said, "And humans teach this as success."

No human contradicted him.

Ren had the absurd thought that a good school could be a machine for preserving wrong order. Survey, accident, framework, reform. It had all sounded responsible when the injury was distant and translated into outcomes. Here the order was different. Promise, hidden instrument, bite, heat, damaged future, party made under need, aid released through the wound.

Rusk lifted his head. "The routeholder offer is not Beryl Shoal."

Keeps-Water-Calm inclined his body. "No."

The answer did not help him.

"We are trying to identify a private hazard before it harms more bodies," Rusk said. "I am not asking you to accept a permanent representative. I am asking for a provisional operational recipient."

"Yes."

"That matters."

"Yes."

Rusk spread his hands, palms open under the water. "Then what do you want from me?"

Keeps-Water-Calm looked at the hands first, then the face. "Name what your signature cannot touch."

Rusk was silent.

Lael did not rescue him.

Ren saw the routeholder in him fight the bureaucrat in him and the frightened person under both. If he answered too narrowly, the chamber would reject him. If he answered too honestly, his coalition might reject him. If he refused to answer, the private route tooth would keep waiting.

"It cannot make Parliament singular," Rusk said at last.

Third-Voice's amber fan lifted.

"It cannot represent injured memory that has no designated speaker."

Keeps-Water-Calm watched him.

Rusk swallowed. "It cannot cure prior simplifications. It cannot prevent future misuse by itself. It cannot convert technical receipt into consent for treaty alteration."

Salt-Before-Shell said, "By itself."

Rusk grimaced. "I hear it."

"Say without escape."

Lael looked at Salt-Before-Shell sharply, but Keeps-Water-Calm raised one hand.

Rusk said, "Technical receipt is not consent for treaty alteration."

Ren wrote it before anyone could improve it.

The room changed around the sentence. Not healed. Not convinced. Changed.

Oru-Kel brightened slightly. "More."

Rusk's voice roughened. "A provisional receiver cannot be treated as the whole wounded relation. It cannot bind dissenting bodies to silence. It cannot be renewed automatically because my systems find it convenient."

Lael said, "And the data?"

He looked at her.

"What can you release before signature?"

"Enough to verify the hazard class and replacement-channel pattern."

"Enough for independent nonhuman review?"

Rusk hesitated.

Lael's expression hardened.

He said, "Enough for a sealed mixed witness group, with routeholder proprietary fields blinded."

Salt-Before-Shell started to object.

Ren said, "Blinded fields can hide the owner."

Rusk shook his head. "Not if the blinding key is held outside routeholder custody."

"By whom?"

That question moved through the chamber like a current looking for a crack.

Keeps-Water-Calm answered, "By damaged party memory."

Rusk stared. "That is not a custodian."

"It is why custody matters."

Ren felt their hands begin to move, chasing a structure they did not yet understand. Mixed witness group. Nonhuman review. Limit statement. Damaged party memory as custody constraint. Provisional receiver not equal to consent. It sounded almost usable. It also sounded like another way to make a record that centered the human problem of enforceability.

They did not see the flaw yet.

That was how flaws worked.

Third-Voice saw Ren writing and turned all three fans toward the pane.

Blue-white: "Careful."

Amber: "Record will want center."

Green-black: "Do not give it only human spine."

Ren stopped.

The warning arrived a breath too late to prevent confidence.

"I can draft a multi-state witness structure," they said.

Lael looked relieved.

Rusk looked relieved.

That should have warned them more than Third-Voice had.

Keeps-Water-Calm lowered his scarred shoulder back into ordinary light. The pale ridge remained visible even when the light moved away from it.

"Draft," he said. "Then we will see what it harms."

Ren drafted too fast.

They knew it as they did it, which did not stop the hand. The structure came easily because human law had trained them to make crisis usable: identify a protected data set, define custodians, mark disclosure levels, appoint reviewers, create a correction channel, limit precedent, attach expiration. It was all good practice. It was also a set of grooves, and Ren's mind slid into them under pressure.

MULTI-STATE WITNESS STRUCTURE / ROUTEHOLDER TRACE PACKET

1. ROUTEHOLDER DATA CUSTODIAN

2. COMPACT ADVOCATE REVIEW

3. PARLIAMENT BOUNDARY OBSERVER

4. ORISON BODY-FIRST COMMENT WINDOW

5. PROPRIETARY FIELD BLINDING

6. EMERGENCY USE LIMIT

7. EXPIRATION AFTER ROUTE TOOTH IDENTIFICATION

The list looked responsible.

Lael leaned toward it with visible hunger. "That could work."

Rusk said, "That is close to something my office can defend."

Ren's stomach sank.

There it was again: the relief of powerful systems when a structure fit their hands.

Third-Voice's amber fan snapped open. "Human spine."

Ren closed their eyes.

Keeps-Water-Calm did not sound angry. "Show harm."

The basin obeyed before Ren could ask how. The draft became a shape in water. Routeholder data custodian formed as a heavy central stem. Compact advocate review wrapped around it like a brace. Parliament boundary observer appeared as a lateral node attached to the stem. Orison body-first comment window became a soft fringe at the outer edge, opening after the main structure already existed.

Salt-Before-Shell struck the basin rail. "Comment window."

Two words. Enough.

Rusk looked at the shape and then away.

Lael said, "We made Orison bodies respondents again."

"Yes," Ren said.

They wanted to delete the draft. The record would not let them. Good. Bad drafts were evidence too.

Keeps-Water-Calm touched the pale ridge on his shoulder. "Beryl had comment window. After party shape. After aid instrument. After human file already knew where answer should live."

The Pelagos diplomat moved one finger along a green branch that stopped at the scar boundary. "This line did not cross. Human file asked it for comment anyway."

The translation beads struggled with that and rendered:

COMMENT REQUEST SENT TO MEMORY THAT HAD BEEN MADE UNABLE TO CONTINUE.

The room absorbed the sentence in layers.

Ren wrote under their draft:

HARM: STRUCTURE CENTERS ROUTEHOLDER DATA AND MAKES ORISON RELATION COMMENT AFTER THE HUMAN SPINE EXISTS.

Lael added:

HARM: BODY-FIRST COMMENT WINDOW IS NOT BODY-FIRST IF IT OPENS AFTER CUSTODY ARCHITECTURE IS FIXED.

Rusk added nothing.

Salt-Before-Shell turned toward him. "Routeholder adds harm."

He lifted his head. "Harm: proprietary blinding still lets my office define what must be hidden before affected relations can contest whether hiding is the harm."

Keeps-Water-Calm's scarred shoulder dimmed once.

"Better," he said.

Ren deleted nothing. Instead they opened a second pane.

"What is the nonhuman spine?" they asked.

Oru-Kel pulsed low. "Wrong second question. Still wants spine."

Ren put both hands flat on the slate edge and waited until shame stopped trying to become speed.

"What shape does not need a spine?" they asked.

The chamber did not answer quickly.

That was the first sign the question had improved.

Vessel-kin moved from the folded body to the edge of the witness water. "Cluster. Not spine. Each holder keeps what it can be harmed by holding."

Holt frowned. "Distributed custody?"

Lael said, "No. That still makes custody the governing concept."

Vessel-kin touched the water again. "Distributed exposure."

The phrase entered the chamber and did not settle. It moved.

Keeps-Water-Calm said, "Beryl failed because exposure arrived through one made party. Harm had many places. Aid had one gate."

Ren began again, slower.

DISTRIBUTED EXPOSURE STRUCTURE / DRAFT AFTER HARM

1. ROUTEHOLDER RELEASES EMERGENCY COURTESY PACKET WITHOUT SIGNATURE.

2. PROPRIETARY BLINDING CLAIMS ARE LISTED BEFORE ACCEPTED.

3. EACH BLINDING CLAIM RECEIVES A HARM QUESTION: WHO OR WHAT IS MADE UNABLE TO OBJECT IF THIS FIELD STAYS HIDDEN?

4. PARLIAMENT BOUNDARY WITNESS HOLDS DISTURBANCE AGAINST MODEL FINGERPRINT, NOT PARTY STATUS.

5. CARE-PASSAGE BODIES HOLD NONPRECEDENT NOTICE ONLY; THEY DO NOT RECEIVE ROUTE WARNINGS AS A SOCKET.

6. PELAGOS MEMORY REVIEW MAY MARK CATEGORY OR PARTY-SHAPE RISKS BY ANALOGY, WITHOUT BECOMING AUTHORITY OVER SHOALS BODIES.

7. COMPACT ADVOCATE HOLDS SANCTION LIMITS AND UNCERTAINTY LANGUAGE REVIEW.

8. ROUTEHOLDER OFFICE HOLDS ITS OWN TOOL LIMITS, INCLUDING WHAT IT CANNOT BIND, REPRESENT, SIMPLIFY, OR CURE.

9. NO HOLDER'S SILENCE COMPLETES THE STRUCTURE.

10. TRACE WORK MAY PROCEED ONLY ON FIELDS WHOSE HIDING HAS SURVIVED HARM QUESTION REVIEW.

Rusk read it with the expression of a man watching work become harder and therefore less deniable.

"This is slower than the socket," he said.

Oru-Kel replied, "Socket was wound made convenient."

He nodded once. "Yes."

Lael said, "Can your office release the courtesy packet under this structure?"

"Yes."

"Can it release enough for harm-question review before signature?"

Rusk hesitated, then looked at Keeps-Water-Calm's scar and did not hide behind the hesitation. "Yes, but it will expose our blinding logic to challenge."

Salt-Before-Shell said, "That is point."

"I know."

Keeps-Water-Calm lowered his hand from the scar. "Now scar has spoken to tool."

Ren marked both drafts active in the record: the harmful human-spine draft and the revised distributed exposure draft.

They wanted the second to replace the first.

The chamber made them keep both.

Because forgetting the bad shape was how it returned clean.

Chapter 26: Ren Builds a Bad Record

Ren built the first draft too well.

That was the problem.

They worked in the recessed witness alcove while the chamber settled into a waiting current. Lael stood close enough to read every line before it entered the formal pane. Rusk waited at the opposite edge with a routeholder slate sealed against the brine, his thumb moving in small frustrated circles over the lock ridge. Third-Voice stayed between them and the cracked vote body, three fans half-open, every color subdued.

Keeps-Water-Calm did not watch the draft.

He watched Ren.

Ren should have taken that as instruction.

Instead they took it as pressure and worked faster.

The structure made sense. That was how it betrayed them. It named five states: Compact emergency notice, routeholder technical disclosure, Orison Parliament witness, Pelagos damaged-memory custody, and affected care-passage body review. It placed each state beside the others in a shared record. It blocked conversion of technical receipt into treaty consent. It required a limit statement from the routeholder coalition before any provisional receiver could operate. It forbade automatic renewal. It created a sealed key split outside routeholder custody.

Lael read the first section and said, "This is useful."

Rusk read the second and said, "This might pass."

Ren should have stopped there.

Useful to Lael meant it could be filed. Might pass to Rusk meant routeholder systems could digest it. The two approvals arrived from opposite sides and met inside the same human machine.

Ren kept writing.

They added definitions.

Witness State One: Compact Emergency Office.

Witness State Two: Routeholder Technical Coalition.

Witness State Three: Salt Parliament Boundary Witness.

Witness State Four: Pelagos Damaged Memory Custodian.

Witness State Five: Care-Passage Affected Bodies.

The words looked clean. The alignment looked generous. No single party held the full key. No single signature claimed total consent. Every state had a declared scope. Every scope had a limit.

Ren felt, dangerously, proud.

"Read aloud," Third-Voice said.

Ren did.

At first the chamber held.

When Ren reached State Three, the water around the cracked vote body tightened.

When they reached State Four, Keeps-Water-Calm's scar darkened.

When they reached State Five, Salt-Before-Shell laughed.

It was not a human laugh. It carried no surprise and no joy. It sounded like a shell split after pressure had already done the work.

"There," he said.

Ren stopped. "Where?"

"Human asks where. Good."

Lael looked from the pane to the chamber. "Salt-Before-Shell, state the objection."

"No."

The refusal hit harder than an argument.

Lael's patience thinned. "We cannot revise an objection that is not stated."

Salt-Before-Shell extended one limb toward the draft without touching it. "That sentence is the objection."

Ren looked at the line under their cursor.

State Five: Care-Passage Affected Bodies shall provide review of operational impacts through designated representatives approved by the Parliament witness.

It was not the worst sentence they had ever written.

That was also the problem.

Third-Voice's green-black fan lowered. "Designated representatives approved by Parliament witness."

Ren felt heat rise under their collar.

"I was trying to keep review from being captured by routeholder procedure," they said.

Blue-white fan: "You moved capture to Parliament form."

Amber fan: "You made affected bodies legible by permission."

Green-black fan: "You gave the witness a gate."

Ren stared at the line until the words came apart.

Lael said, carefully, "That is fixable."

Keeps-Water-Calm finally looked at the pane. "Yes. It is fixable. The scar is also healed."

No one in the chamber mistook that for comfort.

Rusk said, "We need a workable gate. If everyone can enter the witness state without designation, the record becomes unusable."

Salt-Before-Shell turned on him with terrifying calm. "Unusable to whom?"

"To anyone who has to act on it."

"You mean you."

"I mean the systems that can stop the private instrument."

"Human systems again become the spine."

Rusk opened his mouth, then closed it.

Ren looked back at the draft. The spine was everywhere now that Third-Voice had named it. The headings were parallel, but the grammar was not. Compact office shall receive. Routeholder coalition shall disclose. Parliament witness shall approve. Pelagos custodian shall hold. Care-passage bodies shall provide. Every nonhuman relation had been converted into a function beside a human verb.

They had built a table and mistaken symmetry for fairness.

Oru-Kel pulsed from the far side of the basin. "Bad record smells clean."

Ren let out a breath that was almost a laugh and almost not. "Yes."

Lael touched the edge of the pane. "We revise."

Salt-Before-Shell said, "You revise because caught. Human law always revises after bite."

That landed where he meant it to land. On Keeps-Water-Calm's scar. On the cracked vote body. On the medical convoy. On the route tooth still waiting behind the diagram.

Lael's face tightened. "Do not make correction impossible because first draft failed."

"I make trust impossible because first draft revealed truth."

"Trust was already damaged."

"Then stop asking damaged trust to sign tools."

The chamber current changed.

Ren saw it before the formal motion appeared. Bodies were aligning around injury instead of procedure. Salt-Before-Shell was not merely angry now. He was gathering those who had been waiting for a reason to leave the human frame entirely.

Third-Voice sensed it too. All three fans opened.

Blue-white: "Careful. Withdrawal current forming."

Amber: "Do not answer with command."

Green-black: "Do not answer with apology that asks for quiet."

Lael heard the warning and still stepped toward duty. "If Parliament suspends all human treaty obligations now, the private route instrument benefits."

Salt-Before-Shell's limbs spread. "Good. Say it plainly. We must remain bound because your enemy benefits if we leave."

"No," Lael said.

"Yes."

Rusk said, "That is not what she means."

"Routeholder should not rescue interpreter from her own sentence."

Rusk went silent.

Ren turned off the formal pane.

Lael looked at them sharply. "Ren."

"It is doing harm while open."

"We need the draft."

"We need not to pretend the draft is neutral."

They copied the bad record into a sealed error pane instead of deleting it. The archive accepted the change with a small confirmation pulse:

FAILED WITNESS DRAFT / HUMAN SPINE ERROR / DO NOT USE AS STRUCTURE.

Ren added:

Failure mode: parallel categories centered administrative action, not relation. Affected bodies were granted review through approval rather than presence. Damaged memory was treated as custody role rather than continuing relation. Technical enforceability became hidden center.

Their hands shook after the final sentence.

Keeps-Water-Calm read it and gave the smallest possible sign of acknowledgment.

Not forgiveness.

Acknowledgment.

"Now," he said, "you have a useful bad thing."

Ren thought that should have been the end of the error.

The chamber disagreed.

The sealed pane opened a copy of the failed draft in the water, not the text but the shape beneath it. Compact emergency office became a bright hinge. Routeholder technical coalition became a locked bar. Parliament boundary witness became a gate with attractive openings. Pelagos damaged-memory custody became a bowl set below the bar. Care-passage affected bodies became small currents flowing toward the gate and stopping there.

Ren saw the harm more clearly as geometry than they had as prose.

"I made the routeholder problem the center," they said.

Third-Voice's blue-white fan answered, "You made stopping harm the center."

That sounded kinder.

Then amber said, "Stopping harm through human mechanism."

Green-black: "Mechanism became center."

There it was. The trap had not been bad intention, or panic, or routeholder capture alone. It had been the old emergency theology: if a structure can act, the structure belongs in the middle. Everything wounded must arrange itself around action.

Lael said, "Then reverse the dependency."

Salt-Before-Shell watched her with dangerous stillness. "Say more."

Lael did, slowly. "The trace process cannot ask affected relations to enter a human witness state. The routeholder packet must enter existing relations with stated limits. If a relation cannot receive a field without being reshaped, that field remains withheld and the withholding is recorded as routeholder cost, not Orison silence."

Rusk's head lifted. "That may make the trace incomplete."

"Yes," Lael said.

"Incomplete trace means the owner may escape."

Vessel-kin said, "Complete trace that makes new wound also escape."

Rusk's face shut down, then opened again with effort. "Yes."

Ren opened a new pane, but they did not write headings first. They wrote prohibitions:

NO CENTRAL WITNESS STATE SHALL BE CREATED FOR ROUTEHOLDER CONVENIENCE.

NO AFFECTED BODY SHALL BE REQUIRED TO BECOME DESIGNATED REPRESENTATIVE IN ORDER TO BE HARMED BY, OBJECT TO, OR LIMIT USE OF TRACE DATA.

NO DAMAGED MEMORY SHALL BE MADE CUSTODIAN OF HUMAN PROPRIETARY RISK UNLESS IT REQUESTS THAT ROLE.

NO TECHNICAL COMPLETENESS SHALL OUTRANK RELATIONAL NONINJURY.

The chamber held.

Not approval. Attention.

Ren continued, this time with a structure that kept refusing to become smooth:

ANTI-SPINE TRACE REVISION / UNSTABLE DRAFT

1. ROUTEHOLDER DATA ENTERS AS OFFERED MATERIAL, NOT CENTER.

2. EACH DATA FIELD CARRIES ITS CLAIMED USE, CLAIMED HIDDEN PORTION, AND EXPECTED ACTION.

3. EACH RELATION MAY ACCEPT, REFUSE, DELAY, OR MARK FIELD AS RESHAPING PRESSURE WITHOUT BECOMING A REPRESENTATIVE.

4. FAILURE TO RECEIVE A FIELD DOES NOT EQUAL NONRESPONSE.

5. INCOMPLETE TRACE CAUSED BY NONINJURY LIMITS SHALL BE RECORDED AS COST OF ROUTEHOLDER TOOL DESIGN.

6. ANY PROVISIONAL RECEIVER, IF LATER CREATED, CAN RECEIVE ONLY FIELDS ALREADY TESTED AGAINST RESHAPING PRESSURE.

7. BAD DRAFT REMAINS ATTACHED AS WARNING.

Rusk read the revision like a man reading the invoice for a system he had inherited and used anyway.

"My office can work with parts of this," he said.

Salt-Before-Shell's limbs lifted. "Again."

Rusk looked at him.

"Human says can work. Means can eat?"

"No," Rusk said, too fast.

Then he stopped.

The room let him stop.

"Maybe," he corrected. "It means my office will try to digest it into workflow. That is a risk."

"Name guard," Salt-Before-Shell said.

Rusk stared at the revision. "Workflow conversion guard. Any operational conversion must preserve the prohibitions and the attached bad draft. If a system drops the bad draft, the converted workflow loses authority."

Holt said, "I can implement that as dependency."

Lael turned. "Can or should have already?"

"Both," Holt said, no longer needing the lesson twice.

He added:

WORKFLOW CONVERSION GUARD: DERIVATIVE PROCEDURES MUST CARRY ANTI-SPINE PROHIBITIONS AND FAILED WITNESS DRAFT. OMISSION LOWERS AUTHORITY AND BLOCKS OPERATIONAL RELIANCE.

The sealed bad draft pulsed once beside the revision.

For one breath, Ren thought the current might settle.

Then Salt-Before-Shell moved.

Salt-Before-Shell moved toward the central basin, and the chamber made way for him in a different manner than it had for the scar. That earlier room had been witness room. This was motion room.

Lael said, "Salt-Before-Shell, wait."

"No."

The word needed no translation.

He placed two limbs against the cracked vote body's outer brace. The body shivered, not from damage this time but from recognition. Minority warmth moved inside it. Majority structure moved beside it. Neither resolved into the other.

Salt-Before-Shell spoke to the chamber, not to the humans.

"We have heard offer. We have heard scar. We have seen human friend build human cage with soft hands. We have seen routeholder name limits because forced. We have seen Compact office fear the shape of our leaving more than the shape of our injury."

Lael flinched.

Ren wanted to object and could not find a sentence that did not prove him right.

Salt-Before-Shell continued, "I call for formal withdrawal consideration."

The chamber temperature seemed to drop.

Third-Voice's amber fan snapped open. "Full suspension?"

"All human treaty obligations pending re-bodying of consent."

Rusk cursed under his breath.

Lael went very still.

Ren looked at the sealed bad draft, then at the cracked vote body, then at the hidden tooth behind the chamber diagram.

The private route instrument brightened.

Not much.

Enough.

Chapter 27: Salt-Before-Shell Calls for Withdrawal

Formal withdrawal did not begin with a vote.

It began with inventory.

The Salt Parliament changed its light, and every human system in the chamber misunderstood the change for three seconds. Ren's pane flashed amber, then white, then displayed a useless message:

PROCEDURAL STATE UNKNOWN.

Lael's Compact assistant whispered into her earlink and went silent when she raised one hand. Rusk's routeholder slate locked itself behind emergency compliance glass. The medical monitors along the outer membrane dropped into read-only mode. Even the translation beads paused, as if language had stepped to the edge of a pier and found no water beneath it.

Then the chamber counted what human treaties touched.

Not aloud at first.

In bodies.

Care-passage currents dimmed where human emergency clauses governed access. Basin locks cooled where Compact inspection rights had been negotiated. Route notice threads withdrew from public display and curled into private Orison memory. Exchange bodies carried their stored dissent closer to their centers. Delegates who had accepted human-facing roles loosened those roles from their limbs one by one.

Ren saw the map of obligation appear by absence.

It was everywhere.

Salt-Before-Shell kept two limbs on the cracked vote body's brace. "This is the first count."

Third-Voice's blue-white fan translated for the human record. "Inventory of active human treaty contact."

Lael said, "Acknowledged."

Her voice did not shake. That cost her something.

Salt-Before-Shell turned one limb toward her. "Do not make courage into permission."

"I will not."

"You will try."

Lael accepted that like a blow she had earned but did not deserve entirely. "Probably."

Ren looked at her then. The honesty was not enough, but it kept the room from snapping.

The second count began.

This one named harm.

The chamber did use sound now, but not speech alone. Each active obligation lit beside the injury associated with it. Emergency access beside quarantine overreach. Translation assistance beside misrecorded consent. Route protection beside private route teeth. Scientific exchange beside hidden instruments too small to be declared. Compensation beside Beryl Shoal's shaped wound. Human chairs beside wet bodies forced to sit in dry categories.

Rusk watched the list grow and lost color.

"Some of these were corrected," he said.

Salt-Before-Shell looked at him with the patience of deep water. "Corrected does not mean removed from body."

"Some obligations prevent worse harm."

"Yes."

That yes frightened him more than refusal.

Salt-Before-Shell addressed the chamber again. "Motion: suspend all human treaty obligations until consent can be re-bodied without human spine, routeholder pressure, Compact emergency shadow, or post-harm party manufacture."

The translation beads worked hard over re-bodied. They offered reconstituted, reauthorized, reconsensed, re-embodied. None held. Ren left the Orison-rooted term in the formal pane with a note: not equivalent to re-signing.

Lael stepped forward. "Compact office requests standing to respond."

Several bodies recoiled.

Third-Voice's amber fan moved between them. "Standing granted only if response is not defense."

Lael breathed in. "Then I will not defend."

Rusk looked alarmed.

Lael continued, "Full suspension will immediately end care-passage support, emergency hazard routing, cross-current medical priority, and several protections that Parliament fought to include. I am not saying this to threaten. I am saying these obligations include work the Shoals demanded because humans had already made the outer system dangerous."

Salt-Before-Shell said, "We know what we demanded."

"Yes. I am saying withdrawal from human treaty obligations may also withdraw tools you forced us to build because we were unsafe without them."

"Then we count which tools are wound and which tools are splint."

"Agreed."

The word surprised the chamber.

Lael did not soften it. "Agreed. Count them. Do not let my office decide the difference."

Rusk whispered, "Lael."

She did not look at him. "If we cannot survive that, the treaty was already fiction."

Ren wrote the sentence into the live record before caution could stop them.

Salt-Before-Shell withdrew one limb from the cracked brace. "Compact office admits fiction."

"No," Lael said. "Compact office admits possibility of fiction."

"Human keeps one step."

"Human is trying not to lie more than necessary."

The chamber held that without approving it.

Rusk asked for standing next.

The answer was not immediate. Routeholder authority had no natural place in a withdrawal motion except as injury and instrument. The chamber conferred through currents too fast for Ren to read. Oru-Kel moved near the hidden tooth, dimming whenever the private route instrument tried to brighten.

Finally Third-Voice spoke.

Blue-white: "Standing denied as party."

Amber: "Standing permitted as exposed machinery."

Green-black: "Answer only questions asked."

Rusk's face closed. "Understood."

Salt-Before-Shell asked, "If obligations suspend, what does routeholder coalition do?"

Rusk's answer came too quickly. "We lose authority to deliver binding warnings."

"Not asked."

He stopped.

Ren saw him find the real answer and hate it.

"Some members will reroute around the Shoals."

"Some."

"Some will attempt private instruments."

"Attempt?"

"Use," Rusk said.

The private tooth pulsed once.

Oru-Kel darkened it.

Salt-Before-Shell said, "So obligation binds not only humans to care. It binds human appetite to visible path."

Rusk nodded once. "Yes."

"And you made hidden teeth anyway."

"Not all of us."

"Enough of you."

"Yes."

Keeps-Water-Calm moved close to the central basin. "Withdrawal may be necessary. Withdrawal may also feed the hidden path. Both truths must remain wet."

Salt-Before-Shell turned toward him. "You ask us to stay injured for strategy."

"No. I ask us not to call every exit freedom."

The chamber's memory shifted. Ren felt the sentence pass through the cracked vote body and catch on something inside it.

The damaged exchange body shuddered.

A voice came from within it.

Not Third-Voice's threefold register. Not Salt-Before-Shell. Not the majority warmth. Not the minority heat they had learned to recognize. This voice was two pressures at once, braided badly.

"Do not repair us for counting."

Everything stopped.

The cracked vote body's outer skin flexed. Vessel-kin in the care-passage alcove lifted both hands but did not intervene.

Lael whispered, "Who is that?"

Third-Voice answered with all three fans low. "The body that failed."

Ren's skin prickled. "The exchange witness?"

"What remains of it."

The voice came again, clearer and more painful.

"Do not make us one vote so you can decide whether to leave humans."

Salt-Before-Shell's posture changed. For the first time since the motion began, uncertainty entered his limbs.

The cracked vote body pulsed with majority and minority memory both, not reconciled, not separated, not dead. Its wound had become a participant none of their procedures knew how to seat.

Lael's eyes found Ren.

Ren did not open a draft.

Not yet.

Third-Voice said, "Withdrawal motion pauses."

Salt-Before-Shell looked ready to object.

Keeps-Water-Calm said, "If the harmed body asks not to be repaired for our convenience, we hear it before deciding freedom."

The private route tooth dimmed again, as if even hidden appetite had lost its clean timing.

Ren wrote only one line:

BODY REQUESTS DIVISION REMAIN PRESENT.

The line did not enter the withdrawal record.

It hovered beside it.

The distinction mattered immediately. If the line entered the withdrawal record, the failed body would become evidence for or against suspension. If it hovered beside the record, it could speak to the motion without being consumed by it. Ren did not know whether that was right. They knew only that the body had asked not to be repaired for counting, and using the request as a count would be a fast, elegant betrayal.

Lael saw the placement and nodded once.

Salt-Before-Shell saw it too. "Human makes side water."

"Temporary," Ren said. "Until the body chooses where it belongs."

"Body may not choose human where."

"Then the side water remains."

The cracked body pulsed, shallow and irregular. Majority structure brightened near one side of the wound. Minority warmth answered from within the fold. Between them, the braided voice returned.

"Inventory hurts when it asks clean side."

Third-Voice translated no further.

There was nothing further to translate.

Lael looked at the treaty inventory. Wound. Splint. Obligation. Appetite. Protection. Handle. Every category had begun to harden because the chamber needed to decide what human obligations to suspend. The failed body had felt the hardening first.

"Then the inventory needs a divided-status field," Lael said.

Salt-Before-Shell's limbs tightened. "Again field."

"Yes," Lael said. "A bad word. Help me make it less bad."

The chamber held her in silence, measuring whether the request was honest or merely useful. Lael did not fill the silence. That helped.

Vessel-kin moved close to the cracked body. "Not divided-status. Division-presence."

Ren entered, beside the withdrawal record but not inside it:

DIVISION-PRESENCE CONDITION

The failed body pulsed once.

Vessel-kin continued. "When counting treaty obligations, do not force a harmed relation to identify as wound, splint, support, breach, consent, refusal, majority, or minority if its injury is the continued presence of more than one state."

The clerk entered slowly:

DIVISION-PRESENCE CONDITION: INVENTORY SHALL NOT FORCE A HARMED RELATION INTO A SINGLE FUNCTION WHEN ITS CURRENT TRUTH IS THE CONTINUED PRESENCE OF UNMERGED STATES.

Rusk said, "How do we act on that?"

Salt-Before-Shell turned, and Rusk lifted both hands before the strike arrived.

"I know. I am asking because action can harm. Not because I want the answer clean."

Salt-Before-Shell did not soften. "Still dangerous."

"Yes."

Oru-Kel pulsed from the boundary. "Action question allowed if it carries danger."

Lael said, "Then action can be limited: any obligation touching a division-presence body cannot be classified as wound or splint without preserving the division in the exported record."

Ren added:

ANY ACTION BASED ON DIVISION-PRESENCE MUST EXPORT THE DIVISION, NOT ONLY THE RESULT.

Keeps-Water-Calm's scarred shoulder shifted. "Beryl lacked this. Human file exported result."

The Pelagos memory made the sentence heavier than law could have made it.

Rusk looked at the inventory. "Care-passage success exported as relief. Route hazard exported as risk. Strategic understatement exported as conduct review. All of those could have eaten their divisions."

"Yes," Lael said.

"Then the withdrawal inventory needs export guards too."

Salt-Before-Shell's amber plates moved in irritated recognition. "Routeholder learns by being trapped with us."

"Apparently," Rusk said.

Ren opened a guard line under the side water:

WITHDRAWAL INVENTORY EXPORT GUARD: NO OBLIGATION MAY BE SUMMARIZED AS WOUND, SPLINT, ACTIVE, SUSPENDED, ACCEPTED, OR REFUSED WITHOUT ATTACHED DIVISION-PRESENCE NOTES WHERE A HARMED BODY OR RELATION HAS REQUESTED DIVISION REMAIN PRESENT.

The private route tooth brightened, then dimmed again when Oru-Kel pulsed the boundary rhythm against the guard. The tooth could use clean suspension. It could use clean continuity. It had less use for a record that carried division outward like grit in a gear.

Salt-Before-Shell looked at the cracked body.

"I do not withdraw the motion," he said.

The body pulsed.

"I pause my motion before your division," he continued. "Not before human fear."

Lael bowed her head. "Recorded."

"Do not make me generous."

"Recorded."

Ren wrote:

WITHDRAWAL MOTION PAUSED BY MOVANT IN RESPONSE TO DIVISION-PRESENCE REQUEST FROM FAILED BODY. PAUSE SHALL NOT BE CHARACTERIZED AS RESTORED TRUST, HUMAN PERSUASION, OR WITHDRAWAL OF WITHDRAWAL CURRENT.

The failed body settled by a fraction.

Not healed.

Present.

Then they stopped, because anything more would already be too much.

Chapter 28: The Body That Wants to Remain Divided

The cracked exchange body asked for no healer.

That was the first difficulty.

Vessel-kin held both hands above the care-passage basin, fingers spread in a posture Ren had learned meant available but not entering. The medical staff beyond the membrane waited for a summons that did not come. Lael's earlink glowed with urgent unanswered requests from the Compact assistant pool. Rusk's slate tried to update the risk clock and was refused by the chamber seal.

The body in the brace breathed in two rhythms.

One slow. One quick.

One carrying majority structure. One carrying minority warmth. The two did not merge. They also did not tear fully apart. The failure everyone had been treating as a damaged instrument had become a person, or persons, or a relation with voice enough to object to repair.

Ren did not know which grammar to use.

That ignorance saved them from writing too soon.

Third-Voice approached the brace with all three fans lowered. "What name may hold you?"

The cracked body shuddered.

"Do not hold."

Blue-white fan dimmed. "What call may reach you?"

The two rhythms crossed. The quick breath answered first; the slow breath followed with a pressure that altered the meaning.

"Here."

Ren felt the translation beads resist. Here was not a name. Here was not a party. Here could not be filed without context. The beads offered present witness, local remainder, unresolved body, then failed into silence.

Ren let the silence stand.

Salt-Before-Shell's limbs had tightened against his own body. "Here," he repeated, not as translation but as acknowledgment.

The cracked body pulsed.

Lael took one careful step closer. "Here, do you object to medical stabilization?"

Vessel-kin's eyes shifted toward her with something like warning.

The body answered, "Stabilize pain. Not position."

Lael absorbed that. "You consent to care that reduces suffering, but not care that resolves you into one vote."

The body made a sound that might have been assent if assent did not imply unity.

Ren wrote only after looking to Third-Voice, to Keeps-Water-Calm, and finally to Vessel-kin. No one stopped them.

HERE: CARE MAY STABILIZE PAIN; CARE MAY NOT RESOLVE POSITION.

The letters looked too straight.

Ren changed the label.

VOICE-PRESENT-AS-HERE: CARE MAY STABILIZE PAIN; CARE MAY NOT RESOLVE POSITION.

Still wrong, but less hungry.

Rusk whispered, "How can a vote remain operational if the body refuses resolution?"

Salt-Before-Shell turned so slowly that Rusk understood the mistake before the answer arrived.

"Not everything alive is operational."

Rusk closed his mouth.

Third-Voice's amber fan lifted toward the cracked body. "Withdrawal motion paused by Here. Does Here ask to enter motion?"

The slow rhythm pressed first this time.

"No."

The quick rhythm struck after it.

"Yes."

The brace rang softly.

Several Orison delegates moved back as if the contradiction had physical heat. Ren felt the human training inside them search for a method: separate the channels, assign provisional weights, mark one impaired, request clarification, obtain a deciding protocol. Every option was a hand reaching for the crack.

They kept their hands still.

Keeps-Water-Calm spoke from beside the basin. "Can Here ask both no and yes without being repaired?"

Third-Voice's green-black fan answered, "Parliament has no comfortable form."

"Comfort is not requirement."

Salt-Before-Shell said, "If Here enters motion as divided, withdrawal count cannot close."

Lael looked at him. "Would that be wrong?"

He did not answer at once.

Ren saw the cost of the question land in him. Salt-Before-Shell had called withdrawal because injury demanded it. Now injury itself refused to become usable for withdrawal. The motion could still proceed by overruling the cracked body, by calling it damaged, by treating its contradictory request as non-counting. That would be easy. That would also repeat the harm in another direction.

"It would be convenient," Salt-Before-Shell said finally.

No one mistook the answer for enough.

Vessel-kin lowered one hand into the care-passage water. "Pain rises."

The cracked body tightened.

Third-Voice asked, "Care?"

"Care," the body answered in both rhythms, and for one breath the two meant the same thing.

Vessel-kin entered the brace field with ritual slowness. The medical act that followed looked almost too small to matter: a pulse of mineral-dark fluid, a pressure adjustment along the left fracture, a cooling thread placed near the quick rhythm without touching the slow one. The body's pain signal reduced. Its division remained.

Ren watched more closely than they had watched any treaty lesson in their life.

Care could act without taking sides.

Not always.

Not automatically.

But here, in this basin, under these constraints, it did.

Lael watched too. Her face had gone still in the way it did when a policy assumption died and a better one had not yet arrived.

The cracked body spoke again.

"Humans ask for receiver."

Rusk's shoulders tightened. "Yes."

"Parliament asks for vote."

Third-Voice lowered all three fans. "Yes."

"Salt asks for leaving."

Salt-Before-Shell's mouth plates closed. "Yes."

"Here asks to remain crack."

The sentence did not translate into metaphor. It arrived as a structural demand.

Ren wrote:

HERE REQUESTS CONTINUING DIVISION AS ACTIVE WITNESS CONDITION.

Then they stopped again.

The body pulsed in pain at the word condition.

Ren deleted it.

HERE REQUESTS CONTINUING DIVISION AS ACTIVE WITNESS.

The pain dropped by a fraction.

Lael said softly, "If Here remains divided, no single signature can represent this part of the witness."

"Good," Keeps-Water-Calm said.

Rusk looked strained. "Then what can represent it?"

Oru-Kel brightened near the hidden tooth. "Maybe nothing. Maybe relation."

"My systems cannot receive relation."

Salt-Before-Shell answered, "Then your systems are not ready to touch us."

Rusk's frustration broke through. "And while we make them ready, the private instrument moves."

The tooth pulsed as if summoned by hunger for urgency.

Here's quick rhythm fluttered. The slow rhythm pushed against it, not to suppress but to remain beside it.

Third-Voice spoke sharply. "No one use hidden danger to force Here."

Rusk bowed his head. "Understood."

Ren believed he meant it. They also believed his systems did not.

Lael moved closer to the membrane separating dry command from wet witness. She did not cross it. Not yet. The membrane shimmered against her uniform sleeve, reading authorization, refusing category.

"If the problem is that human systems cannot receive relation," she said, "then a human office may need to enter relation instead of asking Parliament to become a receiver."

Every eye turned toward her.

Rusk said, "Lael, no."

The refusal came too fast and too personal.

Lael did not look back. "I am not proposing full embodiment."

Third-Voice's blue-white fan lifted. "Partial wet witness?"

"If Parliament permits. If Here does not object. If the role can be constrained so it cannot become a signature."

Rusk stepped forward. "Compact protocols do not allow an emergency officer to enter an alien witness role during active treaty dispute."

Lael finally looked at him. "Compact protocols also did not imagine a vote body requesting continued division while a private route instrument waits for our impatience."

"You could be disqualified."

"From what?"

He had no quick answer.

Ren saw the shape of it then. Lael had spent the day defending structures she did not fully trust because without them worse structures would rush in. Now she was considering stepping into a form that would damage her authority in order to keep authority from doing more damage.

Keeps-Water-Calm studied her with grave attention. "Partial wet witness does not make you Orison."

"I know."

"It does not make you safe."

"I know."

"It may teach your office that one human body can stand where relation should stand."

Lael flinched, but did not retreat. "Then constrain me."

Here's two rhythms moved through the brace.

"Constrain," the quick rhythm said.

"Witness," the slow rhythm said.

The words overlapped without becoming one.

Third-Voice lifted all three fans.

Blue-white: "Withdrawal motion remains paused."

Amber: "Here remains divided and present."

Green-black: "Lael Shun requests partial wet witness under constraint."

Salt-Before-Shell's limbs shifted with anger, fear, and something Ren did not want to call hope.

"If human enters wet witness," he said, "human cannot carry dry command inside and call it humility."

Lael unsealed the cuff of her uniform.

"Then take it from me before I cross."

No one moved.

That, more than refusal, showed the size of what she had offered. Human authority could be challenged, constrained, embarrassed, routed, corrected, suspended, reviewed, and cited. It was rarely handed over in a wet chamber before anyone knew what taking it would require.

Lael opened her command slate and placed it against the membrane.

"Compact emergency authority," she said. "Active filings, sanction response, care-passage notice maintenance, advocate conduct review, and communication with emergency office. I cannot surrender all of it without causing harm. I can shed operational command while inside partial wet witness. I can retain only passive receipt and emergency life-safety objection."

Rusk said, "That distinction will not hold in your office."

"Then we make the failure visible before it happens."

Ren opened a side pane, not formal yet.

Lael dictated:

COMMAND-SHEDDING DECLARATION / PARTIAL WET WITNESS REQUEST

During any partial wet witness, Advocate Lael Shun shall not issue Compact commands, accept treaty signatures, bind Parliament channels, receive routeholder technical authority, certify Orison consent, approve withdrawal status, or convert witness contact into legal representation. Retained functions are limited to passive receipt, personal witness, and emergency life-safety objection where immediate physical harm would otherwise occur.

Salt-Before-Shell scraped, "Emergency life-safety becomes hole."

"Yes," Lael said.

The speed of her agreement stopped him.

"Then narrow it," he said.

Lael added:

Emergency life-safety objection must name the body at risk, the immediate harm, the action requested, the cost to witness relation, and the review path after the emergency. It shall not be used to restore general command.

Keeps-Water-Calm's scarred shoulder shifted. "Better. Human command still has root."

"Yes."

"Root can grow back."

"Then cut it again if it does."

Third-Voice's green-black fan moved. "Who cuts?"

Lael looked at Here, not at Ren or Rusk. "Here may end the witness. Vessel-kin may end it for pain. Parliament boundary witness may end it for role spread. Compact record may end only by removing my authority, not by converting wet witness into dry command."

Rusk stared. "You are giving an alien body authority to end your operational role."

Lael did not look away from Here. "I am asking the body harmed by operational hunger to police my role inside its presence."

Here's quick rhythm flared.

"Not police," it said.

The slow rhythm followed.

"End."

Lael bowed her head. "End, then."

Ren changed the line:

Here may end the witness. Vessel-kin may end it for pain. Parliament boundary witness may end it for role spread. Compact record may end only by removing Shun's external authority, not by converting wet witness into dry command.

The pain signal did not rise.

Holt spoke from the technical station, voice low. "I need to isolate her channels. If she crosses with an active command slate, the office may continue logging her as available authority."

"Do it," Lael said.

"I need your authorization."

"You have it."

"No," Salt-Before-Shell said. "That is human granting human cut."

Holt froze.

Ren felt the room waiting for the old path.

Lael removed the slate from the membrane and placed it on the floor of the dry gallery, outside her reach.

"Then I authorize nothing further," she said. "Holt reports what he can cut without my new command."

Holt checked the station. "I can sever auto-forwarding, mute outbound command prompts, and mark all emergency office contact as delayed passive copy. I cannot revoke her identity token without her active authorization."

Rusk said, "I can witness that any use of the token while she is inside wet witness is invalid for routeholder reliance."

Lael glanced back, surprised.

He shrugged, badly. "I learn eventually too."

Ren wrote:

IDENTITY TOKEN REMAINS TECHNICALLY ACTIVE BUT OPERATIONALLY CONTESTED. ROUTEHOLDER RELIANCE WAIVED. COMPACT COMMAND OUTPUT MUTED. OUTBOUND OFFICE CONTACT DELAYED PASSIVE COPY ONLY. TOKEN USE DURING WET WITNESS SHALL TRIGGER ROLE-SPREAD REVIEW.

Third-Voice lowered all three fans toward Here.

"Does Here permit partial wet witness under these constraints?"

The two rhythms did not answer together.

The quick rhythm said, "Fear."

The slow rhythm said, "Need."

The brace held both.

Vessel-kin translated with care. "Here does not consent as one. Here permits approach if fear remains recorded beside need."

Lael's face changed.

Ren added:

APPROACH PERMITTED UNDER DIVISION-PRESENCE: FEAR AND NEED BOTH RECORDED; NEITHER CONTROLS THE OTHER.

Salt-Before-Shell moved aside by one body length.

Not invitation.

Not approval.

Space.

Lael touched the membrane with her bare wrist.

It opened only enough for water to take her hand.

Chapter 29: Lael Crosses the Membrane

No one moved to take Lael's authority.

That was the second lesson.

Human command could be removed by order, suspension, resignation, arrest, or failure. None of those had meaning in the chamber's wet law. The cuff seal hanging open at Lael's wrist was not enough. The Compact insignia on her collar was not enough. Her willingness was not enough.

Third-Voice circled her once, three fans reading the dry symbols she had carried into brine.

Blue-white: "She offers command."

Amber: "Command is not a shell that lifts clean."

Green-black: "Command clings by those who answer it."

Rusk stood rigid. "I do not consent to this."

Salt-Before-Shell turned. "Good. Then command clings."

Lael looked at Rusk. "Aven."

He did not answer as coalition officer first. That frightened Ren more than the refusal had.

"You cannot become their instrument," he said.

"I am already someone's instrument," Lael replied. "That is the problem."

"You are the Compact's emergency interpreter."

"Exactly."

"If you cross under Orison constraint, every message you send after this can be challenged."

"Then challenge it."

His face tightened. "That is easy to say before tribunals take years of your life."

Lael's expression softened in a way the chamber probably could not read. "Aven, this is not courage. It is arithmetic. If I stay outside relation, I keep clean authority and ask injured bodies to become administrable. If I cross badly, I become another example of human occupation by humility. If I cross under constraint and everyone sees the constraint, maybe one human office learns a little less harm."

"Maybe."

"Yes."

Rusk looked away first.

Ren saw then that taking command from Lael required more than Lael's consent. It required those accustomed to obeying her to stop making her central. Rusk had to stop treating her as the person who could save the routeholder offer. Ren had to stop looking to her pane for procedural rescue. The Compact assistants beyond the membrane had to stop routing every urgent query through her name.

Lael touched her earlink.

"External command pool, record this statement. I am entering partial wet witness under Salt Parliament constraint. I do not carry Compact authorization into that role. Do not treat any sensory, relational, or embodied output from me as directive, signature, consent, waiver, or emergency order. Maintain dry chain under Deputy Haro until I exit or am removed."

Her earlink erupted with voices.

She removed it and placed it in the basin.

The device died with a small human click.

The chamber listened to the absence afterward.

Third-Voice's amber fan lifted. "Better."

Lael took off the collar insignia next. She held it out.

No Orison accepted it.

Ren understood a beat late. If an Orison body took it, the act might become custody, trophy, proof, insult, or claim. Lael understood too. She set the insignia on the dry side of the membrane, not hidden, not carried.

Rusk whispered, "Lael."

She did not look back this time.

Keeps-Water-Calm approached with a shallow bowl of dark mineral water. "Constraint begins before crossing."

"State it," Lael said.

"You may witness relation. You may not receive treaty consent. You may feel pressure. You may not convert pressure into signature. You may speak pain if pain permits. You may not own pain because it passed through you. You may withdraw if your body fails. You may not withdraw and call the remaining relation closed."

Lael repeated each sentence.

The repetition changed nothing legally.

It changed the water.

Vessel-kin added, "Care boundary: we stabilize your body. We do not stabilize your authority."

Lael repeated that too.

Salt-Before-Shell came last. He held no bowl. He offered no ceremony. "If you use wet witness to soften withdrawal, I will name it."

"Yes."

"If you use wet witness to make yourself necessary, I will name it."

"Yes."

"If you suffer and expect gratitude, I will not give it."

Lael breathed once. "Yes."

Here pulsed from the cracked brace.

"Do not become one for us."

Lael's face changed. "I won't."

Third-Voice corrected her.

Blue-white: "Say cannot."

Lael swallowed. "I cannot become one for you."

The quick rhythm steadied. The slow rhythm remained beside it.

Ren had not realized how much of human promise depended on pretending ability was virtue. I will not harm you. I will not erase you. I will not misuse the role. Better, the chamber insisted, to say what structure prevented and what it did not. Better to admit incapacity than to sell restraint as goodness.

The membrane opened.

It did not slide aside. It accepted a narrow vertical line through itself, no wider than Lael's shoulders. Brine thickened around the opening. Beyond it, the wet witness field shimmered with currents too fine for Ren's eyes to hold.

Lael stepped through.

Her first breath failed.

Rusk moved.

Ren moved too.

Vessel-kin moved faster than both, one hand raised, stopping them without touching them. Lael bent forward in the witness field, hands open, mouth working against air that was no longer merely air. The membrane had not drowned her. It had made breathing relational. Her lungs were still human. The field required her body to feel currents she could not command and not immediately translate them into panic.

Keeps-Water-Calm said, "Do not rescue discomfort from teaching."

Rusk's voice broke. "She is choking."

"She is learning boundary."

Lael lifted one hand, not to ask for help but to refuse premature rescue. Her second breath came ragged. Her third found a rhythm.

The witness field touched her skin.

Ren saw the moment it found the places where authority had lived. Not metaphorically. The field brightened at her throat, wrist, ear, and sternum: voice channel, command cuff, dead earlink mark, oath implant under bone. Each point flared and then dimmed as the chamber named it not available.

Lael made a small sound.

Not pain exactly.

Recognition.

"I thought signatures failed because they were too thin," she said.

Third-Voice's green-black fan angled toward her. "And now?"

Lael's eyes were wet, though whether from the field or from herself Ren could not tell. "They also fail because they ask the wrong body to be enough."

The chamber did not approve. It received.

Rusk looked at the hidden route tooth. "Can she receive the technical packet?"

Every fan, limb, and eye in the chamber turned toward him.

He knew before anyone answered. "Wrong question."

Salt-Before-Shell said, "At least routeholder learns fast when embarrassed."

Under other conditions, someone might have laughed.

Lael steadied inside the field. "I cannot receive for Parliament. I can witness where Compact demand touches relation and name the touch as touch, not consent."

Keeps-Water-Calm said, "That may be something."

Here spoke from the brace. "Does wet human feel division?"

Lael closed her eyes.

The witness field brightened along her left side, then split into two faint currents that did not reconcile. She swayed. Vessel-kin lifted a hand, ready.

"I feel the demand to choose which current is real," Lael said.

Here pulsed.

"Do not."

"I am trying not to."

Third-Voice corrected again.

Amber fan: "Try is human drama."

Lael opened her eyes with something like irritation, which meant she was still herself. "I am constrained from choosing which current is real."

Here settled.

Ren wrote:

PARTIAL WET WITNESS ESTABLISHED: LAEL SHUN. NO SIGNATURE CAPACITY. NO CONSENT RECEIPT. MAY WITNESS COMPACT TOUCH AS TOUCH ONLY.

They paused, then added:

SIGNATURE FAILURE: WRONG BODY ASKED TO BE ENOUGH.

The chamber seal deepened.

At first Ren thought the membrane was rejecting the record. Then every outer door in the Salt Parliament answered with a low, resonant closure.

One after another.

Care-passage doors.

Routeholder access doors.

Human observation doors.

Dry command doors.

The entire chamber locked itself around the unresolved motion, the divided witness, the partial wet human, and the hidden tooth.

Rusk's slate flashed red.

Lael turned inside the witness field, slow and pale.

Third-Voice spoke with all three fans.

"Parliament has sealed deliberation."

The human systems panicked in sequence.

Rusk's slate tried to classify the door closures as hostile containment. Holt's station raised a facility lockdown warning. The dead earlink in the basin, impossible as it should have been, produced one final emergency ping as the outer command pool lost live access to Lael's identity token. The dry observation glass fogged with pressure seals. Somewhere beyond the chamber, human security protocols would be asking whether the Salt Parliament had taken hostages, whether the Compact advocate had been seized, whether routeholder personnel were being detained, whether the medical transfer had been a prelude to coercion.

All of those questions wanted the same answer.

Ren reached for the local-first gate before the clean wrong sentence could leave.

Lael saw them and lifted one hand from inside the wet witness field. Not command. Warning.

"Do not make me source," she said.

Ren stopped.

She was right. If the first anti-panic statement came from Lael, even under constraint, outside systems would treat her as active authority because panic preferred familiar names.

Rusk looked at the red slate. "My systems need a status."

Salt-Before-Shell said, "Your systems hunger."

"Yes," Rusk said. "And if not fed carefully, they will bite."

Third-Voice's green-black fan moved toward the record. "Status from chamber, not wet human."

The clerk looked at Ren.

Ren looked at Third-Voice.

Third-Voice dictated:

SEALED DELIBERATION STATUS / NOT HOSTILE CONTAINMENT

Parliament doors sealed by internal deliberative procedure after recognition of unresolved withdrawal motion, division-presence witness, partial wet witness under command-shedding constraint, and active private route pressure. Sealing is not consent, capture, hostage-taking, route closure, medical breach, or Compact command failure. External systems shall not use seal status to trigger enforcement, sanction, route escalation, or emergency extraction without independent life-safety evidence.

Holt said, "Add human life-safety channel."

Salt-Before-Shell's limbs lifted.

Holt did not retreat. "Not extraction. Status. If we do not provide a life-safety channel, security systems will invent one."

Keeps-Water-Calm said, "Useful fear."

Lael's breath had steadied but remained costly. She did not speak.

Ren added only after Third-Voice's blue-white fan inclined:

Human and Orison life-safety status will be reported at fixed intervals by mixed noncommand witness: Vessel-kin for body condition, Holt for facility pressure and atmosphere, clerk for dry chamber human status. Lael Shun shall not serve as life-safety certifier while inside partial wet witness.

Rusk read it. "I need my own status listed. Otherwise my office will assume I am blocked from speaking."

Salt-Before-Shell said, "Are you?"

Rusk looked at the sealed routeholder access door. "Physically, yes. Politically, less than I deserve."

That was either honest or exhaustion so complete it had become useful.

Third-Voice allowed:

Routeholder witness Aven Rusk physically present, not held as party, not authorized to issue demands through seal status. May report personal body status through fixed interval channel. May not use seal to renew socket offer or demand route access.

Rusk nodded. "Accepted."

The private tooth brightened behind the diagram.

Oru-Kel pulsed dark. "Tooth likes locked room."

Ren saw why. Outside systems would read seal as risk. Risk would feed bypass. Bypass would feed the tooth. Every procedure could become a meal if exported cleanly enough.

They added:

SEALED DELIBERATION SHALL NOT BE PRICED AS ROUTE FAILURE WITHOUT INDEPENDENT NAVIGATIONAL EVIDENCE. PREMIUM, BYPASS, ESCORT, OR GRAY-POOL ACTIVITY BASED SOLELY ON SEAL STATUS SHALL BE RECORDED AS SPECULATIVE PRESSURE AGAINST PARLIAMENT DELIBERATION.

Rusk's mouth tightened. "Underwriters will hate that."

"Good," Lael whispered from the field, then closed her eyes as if even that small satisfaction had weight.

Salt-Before-Shell turned toward her. "Wet human still comments."

Lael opened her eyes. "Personal lapse. Not command."

Here's quick rhythm flickered.

The slow rhythm answered.

"Recorded as lapse," Vessel-kin translated.

Ren entered:

WET WITNESS COMMENT: PERSONAL LAPSE / NOT COMMAND / NOT STATUS.

Lael's face flushed, but she did not object.

The first external query struck the seal.

COMPACT EMERGENCY OFFICE: CONFIRM ADVOCATE SHUN STATUS.

The chamber did not send Lael.

The mixed noncommand witness sent:

Alive. Breathing under partial wet witness constraint. No command capacity. No extraction request. Next interval in three minutes unless life-safety threshold changes.

The second query came from Rusk's coalition:

ROUTEHOLDER BOARD: IS ACCESS DENIED?

Rusk looked at Third-Voice.

Third-Voice answered through the record:

Physical access sealed by Parliament deliberation. Routeholder witness present. No routeholder party status granted. No technical packet demand accepted or refused during seal. Await fixed interval status.

The third query did not name itself.

It was a market probe against the hidden route tooth, asking price without asking permission.

Oru-Kel darkened the probe, and the chamber recorded it:

UNATTRIBUTED SPECULATIVE QUERY RECEIVED WITHIN ONE MINUTE OF SEAL STATUS. TREAT AS PRESSURE, NOT INFORMATION.

The tooth dimmed again.

Not because hunger had vanished.

Because the room had named its mouth.

Ren looked at the doors, then at the record, then at the people and bodies trapped together by a procedure no human system had authorized.

Chapter by chapter, the room had been removing exits.

Now it had removed the literal ones.

Chapter 30: The Parliament Locks Its Doors

The first human reaction was inventory of escape.

Ren hated that they did it too.

Their eyes moved to the nearest membrane seam, then to the care-passage hatch, then to the dry observation gallery where Deputy Haro and two Compact technicians were now shapes behind sealed glass. Rusk checked his routeholder slate. Lael, inside the wet witness field, looked toward the place her dead earlink lay in the basin. Even Vela-Short, who had been quiet enough to become furniture in human minds, shifted her weight toward the maintenance conduit behind the translation rack.

The chamber noticed.

Third-Voice's blue-white fan opened. "No exit counted as first answer."

Ren flushed.

Salt-Before-Shell said, "Human bodies teach truth before human mouths."

"Or fear," Ren said.

"Fear is truth with fewer decorations."

The sealed doors did not look aggressive. That made them worse. No blast shutters had dropped. No alarms sounded. The membranes simply refused passage. The care-passage doors remained translucent. The dry command doors still showed the corridor beyond. The routeholder access lock displayed its own reflection with bureaucratic politeness.

Rusk's slate chimed once.

ACCESS DENIED: DELIBERATION SEAL ACTIVE.

He turned it toward Lael by reflex, then remembered she could not receive command.

That small aborted motion did more than any speech to prove the necessity of the seal.

Third-Voice addressed the human record. "Parliament seal is not imprisonment in human criminal sense. It is pressure boundary. No outside command, no market timing, no procedural flight, no emergency override until withdrawal motion, Here witness, partial wet witness, and routeholder hazard are held in one unresolved room."

Rusk said, "How long?"

Amber fan: "Wrong measure."

"We have convoy traffic outside the Shoals."

Green-black fan: "That may become right concern. Not yet right weapon."

Rusk clenched his jaw. "I am not weaponizing it."

Lael spoke from the witness field before anyone else could. Her voice had changed. It still carried her, but the edges of the words were dampened by currents she could not own.

"You are reaching for it."

Rusk turned to her. "You can feel that?"

"I can feel Compact demand touching relation. I can feel routeholder demand when it tries to borrow emergency."

He looked wounded.

Lael closed her eyes briefly. "Aven, I am not accusing your motive. I am naming the touch."

Ren wrote:

SEAL FUNCTION: PREVENTS OUTSIDE PRESSURE FROM BECOMING ARGUMENT BEFORE RELATION IS NAMED.

The chamber accepted that line without pain.

Progress, maybe.

Vela-Short cleared her throat. "Practical question from someone who very much enjoys breathing and leaving eventually. What happens if the sealed room has a medical emergency?"

Vessel-kin answered, "Care enters. Command does not."

"Who decides the difference?"

Vessel-kin looked at Here.

The cracked exchange body pulsed in two rhythms. "Pain calls care. Fear calls many things."

Vela-Short nodded slowly. "Deeply inconvenient, but clear."

The dry command gallery flickered. Deputy Haro appeared on the inner glass with a written placard because audio had been cut:

STATUS? NEED CONFIRMATION LAEL ALIVE.

Lael turned toward the glass.

The witness field brightened around her throat and then dimmed.

"I cannot answer as command," she said.

Ren said, "Can I?"

Third-Voice considered. "You are recorder, not sealed witness."

Salt-Before-Shell snapped, "Human recorder still human."

"Yes," Ren said before Third-Voice could answer. "So constrain the reply."

Keeps-Water-Calm moved closer to the glass. "State what is observed, not what it authorizes."

Ren drafted on a plain display, visible to the chamber:

OBSERVED: LAEL SHUN IS ALIVE, CONSCIOUS, AND UNDER PARTIAL WET WITNESS CARE BOUNDARY. NO COMPACT DIRECTIVE ISSUED FROM THIS OBSERVATION. DELIBERATION SEAL ACTIVE.

They looked to Lael. "Does that make you into proof for them?"

Lael read it twice. "Less than silence would."

Here's quick rhythm fluttered.

"Alive is not enough."

Ren added:

ALIVE DOES NOT MEAN UNHARMED, AUTHORIZED, AVAILABLE, OR CONSENTING.

The slow rhythm settled.

Deputy Haro's face changed when the message appeared on the glass. He looked relieved first, then angry, then disciplined enough to write:

ACKNOWLEDGED. DRY CHAIN HOLDS.

Lael let out a breath that shook.

Rusk watched her breathe and did not speak. For once, that was the useful thing.

The silence that followed was not empty enough to be peace.

It had registers.

The low register was chamber infrastructure: salt pumps easing their stroke, membrane ribs tightening by increments too small for human engineering displays to dignify, witness pools changing temperature in bands that did not appear on Ren's skin but did appear in the way Here held itself. The middle register was bodies pretending not to count time. Rusk's thumb hovered near a slate he could not use. Vela-Short rotated one shoulder twice and then stopped because the motion had become a visible wish to move. Lael kept her hands open inside the wet witness field, palms turned toward the water, as if closed fingers would be mistaken for a claim.

The high register was the room learning what the lock had removed.

No one outside could tell them how the delay looked from trade boards. No legal assistant could offer a sentence that converted uncertainty into risk-managed style. No corridor aide could whisper that a senator, captain, shareholder, survivor, or courier had a personal stake. Even the untranslated murmurs from side channels had gone absent.

Ren had hated those channels for most of the hearing.

They missed them now with embarrassing force.

Third-Voice lifted a pale fan. "Human recorder shows withdrawal symptom."

Ren's first answer was too sharp. "From what?"

"From permission to believe noise is context."

They looked down at their pane. The pane did not update itself with institutional weather. It only waited for them to write what the bodies in the room were actually doing.

Ren wrote:

SEAL SIDE EFFECT: REMOVES CONTEXT-FEEDS THAT WOULD OTHERWISE LET PARTICIPANTS BORROW ABSENT URGENCY.

Salt-Before-Shell clicked once. "Too gentle. Borrow is a soft theft."

Ren changed it.

SEAL SIDE EFFECT: REMOVES CONTEXT-FEEDS THAT WOULD OTHERWISE LET PARTICIPANTS STEAL ABSENT URGENCY AND WEAR IT AS NECESSITY.

The chamber accepted the revision with a slight warming of the nearest pool.

Rusk said, "That sentence will be used against us."

"It should be," Ren said.

He looked at them, and for a moment the routeholder did not answer as a routeholder. "Against all of us?"

Ren wanted the clean mercy of saying yes. The room would have liked that. The record would have looked balanced.

They did not give it.

"Against whoever benefits from being able to make absence speak first."

Rusk absorbed that and looked at the dead slate again. "Then I need to know what I am allowed to do while locked in a room with a hazard I helped bring."

The amber fan that opened over Third-Voice was narrow, not warning but attention.

Rusk set the slate on the floor between himself and the diagram of the hidden tooth. The gesture was awkward because human floors were not Orison basins and slates were not offerings. It still changed the room.

"I will not send. I will not query. I will not request authority from dry command. I will not ask Lael to certify anything. I will not ask Ren to carry routeholder need under recorder privilege." He swallowed. "I would like to list the pressure channels from memory and mark which ones I cannot verify without outside systems."

Vela-Short breathed out. "That is either useful or the prettiest trap I have heard today."

"Yes," Rusk said.

The answer helped more than denial would have.

Keeps-Water-Calm turned one iris toward Here. "Can a sealed participant make inventory of pressure without making pressure?"

Here's slow rhythm answered first. "Inventory can be care if it does not hurry the wound."

The quick rhythm cut across it. "Inventory can be hunger if it counts what can be eaten."

Lael's wet witness field darkened around her wrists.

"Then make him write the hunger too," she said.

Everyone looked at her. The field brightened at the attention, and Lael did not flinch this time.

"If he names a channel, he names how it would tempt him. Not just what it does. What it promises him. What it promises the Compact. What it promises the people outside who need passage. Otherwise the inventory becomes another clean diagram."

Rusk closed his eyes.

Ren expected refusal, or at least the tired routeholder version of refusal where a man conceded principle and defended implementation until the principle died.

Instead he said, "Agreed."

Ren wrote a new heading:

PRESSURE-CHANNEL INVENTORY UNDER SEAL: EACH CHANNEL MUST NAME FUNCTION, ABSENT VERIFICATION, BENEFICIARY, TEMPTATION, AND POSSIBLE HARM IF TREATED AS NECESSITY.

Third-Voice added, "Also what body pays first."

Ren added it.

Rusk took an unnetworked wax stylus from the emergency record kit. He had to ask Vela-Short for paper. The fact that the richest navigation consortium in the room had been reduced to borrowing a mechanic's folded maintenance sheets carried an ugly satisfaction Ren did not trust.

Rusk wrote slowly.

The first channel was obvious: live route-risk timing.

Function: report probability of passage loss or delay.

Absent verification: current gate drift, convoy position, weather in the meridian fold, maintenance state of the Shoals edge buoys.

Beneficiary: routeholders, insurers, convoy captains, medical recipients, anyone spared delay, anyone paid to price delay.

Temptation: make time look like command.

Possible harm if treated as necessity: override witness, compress Orison deliberation, convert care into ransom.

Body that pays first: bodies needing cold-chain medicine; bodies asked to disappear from the route map so those medicines move.

He stopped there.

The room did not praise him.
