Rusk looked at her with a kind of exhausted gratitude and did not let the gratitude become an appeal. "It can."

He drafted on the dark slate, local only:

CONVOY FACT MARKER: COLD-CHAIN STATUS AND TRANSIT STATUS ONLY. SUCCESSFUL OR CONTINUING TRANSIT DOES NOT PROVE PARLIAMENT BENEVOLENCE, TREATY STABILITY, ROUTE SAFETY, OR FALSEHOOD OF ALL OTHER HARMS. IT ONLY CONTRADICTS CLAIM THAT MEDICAL CONVOY WAS BLOCKED AT THIS MARKER.

Salt-Before-Shell moved closer. "Too clean at end. At this marker becomes door for next marker."

Rusk revised:

IT ONLY CONTRADICTS THE SPECIFIC CLAIM THAT THIS MEDICAL CONVOY WAS BLOCKED BY THE PARLIAMENT AT THE RECORDED TIME.

Here's quick rhythm pulsed once.

Slow rhythm followed.

Ren wrote:

COUNTER-SIGNAL LIMIT: VERIFIED CONVOY FACT MAY CONTRADICT A SPECIFIC BLOCKADE CLAIM BUT MAY NOT BE USED AS PROOF OF GENERAL TRUST, FULL SAFETY, OR RESOLVED HARM.

The chamber accepted that line, but the acceptance came with pressure. They were asking the sickly little green trace to run against a red flood while carrying disclaimers tied to its ankles.

Rusk sent the limited fact marker to his risk office.

The response came back in two colors.

GREEN: FACT MARKER RECEIVED.

RED: LIMIT LANGUAGE REDUCES MARKET UTILITY.

Vela-Short laughed again. "It complains because truth is shaped wrong for profit."

Rusk did not smile. "Yes."

He appended:

MARKET UTILITY IS NOT THE ONLY VALID MEASURE OF EMERGENCY TRUTH.

The red system did not know where to put that.

For three seconds, neither did the room.

Oru-Kel brightened sharply near the tooth.

"Careful," they said.

Rusk froze. "What?"

Oru-Kel did not answer in human cadence. Their body pulsed toward the tooth, then toward the relay metrics, then toward the chamber's old dark where the Pale Arc warning had first been felt.

Ren felt the temperature of the room drop.

Third-Voice's blue-white fan rose. Amber followed. Green-black flickered weakly, but it flickered.

Oru-Kel said, "Same shape."

Lael turned inside the witness field. "Same as what?"

"Older warning."

The private tooth flared in response, and the flare did something it had not done before. It bent. Not toward Rusk. Not toward the market lines. Toward the boundary rhythm Oru-Kel had shown in darkness.

Pale Arc.

Ren did not write yet.

Oru-Kel moved slowly, as if any speed would teach the wrong lesson. "Relays make simplification. Market eats simplification. Private tooth grows through simplification. Pale Arc warning also touched simplification."

Rusk said, "The Pale Arc is not a political actor."

Oru-Kel's limbs darkened. "You still ask actor. Wrong hunger."

Keeps-Water-Calm said, "Pattern, not party."

"Yes."

Ren looked at the red metrics again. The distortion reduced the chamber to one danger. The market priced the one danger. The price forced route decisions. The route decisions would prove instability. The proof would simplify more. A loop. Dock Seven again, but faster and larger. A mirror refusal pattern running through finance, route law, public fear, and the private instrument.

The Pale Arc warning had not sent a message. It had touched relation where simplification made passage through what had not consented to become passable.

Ren's skin prickled.

"The warning is about conditions that make boundary violation easy," they said.

Oru-Kel brightened.

Not approval.

Recognition.

The relay glass flashed:

ORISON ROUTE RISK: +22%.

CARE-PASSAGE INSURANCE SUSPENSION: INITIATED IN THREE POOLS.

CONVOY STATUS: DOCK SEVEN CURRENT STRESS RISING.

Lael took a step inside the wet witness field and almost fell. Vessel-kin moved close but did not touch.

"If the market forces carriers away," she said, "the Shoals become more dependent on private channels."

Rusk said, "Yes."

"Including the tooth."

"Yes."

Salt-Before-Shell's voice lowered. "So public fear sells the hidden bite as rescue."

Rusk looked at the private tooth. "Yes."

Here's slow rhythm pressed hard enough that the brace hummed.

"Do not use us to prove old warning."

Oru-Kel turned toward Here. "No. Here is not evidence. Here is harmed by same water."

The distinction mattered. Ren saw the chamber receive it.

They wrote:

RELAY DISTORTION, MARKET REPRICING, PRIVATE ROUTE TOOTH, DOCK SEVEN MIRROR, AND PALE ARC WARNING SHOW RELATED PATTERN: SIMPLIFICATION CREATES PASSABLE VIOLATION. HERE IS NOT PROOF OF PATTERN; HERE IS HARMED WITHIN IT.

The room held the line.

The private tooth dimmed by a degree.

Rusk whispered, "What do we do with that?"

Oru-Kel looked toward the older dark beyond the chamber lights.

"Name warning older than politics."

Salt-Before-Shell said, "Will naming stop market?"

"No."

"Will it stop tooth?"

"Not alone."

"Then why?"

Oru-Kel's body became almost black.

"Because if humans think this is only scandal, they will answer with cleaner scandal. If Orison thinks this is only human malice, we answer with cleaner leaving. Both feed bite."

No one moved.

The relay glass flashed again.

ORISON ROUTE RISK: +24%.

One point below the automatic carrier suspension threshold.

The chamber had almost no time left to learn the older warning correctly.

Chapter 37: Oru-Kel Names the Older Warning

Oru-Kel asked for darkness again.

This time no one mistook it for privacy.

The chamber lights lowered in layers. Human screens dimmed to emergency red. The relay metrics remained visible, but softened, as if the room had put them behind water instead of glass. Lael's wet witness field became a pale outline around her body. Rusk's face lost its market color. Salt-Before-Shell's limbs turned into angles against the basin glow. Third-Voice's blue-white and amber fans held enough light for orientation; green-black was a faint line, present because absence had become dangerous to hide.

Oru-Kel darkened until they were almost indistinguishable from the old water.

"Warning older than politics," they said, "does not mean warning outside politics."

Ren did not write yet.

Oru-Kel approved by not stopping.

"Pale Arc touches boundary where relation made too simple to resist passage. Human route tooth does this. Market story does this. Compact clean party does this. Orison leaving can do this if leaving makes one wound speak for all wounds."

Salt-Before-Shell's posture sharpened.

Oru-Kel turned toward him before he could answer. "Not accusation. Warning."

"Warning can still choose target."

"Yes. This warning chooses shape."

The relay glass flashed in dim red:

ORISON ROUTE RISK: +24.4%.

No one moved toward it.

That restraint felt like holding a door shut against wind.

Keeps-Water-Calm said, "Name the shape."

Oru-Kel's body pulsed once, so dark that Ren saw the pulse as absence moving.

"Passable violation."

The translation beads, still cooled from the untranslated session, tried to wake around Ren's collar. They offered trespass vector, consent bypass, boundary breach, then fell quiet. Passable violation stayed because no cleaner phrase could carry the dirt.

Oru-Kel continued, "Passable violation begins when a relation is made into path by reducing what can object."

Here pulsed in the brace.

Quick rhythm: "Reducing."

Slow rhythm: "Object."

Oru-Kel faced Here. "Here objects by remaining divided. Reduction says: become one or become unusable. That is passable violation."

The cracked body steadied.

Oru-Kel turned to Rusk. "Routeholder tooth says: become receiver or warning cannot bind. Then receiver becomes path. Passable violation."

Rusk nodded once.

Not enough. True enough to continue.

Oru-Kel turned to Lael. "Compact clean party says: become stable party or protection cannot attach. Then stability becomes path. Passable violation."

Lael flinched as if the field had touched bone.

It had.

Oru-Kel turned to Salt-Before-Shell. "Withdrawal says: become injured people leaving humans or injury remains trapped. Then injury becomes path. Passable violation can wear freedom."

Salt-Before-Shell's limbs curled inward.

Ren had seen him angry, contemptuous, wounded, strategic. This was different. Oru-Kel had named a danger inside the only motion he had left to trust. He did not reject it quickly. That made him brave in a way Ren had not expected.

"So no path," he said.

"No," Oru-Kel answered. "Care-passage still path. Storm-egg still path. Withdrawal may be path. Treaty may be path. Path not wrong. Path made by reduction is warning."

Ren felt the sentence settle into their skin.

Path not wrong.

Reduction warning.

They opened the record pane.

This time Oru-Kel watched and allowed.

Ren wrote:

OLDER WARNING NAMED BY ORU-KEL: PASSABLE VIOLATION.

They paused.

The room did not flinch.

They continued:

Definition held in chamber: passable violation begins when a relation is reduced into a usable path by narrowing what may object, refuse, remain divided, remain untranslated, or remain unowned. Pale Arc boundary rhythm, private route tooth, market simplification, Dock Seven mirror, stable-party demand, and withdrawal pressure are related by shape, not by identical actor.

Oru-Kel moved closer to the pane and darkened one edge beside the definition.

"Add: not metaphor."

Ren's fingers stilled.

"Humans will make metaphor when machine not found," Oru-Kel said. "Orison will make spirit when metal not found. Both wrong enough."

Rusk said, "You think the pattern has operational consequences."

Oru-Kel faced him. "Think smaller. Pattern is already operation."

They turned toward the relay glass. The red metrics pulsed in their softened layer, each number a decision pretending to be a condition.

"Risk number reduces chamber to one danger. Carrier rule reduces one danger to one action. Suspension reduces action to need for alternate path. Alternate path makes private tooth useful. Private tooth requires receiver. Receiver narrows relation. Narrowed relation becomes route. Route crosses boundary. Passable violation."

No one spoke for several seconds.

Ren wrote as fast as they dared:

OPERATIONAL CHAIN: RISK NUMBER REDUCES CHAMBER TO ONE DANGER; CARRIER RULE REDUCES DANGER TO SUSPENSION; SUSPENSION CREATES NEED FOR ALTERNATE PATH; ALTERNATE PATH MAKES PRIVATE TOOTH USEFUL; PRIVATE TOOTH REQUIRES RECEIVER; RECEIVER NARROWS RELATION INTO ROUTE.

The private tooth pulsed against the line.

Oru-Kel dimmed it with absence rather than force.

Lael whispered, "That is why the clean line feels like rescue."

"Yes," Oru-Kel said.

Rusk looked at the chain, not defending, not yet able to accept the whole of it. "Stable-party certification interrupts the chain before suspension."

"It changes tooth's meal," Oru-Kel said.

"How?"

"Instead of alternate path requiring receiver, receiver already prepared."

Rusk went still.

Ren understood at the same time he did. A stable-party line would not simply reassure carriers. It would create the administrative socket the hidden instrument needed: a legible Orison receiver, accountable enough for human protection, narrow enough for route attachment, clean enough for markets, and too urgent to contest while the threshold burned.

They added:

STABLE-PARTY CERTIFICATION MAY INTERRUPT CARRIER SUSPENSION WHILE PREPARING THE RECEIVER SOCKET REQUIRED BY THE PRIVATE ROUTE TOOTH. THIS IS NOT SAFETY WITHOUT COST.

Lael closed her eyes.

"Say worse," Salt-Before-Shell said.

Ren did not know whether he meant the record or Lael.

Oru-Kel answered for both. "Clean rescue can pre-install violation."

Ren wrote it exactly.

The chamber accepted the ugliness.

The relay glass ticked:

ORISON ROUTE RISK: +24.7%.

Rusk hissed through his teeth.

Lael spoke before he did. "If we answer this with stable-party certification, we make the warning true."

The wet witness field brightened around her sternum and then dimmed.

It allowed the sentence.

Rusk looked at her. "Stable-party certification is the fastest way to stop automatic suspension."

"Yes."

"It tells carriers Parliament has an accountable treaty receiver."

"Yes."

"It cuts risk."

"It cuts by making one throat."

Salt-Before-Shell said nothing.

That was how Ren knew the blade had reached him too.

Deputy Haro appeared behind the outer glass with another placard:

COMPACT PRESS OFFICE AGAIN REQUESTS STABLE-PARTY LINE. RISK NEAR THRESHOLD.

Lael read it and closed her eyes.

The chamber waited.

Rusk said, very softly, "Lael, if the threshold crosses, carriers suspend. If carriers suspend, medicine, food-chain additives, hatchery minerals, and legal observers all reroute or stop. Private channels will bloom."

"I know."

"The clean line prevents that."

"The clean line becomes infrastructure."

"Maybe temporarily."

"Temporary sockets teach permanent hands."

Keeps-Water-Calm's scar darkened at that.

Rusk looked away.

Oru-Kel said, "Stable-party line may stop one fire by laying fuel under next water."

Lael's hands opened inside the wet witness field. "Then I have to burn the clause."

Rusk's head snapped up. "No."

"Yes."

"That clause is the basis of Compact emergency recognition."

"It is the basis of passable violation."

"It is also the basis for protections you fought to keep."

Lael turned toward him. Her face was pale and exhausted and clear in a way Ren had not seen before. "Then I fought with a tool that cuts the body I meant to protect."

"You amend it. You don't burn it during active crisis."

"Amending it later is how Beryl Shoal got a framework after the scar."

Keeps-Water-Calm lowered his head.

The relay glass flashed:

ORISON ROUTE RISK: +24.9%.

One tenth below threshold.

The chamber seemed to hold its breath through every body that had breath.

Lael looked at Deputy Haro behind the glass. She could not command him. She could not issue Compact language from the wet witness field. She could, however, name what Compact touch had done.

"Record," she said.

Ren's fingers moved.

Lael spoke slowly, making each word pass through constraint.

"Partial wet witness observation: Compact stable-party demand narrows Orison relation into a receiver for human protection, hazard routing, and market reassurance. Under present conditions, invoking that clause would create passable violation. I do not authorize its use from this role. I name it as unsafe."

The witness field flared white.

For one terrible second Ren thought it would reject her.

Then the flare broke into currents and dimmed.

Accepted.

Not as command.

As witness.

Deputy Haro stared through the glass.

Rusk whispered, "You just burned your clean clause."

Lael did not look away from the chamber.

"Good," she said, and the word cost her.

The relay glass crossed the threshold.

ORISON ROUTE RISK: +25.1%.

AUTOMATIC CARRIER SUSPENSION TRIGGERED IN SEVEN POOLS.

The private tooth blazed.

But beneath its flare, Oru-Kel's older darkness remained.

"Now," Oru-Kel said, "we stop pretending clean answer saves us."

Chapter 38: Lael Burns Her Clean Clause

Compact censure arrived as a request for clarification.

That was how human institutions showed teeth politely.

Deputy Haro did not want to place the message on the glass. Ren could see it in the delay between his receiving it and his hand lifting the placard. The sealed chamber gave him no audio channel, no private sideband, no way to soften what had come from outside. He wrote in block letters because small letters would have looked like shame.

COMPACT OVERSIGHT DEMANDS WHETHER LAEL SHUN HAS RENOUNCED STABLE-PARTY BASIS FOR EMERGENCY RECOGNITION.

A second placard followed after a visible swallow:

FAILURE TO CONFIRM MAY RESULT IN TEMPORARY RELIEF OF AUTHORITY.

Rusk closed his eyes.

Vela-Short said, "Relief. That's a pretty word for taking the knife after asking her to hold it."

Lael stood inside the wet witness field with her hands still open. The field had thinned since her observation, but not released her. It held the points where authority had lived: throat, wrist, sternum, ear. Each point glowed faintly now, not as available command but as cauterized site.

"They cannot relieve what I am not carrying," Lael said.

The field did not flare.

Rusk looked at her. "Outside, they can."

"Outside, yes."

"Lael."

"Say it."

He took a breath. "They can end your career."

"They can end the part that required a clean party."

"And the parts that kept bad actors from taking your chair."

She looked toward the hidden tooth. Its flare had reduced to a hard line, furious and fed by the carrier suspensions outside. "My chair is already a route."

No one answered.

Ren opened a record pane, but kept it blank.

Lael looked at them. "Write only if the room allows."

"I know."

"No. You are learning. Not same."

Fair.

The outer glass flashed another metric:

CARRIER SUSPENSION: NINE POOLS.

PRIVATE CHANNEL INQUIRIES: SPIKING.

ROUTEHOLDER EMERGENCY DESKS: REQUESTING CENTRAL ORISON CONTACT.

Salt-Before-Shell made a low sound. "The clean line returns as hunger."

Keeps-Water-Calm said, "Then burn must show flame."

Lael nodded. "Haro needs language."

Third-Voice's blue-white fan lifted. Amber followed. Green-black remained dim but responsive.

Blue-white: "Language for what purpose?"

Lael answered carefully. "To tell Compact Oversight that stable-party basis is unsafe and may not be used as emergency recognition here."

The wet field brightened.

She stopped.

Amber fan: "May not be used by whom?"

Lael's jaw tightened. "By me."

Green-black flickered.

Not enough.

Lael's eyes closed. "By any Compact office relying on my witness."

The field flared brighter, painful.

Vessel-kin moved one hand, ready.

Lael breathed through it. "I cannot bind offices outside the room. I can contaminate the clause with witness so use of it has to show the cut."

The flare broke.

Accepted.

Ren wrote:

LAEL SHUN WITNESS LANGUAGE FOR COMPACT OVERSIGHT: STABLE-PARTY BASIS IS UNSAFE IN THIS DELIBERATION. ANY COMPACT OFFICE USING IT MUST NAME THAT IT REDUCES ORISON RELATION INTO A RECEIVER FOR HUMAN PROTECTION, HAZARD ROUTING, AND MARKET REASSURANCE. USE OF THE CLAUSE AFTER THIS WITNESS IS NOT CLEAN.

Lael read it and shook her head. "Add censure."

Rusk said, "No."

She did not look at him. "Add censure."

Ren waited.

The chamber waited.

Lael said, "If Oversight relieves me for refusing clean reduction, that relief is part of the record."

Ren added:

IF OVERSIGHT RELIEVES LAEL SHUN FOR REFUSING CLEAN REDUCTION, RELIEF ITSELF BECOMES EVIDENCE OF COMPACT DEMAND FOR PASSABLE VIOLATION.

The room went still.

Not because the sentence was dramatic.

Because it removed the institution's favorite hiding place.

Relief of authority usually traveled as administrative hygiene. A temporary measure. A continuity precaution. A way to protect the process from a compromised officer. It let the institution claim sorrow while replacing the person who had made its tools visible. Lael's added line did not stop Oversight from doing it. It made the relief carry its own method into the room.

Ren saw Haro read the line and then look away from the glass for the first time.

He was not refusing transmission.

He was preparing to become implicated by sending it.

Lael saw that too. "Deputy Haro may mark transmission under objection if required."

Haro looked back sharply.

The field around Lael's throat brightened, then dimmed when she added, "Observation only. I do not instruct dry chain."

Haro wrote:

DRY CHAIN TRANSMITS AS RECEIVED. NO OBJECTION ENTERED. PERSONAL NOTE RESERVED.

Rusk made a quiet sound. "Haro."

Behind the glass, Haro did not answer him. He kept his eyes on Lael because looking at Rusk would have turned the act into human office drama, and the chamber had enough hunger already.

Ren added:

DRY CHAIN TRANSMISSION DOES NOT CLEAN OR ENDORSE CONTENT. IT CARRIES WITNESS LANGUAGE WITH SENDER EXPOSURE VISIBLE.

Keeps-Water-Calm's scar lightened.

"Good," they said. "Carrying without washing."

Lael swallowed. "Send."

Rusk whispered, "That is career suicide."

Lael smiled faintly. "No. It is making the execution public."

Salt-Before-Shell stared at her with an expression Ren could not read because it was not for humans. "You burn clause and chair."

"Maybe."

"Do not ask gratitude."

"I am constrained from asking gratitude."

Here pulsed in the brace. Quick rhythm, then slow.

"Good."

Deputy Haro received the language through the glass. He read it once, then again, then looked at Lael.

She nodded.

He transmitted.

The relay metrics shuddered as if a new kind of dirt had entered the system. Compact Oversight did not answer immediately. Press office did. Risk desks did. Legal observers did. The glass filled with partial reactions:

COMPACT PRESS: LANGUAGE TOO COMPLEX FOR PUBLIC STABILIZATION.

OVERSIGHT LEGAL: RESERVE FINDINGS.

ROUTEHOLDER DESKS: CENTRAL CONTACT STILL REQUIRED FOR SUSPENSION REVERSAL.

PUBLIC FEED: "COMPACT OFFICIAL BREAKS WITH OWN GOVERNMENT INSIDE ALIEN SEAL."

Vela-Short exhaled. "Well, they made it worse."

"No," Ren said, surprising themself. "They made it visible."

Oru-Kel brightened.

The private tooth did not dim. It changed.

Before, it had fed from hidden pressure. Now its flare had to pass through named channels: carrier suspension, central contact demand, Compact censure, public simplification. The tooth was still dangerous, but less ghostly. Its outline showed more root than fang.

The named roots looked worse than the hidden outline.

That was the first lesson.

Carrier suspension fed it from below: each suspended pool became an argument for alternate routing. Central contact demand fed it from the side: every request for one Orison receiver shaped the socket Lael had named unsafe. Compact censure fed it from above: if Oversight relieved Lael, the next official would arrive under pressure to restore stable-party language quickly. Public simplification fed it everywhere: every headline made fewer forms of objection sound legitimate.

Ren began mapping the roots as separate lines.

Oru-Kel stopped them with a dark pulse.

"Not yet map."

Ren froze. "Why?"

"Map can become recipe while tooth hungry."

Rusk looked stricken because he understood before Ren did. A precise root map, exported too early, would tell every interested party where to push. Insurers would push suspension. Routeholders would push alternate path. Compact offices would push relief. Public feeds would push simplification. The map would be true and useful in the worst possible order.

Ren closed the map pane.

They wrote instead:

ROOTS NAMED IN CATEGORY ONLY. DETAILED ROOT MAP WITHHELD UNDER ACTIVE FEED RISK. WITHHOLDING IS NOT SECRECY CLAIM; IT IS RECIPE CONTROL UNTIL BODY-FIRST REVIEW.

Salt-Before-Shell's mouth plates shifted. "Humans will call that concealment."

"Yes," Ren said.

"Mirror warning holds?"

"It has to."

Lael, pale in the field, said, "Add that withholding cannot be used to infer absence of roots."

Ren added it.

The chamber accepted the awkwardness.

Rusk saw it. "Exposure is not enough."

"No," Oru-Kel said.

"But it changes what the tooth can pretend to be."

"Yes."

Lael swayed. The wet witness field had begun to take a physical toll. Her lips had gone pale. Vessel-kin moved closer again.

"Care?" Vessel-kin asked.

Lael opened her mouth to refuse automatically.

The chamber caught the reflex.

She closed it.

"Care," she said.

Vessel-kin placed a cool mineral current through the field, not touching her authority sites, only her breath and knees. Lael's body steadied. The care did not make her right. It kept her available to consequence.

At the far side of the chamber, one of the unused vote bodies stirred.

Ren had almost forgotten it was alive.

The third vote body had remained in reserve since the second body cracked. It was larger than the exchange witnesses, built to receive temporary positions from several factions and hold them long enough for Parliament form. Its outer membrane had the opalescent sheen of readiness. Human systems would have called it a procedural asset.

It withdrew from its service cradle.

Third-Voice's blue-white fan turned.

Amber followed.

Green-black flickered with sudden alarm.

Salt-Before-Shell said, "Third body?"

The vote body opened one sensory seam and spoke in a voice like water passing through a closed shell.

"No service."

The chamber temperature shifted.

Lael, still breathing through care, whispered, "It can refuse?"

Here pulsed hard enough to shake the cracked brace.

"Living body," Here said.

The third vote body moved one slow measure farther from the cradle.

"No exchange until dissent has place that is not fracture."

No one spoke.

The clean clause was burned.

The next instrument had refused to become clean.

Chapter 39: The Third Vote Body Refuses Service

The third vote body did not retreat like a machine taken offline.

It retreated like a living thing refusing a hand.

The service cradle opened around it, petals of mineral and soft brace withdrawing too late. The vote body's membrane dimmed from opalescent readiness to a deep pearl gray. It kept one sensory seam open toward Here, another toward Third-Voice, and none toward the human glass.

Rusk stared at it. "If that body refuses exchange, Parliament cannot take a formal stabilizing vote."

Salt-Before-Shell turned. "Still asking what body does for procedure."

"I am naming consequence."

"Consequence begins with body saying no."

Here pulsed in the cracked brace. "Yes."

The third vote body shifted at the sound. "Fracture taught."

Ren felt the sentence settle into the chamber like sediment. The cracked body, the one everyone had treated as failed, had taught the reserve body how refusal sounded.

Lael's wet witness field thinned further. Vessel-kin's care current held her knees, but her face had gone wax-pale. She still watched the third body with full attention.

"What protection is missing?" she asked.

The field did not flare. Good question.

The third vote body did not answer in a list. It opened three faint internal lights. One glowed near the outer membrane, one deep in the central holding tissue, one along the connection point where temporary faction positions would enter.

Third-Voice's blue-white fan translated only structure, not content. "Outer consent. Inner continuity. Entry boundary."

Amber fan added, "It asks protection at all three."

Green-black flickered but did not speak.

Ren waited, then wrote:

THIRD VOTE BODY REQUESTS DISSENT PROTECTION AT OUTER CONSENT, INNER CONTINUITY, AND ENTRY BOUNDARY.

The third body did not pulse with pain.

Progress.

Rusk leaned toward the record. "What does that mean operationally?"

The body closed its sensory seam toward him.

Vela-Short said, "Apparently it means stop starting with operationally."

Rusk stepped back. "Fair."

The third vote body waited until he had fully stepped back before opening the seam again.

That, too, was instruction.

Ren almost missed it because no one spoke. Rusk's retreat had not been enough while his attention still leaned forward. The body had waited for his weight to settle, for his hands to lower, for the operational question to stop standing in the space between them. Only then did the seam open. Consent, Ren realized, was not a yes/no switch at the surface. It was a condition around approach.

They wrote:

OUTER CONSENT INCLUDES APPROACH PRESSURE, NOT ONLY CONTACT.

The third body's outer light brightened.

Rusk read the line and looked as if he had been struck by a small, precise tool. "So even asking the wrong way changes the body?"

Vessel-kin answered, "Asking is touch when body built to receive positions."

Vela-Short folded her arms. "There goes half of human governance."

"More than half," Lael said.

No one smiled.

The third vote body's central light pulsed next. Not faster. Deeper. Its pearled membrane showed a faint internal fold, a shadow of what the cracked vote body had suffered openly. Ren understood with a cold wave that the reserve body had learned not only from the broken body's words but from its tissue memory. It had seen what happened when positions entered, were held, and left no visible account of how holding had changed the holder.

Third-Voice's amber fan moved with difficulty. "Inner continuity asks: if dissent enters and changes the holding body, the changed body must not be treated as corrupted instrument."

The third body held the light steady.

Ren wrote:

INNER CONTINUITY: HOLDING BODY MAY BE CHANGED BY DISSENT WITHOUT BEING CALLED CORRUPTED, FAILED, OR UNFIT SOLELY BECAUSE CHANGE IS VISIBLE.

Here's slow rhythm answered with a low pulse.

"Visible change saved us late," Here said.

The quick rhythm followed. "Invisible change broke us early."

Ren added:

VISIBLE CHANGE IS SAFETY DATA, NOT AUTOMATIC FAILURE.

The third body's central light warmed.

The entry-boundary light came last.

It glowed at the connection point where temporary faction positions would normally pass into service. The light did not widen. It narrowed until it was almost a line. Ren felt the chamber lean away from it, not in rejection but in recognition. Everyone in the room had been tempted by entry. Human law wanted entry into Orison relation so it could protect and govern. Routeholders wanted entry into boundary so they could price and route. Orison factions wanted entry into vote bodies so their pain could act. Care wanted entry so bodies would not die while procedures learned humility.

Entry was not evil.

Entry was where evil could dress as need.

Salt-Before-Shell's voice was quieter than Ren had ever heard it. "Entry boundary says pain cannot be doorway by itself."

The third body opened one seam toward him.

Ren wrote:

ENTRY BOUNDARY: PAIN, URGENCY, REPRESENTATION NEED, MARKET PRESSURE, OR CARE NEED MAY REQUEST ENTRY, BUT NONE MAY BECOME ENTRY BY ITSELF.

Lael said, "Add exit."

The field brightened gently, but did not object.

"Any position that enters under emergency must retain a named exit that does not require the holder to break."

Ren added:

EMERGENCY ENTRY REQUIRES NAMED EXIT THAT DOES NOT REQUIRE HOLDING BODY TO BREAK, DISPLAY PAIN, OR PROVE CONTAMINATION.

The third vote body brightened along all three lights at once.

Not service.

Recognition.

Salt-Before-Shell's limbs loosened by a fraction. "Vote body refuses to be used for urgent neatness."

The third body opened the seam toward him.

"Neatness cuts."

Here answered, "Neatness broke."

The cracked brace hummed with both bodies now, one broken by exchange, one refusing exchange before breaking. The chamber felt full of living procedure. Ren wondered how many human institutions would survive if their voting machines could refuse a ballot on ethical grounds.

Probably none of the ones that needed it most.

Keeps-Water-Calm approached the third body with scar turned neither toward nor away. "Does body refuse all service, or this service?"

The third body held still.

Vessel-kin said, "Do not narrow too quickly."

Keeps-Water-Calm inclined his head. "Correct."

He restated. "What relation would allow service without making fracture?"

The third body's inner light deepened.

"Not allow. Hold."

Ren erased the phrase allow service from the draft before it could become a handle.

The body continued, each sentence slow, made of water pressure and words the translation beads barely carried.

"Dissent enters. Dissent changes holding. Holding shows change. Change not called contamination. Refusal remains able to leave. Pain not required to prove refusal. No outside need may shorten exit."

Ren wrote carefully, line by line:

DISSENT MAY ENTER WITHOUT BEING MADE CONTAMINATION.

HOLDING BODY MUST SHOW HOW DISSENT CHANGES IT.

REFUSAL MUST REMAIN ABLE TO LEAVE.

PAIN IS NOT REQUIRED TO PROVE REFUSAL.

OUTSIDE NEED MAY NOT SHORTEN EXIT.

The third body's membrane brightened a degree.

Lael whispered, "That would slow every exchange."

Salt-Before-Shell said, "Yes."

Rusk looked at the relay metrics. Carrier suspensions had spread beyond the first pools. Private channel inquiries kept climbing. The safe-passage convoy still moved through Dock Seven under stress. Time, the human kind, pressed against every wall.

He said, "If we slow now, people outside pay."

Here pulsed sharply.

"Do not make outside pay enter us as blade."

Rusk bowed his head immediately. "I hear."

The third vote body turned a seam toward him again.

That mattered.

Ren saw the possibility and feared it. The room needed a way to hold multiple states without forcing exchange bodies to absorb everything. Their bad record had centered human categories. The untranslated session had shown boundary without content. Here had demanded division remain present. The third body now described protections not as policy but as conditions for living procedure.

A record could maybe hold some of what a body should not have to hold alone.

Ren hated the thought because it sounded like another human solution.

They said so.

"I am thinking of a record. I distrust that."

Third-Voice's amber fan lifted. "Good."

Blue-white fan: "Distrust can become design."

Green-black flickered faintly.

Here said, "Record must not replace body."

"Yes."

The third vote body said, "Record can carry edges."

Ren looked at it. "Edges?"

"Where positions enter. Where holding changes. Where refusal leaves. Where pain is not demanded."

Keeps-Water-Calm said, "A record of states, not a single state."

Rusk's face shifted. "Multi-state witnessing."

Salt-Before-Shell snapped, "Human already built bad one."

"Yes," Rusk said. "This would need not to be that."

Ren almost laughed. "Helpful."

"I mean it."

"I know. Still helpful in the worst way."

Lael, breathing carefully through Vessel-kin's current, said, "Ren, the first bad record centered administrative action. This one starts with what must not be carried by a body alone."

The wet witness field flared gently, then accepted.

Oru-Kel darkened near the private tooth. "Record edges can reduce tooth food if edges remain visible."

"How?" Ren asked.

"Tooth feeds where relation forced into hidden path. Visible edges make path harder to pretend clean."

Ren looked at the relay metrics, the hidden tooth, Here, the third body, Lael's field, Third-Voice's dim green-black fan. A multi-state witness could hold positions separately, bodily changes separately, refusals separately, unresolved relations separately, and external pressures separately. Not to solve them. To stop any one from being converted into proof of another.

It was not enough.

That was why it might be honest.

They opened a new pane and titled it only:

MULTI-STATE WITNESS, SECOND ATTEMPT.

The chamber did not reject the title.

Ren did not write more yet.

The third vote body moved one measure back toward its cradle, not entering, not refusing entirely.

"Show edges first," it said.

Then it closed every seam except the one facing Here.

The living vote body had not resumed service.

It had assigned homework.

Chapter 40: Ren's Multi-State Witness

Ren began with an empty grid and then deleted the grid.

The chamber noticed.

Rusk noticed too. "Problem?"

"The lines make it look like states are equal because they occupy equal boxes."

"A table is how you keep categories separate."

"A table is how I lied last time."

He accepted that without defense. Progress, and unpleasant.

Ren flattened the pane into five separate fields that did not align. The interface hated it. Human software wanted columns. Ren disabled snap guides, proportional spacing, automatic headers, summary generation, priority tags, and three advisory prompts asking whether they wanted to standardize terms for downstream use.

Salt-Before-Shell watched each prompt die. "Tiny human teeth."

"Yes," Ren said.

Vela-Short, from the translation rack, said, "As the person who maintains some of those tiny teeth, I am offended and also correct."

No one laughed. A few bodies eased.

Ren titled the pane:

MULTI-STATE WITNESS, SECOND ATTEMPT / EDGES FIRST.

The third vote body's seam facing Here opened a little.

Good enough to continue.

Ren created the first field.

POSITION OFFERED.

Then they stopped. The word offered carried too much generosity. Salt-Before-Shell could force a position into the room. Rusk could leak one. Lael could witness one under constraint. Here could refuse the premise of one. Offered was not wrong. It was incomplete in a way that would become permission.

They changed it:

POSITION PRESENT.

The chamber held.

Ren added, under it:

Who or what is making a position present; whether it is demand, witness, refusal, care, warning, fear, strategy, memory, or other; whether the position asks to become decision; whether it denies asking.

Rusk leaned forward despite himself. "Other is vague."

"Good."

Salt-Before-Shell said, "Other keeps water."

Ren created the second field:

BODY CHANGE.

They listed not outcomes but observable changes: exchange body cracked, Here remains divided, Third-Voice green-black made too necessary, Lael in partial wet witness under care boundary, third vote body refusing service, Oru-Kel darkening to name warning, Keeps-Water-Calm's scar offered then withdrawn, Salt-Before-Shell's withdrawal motion paused but alive.

Lael read the line about herself. "Under care boundary, not under care?"

Ren changed it:

Lael in partial wet witness; care supports breath and knees, not authority.

The field accepted the correction.

Third field:

REFUSAL / WITHDRAWAL / NON-ENTRY.

Ren almost put them in separate fields, then stopped. They were not the same. But the room had taught that separation could be theft too if it pretended relations never touched. They wrote the field as a cluster and left space inside it.

Refusal may be boundary testimony. Withdrawal may be freedom or passable violation or both. Non-entry may be care for body. No refusal here may be used alone as evidence of guilt, incapacity, instability, consent failure, or hidden breach. Refusal must remain able to leave record without being called deletion.

Here pulsed.

Quick: "Leave record?"

Ren swallowed. "Yes. If the record holds you by force, it becomes another brace."

The cracked body's slow rhythm pressed against the quick.

"How leave without vanish?"

Ren did not answer quickly.

This was where the bad record would have invented a mechanism.

Keeps-Water-Calm said, "Mark absence as chosen absence, not empty."

Ren wrote:

If a relation leaves the witness, the record may show chosen absence at the edge where it left. Chosen absence is not emptiness, evasion, deletion, or proof.

Here settled.

The third vote body brightened.

Fourth field:

UNRESOLVED RELATION.

Ren's hands slowed. This was the field human systems hated most. Unresolved relation looked like failure. It clogged process. It prevented clean signatures. It kept bodies from being counted and moved.

They wrote:

Relations still active without resolution: Parliament withdrawal and continuing care; routeholder exposure and routeholder harm; Compact protection and Compact reduction; Here's quick and slow rhythms; Third-Voice's unequal voices; safe-passage debt and treaty uncertainty; Pale Arc warning and human political crisis; public distortion and named response; third vote body refusal and possible future service.

Lael whispered, "That is the heart."

The witness field flared gently at heart, then did not reject it.

Rusk said, "Operational systems will ask which unresolved relations block action."

Ren wrote a line below the field:

Unresolved relation is not automatically block, authorization, risk, or delay. Any system claiming it as one must name how and who is changed by that claim.

Rusk stared. "That is impossible to automate."

"Good," Salt-Before-Shell said.

Rusk surprised them by nodding. "Good, and expensive."

"Better than hidden cost," Keeps-Water-Calm said.

Fifth field:

EXTERNAL PRESSURE.

This one filled too quickly: carrier suspensions, private channel inquiries, Compact Oversight censure threat, public feed distortion, routeholder market repricing, medical convoy cold-chain stress, press demand for simplified line, risk threshold, automatic systems, legal observers, human fear of unreadability.

Ren added:

External pressure may be present and urgent without being allowed to shorten consent, repair division, compel translation, centralize receiver, or convert refusal into evidence.

Oru-Kel darkened near the private tooth.

"Add tooth food."

Ren added:

Record shall mark where external pressure feeds private route tooth or other passable violation pathways.

The tooth dimmed by a fraction. Not because the record defeated it. Because the hidden channel had been named as an edge.

The five fields hung in the chamber, uneven, ugly, unsummarized.

The software offered a synthesis button.

Ren disabled the entire toolbar.

Vela-Short made a small satisfied noise.

Third-Voice's blue-white fan lifted. "How used?"

Ren shook their head. "Not as vote."

Amber fan: "Not as treaty."

"Not as proof of consent."

Green-black flickered.

Ren continued, "As witness support. It carries edges so bodies do not have to carry all edges at once. It shows when a proposed action crosses a state it has no right to absorb."

The third vote body opened another seam.

"Test with exchange."

Ren looked at it. "Now?"

"No. Test with refusal."

Keeps-Water-Calm moved.

He had been waiting so still that Ren realized, too late, that the next test had always been his. The Pelagos diplomat turned his scar neither toward nor away. He stood at the edge of the pane and looked not at Ren's words but at Ren's face.

"I refuse to let Beryl Shoal enter this record as support for Lael's burned clause," he said.

The room tightened.

Ren's first instinct was to reassure him.

They strangled it.

Their second instinct was to move his refusal under REFUSAL / WITHDRAWAL / NON-ENTRY.

They stopped that too.

Keeps-Water-Calm watched the stop.

"Good. Now what?"

Ren breathed.

Beryl Shoal had appeared in the record already as scar, memory, warning against post-harm frameworks, and evidence that clean repair could carry a cut. Lael's burned clause had leaned on that history; Lael had said amending later was how Beryl got a framework after the scar. Keeps-Water-Calm was not denying the relation. He was refusing its conversion into support.

Ren created an edge marker between BODY CHANGE, UNRESOLVED RELATION, and REFUSAL / WITHDRAWAL / NON-ENTRY. Not a box. A visible seam.

They wrote:

KEEPS-WATER-CALM REFUSAL: BERYL SHOAL MEMORY MAY REMAIN PRESENT AS INJURED RELATION BUT MAY NOT BE USED AS SUPPORTING EVIDENCE FOR LAEL'S BURNED CLAUSE, COMPACT REFORM, OR HUMAN COURAGE.

Keeps-Water-Calm's scar darkened.

Not pain.

Attention.

Ren added:

This refusal does not erase prior witness. It limits later use.

The scar eased.

Lael bowed her head inside the wet witness field. "Accepted."

The field did not flare.

Rusk said, "Does that mean the public record cannot mention Beryl?"

Ren looked at Keeps-Water-Calm instead of answering for him.

Keeps-Water-Calm said, "Public record may say Beryl memory was present and then limited itself."

Ren wrote it exactly.

The third vote body brightened to pearl gray.

"Edges first," it said again.

This time the phrase sounded less like homework and more like door.

Rusk tested the door badly.

Not maliciously. That almost made it more useful.

He looked at the five fields, at the edge marker around Beryl, at the relay metrics still climbing outside, and said, "Could the witness mark carrier suspension as external pressure without making it Orison fault?"

The third vote body's pearl dimmed.

Rusk stopped so quickly Ren could hear the old sentence die in his throat.

Vela-Short said, "You stepped on it."

"Yes," Rusk said. "I did."

Salt-Before-Shell did not spare him. "You ask record to protect Orison from fault so carriers return."

Rusk took the hit. "Yes."

"Fault not first wound."

"No."

Ren watched the multi-state witness tremble, not visually but structurally. It wanted to help. That was the danger. A human record built to protect edges could still become a tool for reducing consequence if the first test was framed around blame management. They had nearly let that happen because the question sounded responsible.

They wrote nothing.

The silence did more work than a correction would have.

Rusk tried again.

"Carrier suspension is external pressure. It is also a consequence of public distortion, routeholder omission, Compact demand for stable-party language, and Orison unreadability to human systems. If I ask which part is Orison fault, I am already making the wrong cut."

Keeps-Water-Calm said, "Better. Still hungry."

"Then tell me where the hunger remains."

The Pelagos diplomat did not look to Ren. He looked to the third vote body.

The body opened its outer seam toward Rusk.

"You ask how record changes carrier."

Rusk nodded slowly. "Yes."

"Ask how carrier changes record."

Rusk frowned, then understood enough for discomfort to enter his face.

Ren opened a temporary edge line between EXTERNAL PRESSURE and POSITION PRESENT.

They wrote:

CARRIER SUSPENSION ENTERS AS EXTERNAL PRESSURE AND AS POSITION PRESENT: IT MAKES A CLAIM THAT SHOALS APPROACH IS UNACCEPTABLE UNDER CURRENT HUMAN RISK FORM. RECORD MAY NOTE THIS CLAIM WITHOUT ACCEPTING ITS CAUSE, ITS BLAME, OR ITS DEMAND FOR A SINGLE RECEIVER.

The chamber held.

Lael said, "Add changed bodies."

Ren connected the edge to BODY CHANGE:

CARRIER SUSPENSION CHANGES BODIES BY DELAYING OR REROUTING MEDICINE, MINERALS, WITNESSES, FOOD-CHAIN SUPPORT, AND LEGAL PRESENCE. THESE CHANGES ARE NOT ABSTRACT MARKET SIGNALS.

Here pulsed.

Quick rhythm: "Good."

Slow rhythm: "Incomplete."

Ren waited.

Here continued, "Suspension also changes us before cargo fails. It makes chamber feel smaller."

Ren added:

SUSPENSION CHANGES DELIBERATION BY MAKING TIME FEEL LIKE A WALL. THIS FEELING MAY BE RECORDED BUT MAY NOT BECOME CONSENT.

The third vote body's central light warmed.

Rusk looked at the new edge lines. "Then the witness does not answer whether carriers should return."

"No," Ren said.

"It makes their demand visible as one state among others."

"Yes."

Vela-Short said, "And makes it harder for them to pretend they are weather."

Ren wrote:

AUTOMATIC CARRIER RULES ARE NOT WEATHER. THEY ARE DESIGNED PRESSURE WITH AUTHORS, BENEFICIARIES, AND BODY COSTS EVEN WHEN EXECUTED BY MACHINE.

The hidden tooth dimmed.

Not by much.

Enough for everyone to notice.

Oru-Kel brightened at its edge. "Record edge cuts less than blade. Still cuts."

Third-Voice's green-black fan flickered once, visible and faint.

Ren felt the temptation to turn that into success and resisted it.

They marked:

TOOTH RESPONSE OBSERVED. NO CLAIM OF NEUTRALIZATION.

The third vote body brightened again.

"Edges first," it said a third time.

Now it sounded like condition.

Chapter 41: Keeps-Water-Calm Tests the Human

Keeps-Water-Calm did not let the door open easily.

"Second test," he said.

Ren's fingers stayed near the pane but did not touch it.

Good.

The Pelagos diplomat turned his scar fully away from the record. The act had become familiar enough to hurt differently now. It meant: do not ask the wound to work. It meant: what has been shown once is not automatically public resource. It meant, perhaps, that every record hungry for moral weight would have to go hungry for a while.

"I refuse Orison use also," Keeps-Water-Calm said.

Salt-Before-Shell's limbs shifted. "Use of Beryl?"

"Use of Beryl to prove human treaty cannot heal. Use of Beryl to make withdrawal look pure. Use of Beryl to make Salt-Before-Shell's motion older than it is."

Salt-Before-Shell went very still.

The test had turned.

Ren saw the temptation immediately. It would be easy to place this under the same refusal edge as before: not for Compact reform, not for human courage, now not for Orison withdrawal. Symmetry. Clean. Bad.

Keeps-Water-Calm watched them see it.

"Do not balance me," he said.

Ren withdrew their hand from the pane.

"Because balance would make your refusal serve fairness."

"Yes."

"And fairness would become another use."

"Yes."

Salt-Before-Shell made a sound Ren had never heard from him before. Not anger. Not shame. Something like a shell opening under pressure because remaining closed would crack it.

"I have used Beryl in my mind," he said.

Keeps-Water-Calm looked at him.

No rescue. No accusation.

"Yes," the Pelagos diplomat said.

Salt-Before-Shell lowered three limbs. "I do not ask forgiveness."

"Good."

"I ask whether withdrawal can still speak beside Beryl without carrying it."

Keeps-Water-Calm considered. The room waited through the full consideration, which was perhaps the first honest gift it had given either of them.

"Yes," he said. "Beside. Not through."

Ren wrote only after the word beside settled.

They created a second edge marker, not parallel to the first. The first had limited human use. This one limited Orison use. But they placed it at a different angle, touching WITHDRAWAL / NON-ENTRY and UNRESOLVED RELATION, not BODY CHANGE. Beryl as wound had entered differently in each attempted use; the edge had to show that.

They wrote:

KEEPS-WATER-CALM REFUSAL, SECOND EDGE: BERYL SHOAL MEMORY MAY NOT BE USED TO PROVE HUMAN TREATY CANNOT HEAL, TO PURIFY WITHDRAWAL, OR TO MAKE CURRENT ORISON MOTION OLDER THAN ITS PRESENT CHOICES. WITHDRAWAL MAY SPEAK BESIDE BERYL, NOT THROUGH IT.

Keeps-Water-Calm's scar did not darken.

It simply remained.

Here pulsed in two rhythms.

"Beside," the quick rhythm said.

"Not through," the slow rhythm answered.

The third vote body brightened another degree.

Rusk, who had been silent too long, said, "Third test will be routeholder."

Keeps-Water-Calm turned toward him. "You offer?"

Rusk looked at the private tooth, the carrier suspension metrics, the central contact demands, and the multi-state witness hanging unevenly in the room.

"I should."

Salt-Before-Shell said, "Should is clean word."

Rusk nodded. "I am afraid to."

"Better."

Rusk stepped closer to the pane. He did not touch it. "I refuse to let routeholder response use Beryl, Here, Third-Voice's strain, or the vote body's service refusal as proof that Orison systems are too complex for standard routing and therefore require private corridor alternatives."

The room changed around the phrase private corridor.

Ren felt it before the private tooth reacted. Lael felt it too; the wet witness field flared along her sternum and throat.

"Aven," she said.

Rusk's face hardened. Not defensively. Against himself.

"There is a plan," he said.

The tooth brightened.

Oru-Kel darkened at once. "Name only edge first."

Rusk stopped. Swallowed.

Ren understood the danger. If he described the plan now, the private corridor might become a solution in the room before its edges were marked. It would arrive as urgency: carrier suspensions rising, safe-passage dependence, private channels already blooming. A bypass would look practical. Practical was often the first mask of passable violation.

Ren wrote:

RUSK REFUSAL EDGE: ROUTEHOLDER RESPONSE MAY NOT USE BERYL, HERE, THIRD-VOICE STRAIN, THIRD VOTE BODY REFUSAL, OR ORISON COMPLEXITY AS PROOF THAT STANDARD ROUTING MUST BE REPLACED BY PRIVATE CORRIDOR ALTERNATIVES.

The private tooth flared violently.

The chamber did not reject the line.

Rusk stared at the flare. "That touched it."

"Yes," Oru-Kel said.

Lael's voice was thin. "Private corridor alternatives?"

Rusk looked toward the glass, where the risk metrics continued to climb in red increments, then back to Lael.

"If carrier suspensions continue, coalition members will propose a bypass corridor around the Shoals. Emergency-only at first. Private underwriting, external monitoring, no Parliament care-passage dependency. It will be sold as stabilizing trade while the Salt Parliament resolves internal process."

Salt-Before-Shell's limbs spread in slow horror.

"Bypass," he said.

"Yes."

"Around us."

"Yes."

"Using our complexity as hazard."

Rusk did not soften it. "Yes."

Ren expected Salt-Before-Shell to attack the proposal.

Instead he attacked the word temporary.

"Temporary means what body can remove it?"

Rusk answered too quickly. "Coalition vote, risk normalization, Compact review--"

The third vote body's seam closed.

Rusk stopped.

He looked at the closing seam and understood that he had done it again: made exit belong to the systems that wanted entry.

"No," he said, before anyone else did. "That is not an exit. That is owner discretion."

Salt-Before-Shell lowered one limb, not mercy, but space for correction.

Rusk tried again. "Temporary means nothing unless the relations routed around can end it without proving they are safe by the bypass's standards."

The third body reopened the seam.

Ren wrote:

PRIVATE CORRIDOR TEMPORARY CLAIM HAS NO VALID EXIT IF ONLY ROUTEHOLDER, COMPACT, OR MARKET RISK SYSTEMS CAN END IT. EXIT MUST BE AVAILABLE TO RELATIONS ROUTED AROUND WITHOUT REQUIRING THEM TO PROVE SAFETY BY BYPASS TERMS.

The hidden tooth brightened hard enough to turn the wet glass white for a moment.

Oru-Kel absorbed the flare with darkness that shook.

Vessel-kin moved toward them, but Oru-Kel held up a limb.

"Not care yet. Naming first."

Rusk's face had gone gray. "The draft may not have an Orison exit."

"May," Salt-Before-Shell said.

Rusk closed his eyes. "Likely does not."

"Likely."

"It does not," Rusk said. "If it follows the standard emergency corridor template, it ends when risk normalizes or when sponsors withdraw. The routed-around party can comment, not terminate."

Lael whispered, "Comment window after path exists."

Keeps-Water-Calm's scar darkened.

Ren added:

STANDARD EMERGENCY CORRIDOR TEMPLATE LIKELY PROVIDES COMMENT, NOT TERMINATION, TO ROUTED-AROUND RELATION. COMMENT AFTER PATH EXISTS IS NOT EXIT.

The chamber received that with a low pressure shift.

Keeps-Water-Calm said, "And Pale Arc boundary?"

Rusk looked at Oru-Kel.

Oru-Kel's body had gone so dark that only the outline of limbs remained. "Private corridor changes pressure outside Shoals. Boundary warning already bent toward tooth. Bypass may make passable violation larger than Parliament."

Ren wrote the sentence because Oru-Kel had given it as warning, not content theft:

PRIVATE CORRIDOR MAY SCALE PASSABLE VIOLATION BEYOND PARLIAMENT BY ROUTING AROUND THE RELATION THAT OBJECTS.

The third vote body dimmed and brightened in a slow pulse.

"Record edges first," it said.

Ren added a new EXTERNAL PRESSURE edge:

PRIVATE CORRIDOR PLAN MAY NOT BE DISCUSSED AS SOLUTION UNTIL ITS USES OF ORISON COMPLEXITY, MARKET FEAR, PALE ARC BOUNDARY CONDITIONS, AND PRIVATE ROUTE TOOTH FEEDING ARE NAMED.

Rusk said, "That may cost us the last fast option."

Here pulsed: "Fast option maybe hidden bite."

"Yes."

Lael closed her eyes. "Aven, who has authority to propose it?"

Rusk's silence answered before he did.

"My deputy can place it before the coalition if I remain unavailable."

Deputy Haro's glass flashed:

ROUTEHOLDER COALITION EMERGENCY SESSION SCHEDULED.

A second line appeared:

AGENDA ITEM DETECTED: TEMPORARY PRIVATE CORRIDOR STABILIZATION.

No one in the chamber moved.

The private tooth no longer looked like a tooth.

It looked like a doorway being built elsewhere.

Chapter 42: Aven's Private Corridor

Aven Rusk asked to draw the corridor and no one let him.

That refusal saved the room from a map.

Maps were dangerous in human hands. Ren knew it from the Gate, from Dock Seven, from every treaty lesson that pretended a line became harmless when labeled provisional. A map arrived as description and left as inevitability. Once a corridor existed on a display, even as a warning, some part of the human room began calculating transit time.

Salt-Before-Shell understood without needing the history.

"No picture," he said.

Rusk lowered his hand from the slate. "Then I will name edges."

"Ugly."

"Ugly."

The private tooth pulsed at the word, then dimmed when Oru-Kel darkened beside it.

Rusk faced the multi-state witness pane. "Private corridor edge one: it treats Orison deliberation as delay external to route safety."

Ren wrote under EXTERNAL PRESSURE, not POSITION PRESENT.

Rusk watched the placement and nodded. "Edge two: it separates trade continuity from care-passage relation, while still depending on the Shoals' prior stabilizing work."

Keeps-Water-Calm said, "The bypass eats the reef and says it did not enter water."

Rusk swallowed. "Yes."

Ren wrote that too, attributing it to Keeps-Water-Calm.

"Edge three," Rusk continued, "private underwriting gives routeholders the appearance of assuming risk while shifting political risk onto Parliament. If the corridor works, coalition claims necessity. If it fails, Orison instability is blamed."

Salt-Before-Shell's limbs curled inward. "Trap with two mouths."

"Yes."

"Edge four?" Lael asked from the wet witness field.

Rusk looked at her as if hoping she would stop him.

She did not.

"Edge four: external monitoring requires sensor placement near Pale Arc boundary turbulence."

Oru-Kel's old darkness expanded so sharply that Ren's screen dimmed.

The chamber felt the warning before anyone spoke.

Third-Voice's green-black fan flickered twice. Amber lowered. Blue-white steadied.

Oru-Kel said, "Say more. Slowly."

Rusk's voice roughened. "The proposed corridor skirts the Shoals' formal care-passage zones but passes close to the boundary disturbance where Pale Arc rhythm was detected. Routeholders would frame the monitoring as safety verification. But if the rhythm is relation warning rather than signal, sensor pressure could become another touch."

"Another passable violation," Ren said.

Oru-Kel did not brighten.

"Maybe larger."

The third vote body withdrew farther from its cradle.

Here pulsed in the cracked brace, both rhythms sharp.

Rusk said, "I did not design the corridor."

Salt-Before-Shell snapped, "But your office made teeth that show path."

"Yes."

The word landed harder because he no longer hid behind scope.

Deputy Haro's glass showed the coalition emergency agenda expanding:

TEMPORARY PRIVATE CORRIDOR STABILIZATION

PROPOSED FEATURES: EXTERNAL MONITORING / PRIVATE UNDERWRITING / EMERGENCY-ONLY TRAFFIC / NON-PARLIAMENTARY CONTACT NODE

The last item made Lael's field flare.

"Non-Parliamentary contact node," she said.

Rusk looked sick. "A central contact without calling it stable party."

Oru-Kel: "Clean clause wearing routeholder coat."

Lael whispered, "Yes."

Ren saw the old clause reassemble itself from pieces no one wanted to own.

External monitoring would ask for sensor access while insisting it did not ask for political recognition. Private underwriting would ask for risk control while insisting it did not govern. Emergency-only traffic would ask to move first and define limits later. The non-Parliamentary contact node would ask for one receiver while insisting it was only technical. No single feature carried the whole harm. Together they built a corridor that could say it had not demanded stable-party recognition while requiring every function stable-party recognition had performed.

That was the genius of the bypass.

It did not lie in one sentence.

It distributed the lie until each sentence could deny being the lie.

Ren wrote:

CORRIDOR DESIGN DISTRIBUTES STABLE-PARTY FUNCTION ACROSS FEATURES: MONITORING, UNDERWRITING, EMERGENCY SCOPE, AND CONTACT NODE. EACH FEATURE DENIES BEING THE WHOLE CLAUSE WHILE TOGETHER RECREATING THE CLAUSE'S EFFECT.

The wet witness field around Lael went almost white.

She did not fall because Vessel-kin had already braced her breath.

"That is the clean clause after disassembly," she said.

Rusk bowed his head. "Yes."

"My office would have missed it."

"Mine built it."

No one softened either sentence.

Ren added to the witness:

PRIVATE CORRIDOR EDGE FIVE: NON-PARLIAMENTARY CONTACT NODE RECREATES STABLE-PARTY DEMAND OUTSIDE PARLIAMENT AND CALLS IT ROUTE SAFETY.

The private tooth blazed hard enough that several human displays fuzzed.

Vela-Short cursed and slapped the translation rack into passive mode. "It is trying to make my system summarize that."

"Do not let it," Ren said.

"Already didn't."

Rusk's slate flashed. He did not touch it. "Coalition session is requesting my emergency vote."

"Can you vote from here?" Lael asked.

"The seal blocks command."

"Does it block refusal?"

Rusk stared at her.

The chamber turned toward that question.

Refusal again. Not as proof. Not as purity. As boundary testimony. As action that did not enter the court demanding it.

"I can send a non-command refusal edge," Rusk said slowly. "Not a vote. A notice that my office's authority is constrained by witness record and cannot be used to support corridor without naming these edges."

Salt-Before-Shell said, "Will that stop them?"

"No."

"Will it dirty them?"

"Yes."

"Send."

Rusk looked to Third-Voice.

Blue-white fan: "Routeholder may send edge if it does not command room."

Amber fan: "Human systems may use it."

Green-black flickered.

Here pulsed: "Mark use."

Ren wrote:

RUSK NON-COMMAND REFUSAL EDGE TO COALITION: MY OFFICE AUTHORITY MAY NOT BE USED TO SUPPORT TEMPORARY PRIVATE CORRIDOR STABILIZATION UNLESS THE PLAN NAMES ITS USE OF ORISON COMPLEXITY, CARE-PASSAGE SEPARATION, POLITICAL RISK SHIFT, PALE ARC SENSOR TOUCH, AND NON-PARLIAMENTARY CONTACT NODE AS STABLE-PARTY RECREATION.

Rusk read it. "Add: Emergency does not cleanse bypass."

Ren added:

EMERGENCY DOES NOT CLEANSE BYPASS.

Rusk kept reading, and Ren saw that the line still let him hide in office boundaries.

"Add my omission," he said.

Lael looked up.

Rusk did not look at her. "Coalition must not describe this as independent of my earlier advisory. The public distortion that made the corridor plausible followed my omission of the boundary record. If they use the crisis, they use that omission."

The chamber tightened.

Ren added:

CORRIDOR URGENCY IS NOT INDEPENDENT OF RUSK ADVISORY OMISSION AND PUBLIC DISTORTION. ANY PLAN USING CURRENT CRISIS MUST NAME THAT ITS OPENING WAS PARTLY MADE BY OMITTED BOUNDARY RECORD.

Rusk's voice was flat now, but not empty. "Add that my refusal edge is not absolution."

Ren wrote:

RUSK REFUSAL EDGE DOES NOT ABSOLVE RUSK, ROUTEHOLDER OFFICE, OR COALITION SYSTEMS OF PRIOR PRESSURE CONTRIBUTIONS.

Salt-Before-Shell's limbs lowered a fraction.

"Now send," he said.

Rusk sent it through the only channel the seal allowed: not as authorization, not as vote, but as exposed machinery. The glass displayed SENT BESIDE, NOT COMMAND.

For three seconds, the private tooth dimmed.

Then the coalition agenda changed.

TEMPORARY PRIVATE CORRIDOR STABILIZATION - EDGE OBJECTIONS NOTED.

VOTE PROCEEDING.

Rusk's face emptied.

"They are proceeding."

Salt-Before-Shell said, "Of course."

Lael looked at the chamber. "If the corridor vote passes, Parliament faces a route around its own objection."

Keeps-Water-Calm said, "And every faction here must decide what body carries the answer."

The Salt Parliament began to move before the sentence ended.

Not as one chamber.

As several.

Care-passage bodies drew toward Vessel-kin. Withdrawal bodies gathered behind Salt-Before-Shell. Boundary witnesses clustered near Oru-Kel. The third vote body held between cradle and refusal. Here remained cracked and present. Third-Voice tried to orient toward all of them and could not. Green-black flickered under the impossible load.

Ren saw the division form.

Not argument.

Embodiment.

The Salt Parliament was taking incompatible obligations into different bodies.

Chapter 43 had begun before anyone named it.

Chapter 43: The Salt Parliament Divides

The split did not tear the chamber.

It taught Ren what tearing had been preventing.

Bodies moved with a precision too old to be crisis improvisation. Care-passage delegates slid toward Vessel-kin, forming a low crescent around the routes by which medicine, minerals, and living cargo entered the Shoals. Their colors dimmed to practical greens and mineral grays. They did not argue for humans. They carried dependence that had become survival.

Behind Salt-Before-Shell gathered those who had waited years to say no without asking whether humans would call no instability. Their limbs sharpened, but not all in anger. Some held grief. Some held old reef-bite memories not Pelagos, old survey cuts not Beryl, old signatures that had taken too much future for too little safety. They carried the motion to withdraw because remaining had become its own injury.

Near Oru-Kel, boundary witnesses darkened the water. They were not a faction in human terms. They did not want passage or withdrawal first. They wanted the chamber to understand that every proposed path now touched the older warning. Their bodies faced the private tooth, the relay glass, the wet witness field, and the hidden direction of the Pale Arc all at once.

The third vote body stayed between cradle and refusal.

Here remained cracked.

Third-Voice stood at the center, which was now the worst place in the room.

Ren's multi-state witness pane tried to keep up and failed gracefully. That was new. Instead of forcing the bodies into one view, it showed five uneven fields and the edges between them. Care-passage dependence appeared under BODY CHANGE and EXTERNAL PRESSURE. Withdrawal gathered under POSITION PRESENT, REFUSAL / WITHDRAWAL / NON-ENTRY, and UNRESOLVED RELATION. Boundary warning appeared as POSITION PRESENT and EXTERNAL PRESSURE without becoming either. Here's division remained its own edge. The third vote body's refusal stayed visible but did not authorize any side.

For once, the record did not make the room smaller.

It made the room harder to lie about.

Rusk looked at it with a face full of terrible arithmetic. "If the coalition vote passes before Parliament answers, private corridor work begins in hours."

Salt-Before-Shell said from the withdrawal cluster, "Then human appetite shows itself."

Vessel-kin answered from care-passage. "And hatchery supply loses visible path."

"Visible path with hook."

"Hook can still carry medicine."

"Hook pierces."

Care-passage bodies rippled. Some recoiled from the word. Some accepted it and stayed.

Ren saw the danger of wanting one of them to be right.

Lael, still in wet witness, whispered, "They are all right where they stand."

The field flared and held.

Ren waited for the room to punish the sentence for being too neat.

It did not, because Lael had not said all right as agreement. She had said it as location.

The multi-state witness accepted the phrase only after Ren changed it into uglier form:

POSITIONS ARE LOCALLY TRUE TO THE BURDENS THEY HOLD. LOCAL TRUTH DOES NOT AUTHORIZE TOTAL CLAIM.

The care-passage crescent steadied.

The withdrawal cluster did not soften, but it stopped sharpening.

Boundary witnesses kept their dark attention on the tooth.

Rusk read the line and said, "Human systems will call that no decision."

Salt-Before-Shell answered, "Human systems call many things by hunger name."

"Yes."

"What does routeholder call it?"

Rusk looked at care-passage, then withdrawal, then boundary, then Here. "A decision not to let one risk model eat the others."

The private tooth dimmed by a fraction.

Ren wrote:

ROUTEHOLDER PLAIN: LOCAL TRUTHS MUST NOT BE FED INTO ONE RISK MODEL AS IF THE MODEL CAN DIGEST THEM WITHOUT CHANGING THEM.

Vela-Short said, "That sentence is going to ruin someone's dashboard."

"Good," Rusk said, and sounded like he meant it in the exhausted way of someone who had built the dashboard.

Then the care-passage bodies moved again.

One smaller vessel-kin body, mottled blue and gray, separated from the crescent and approached the witness pane. It did not ask Third-Voice for translation. It touched the BODY CHANGE field with a care limb and let the beads carry only a minimal phrase:

CARE DOES NOT CONSENT TO BYPASS.

The withdrawal cluster answered with a low pulse that the record did not translate until Salt-Before-Shell gave it a human edge:

WITHDRAWAL DOES NOT CONSENT TO STARVATION.

Boundary witnesses darkened, and Oru-Kel added:

BOUNDARY WARNING DOES NOT CONSENT TO IGNORANCE AS SAFETY.

Here pulsed quick and slow:

DIVISION DOES NOT CONSENT TO BEING SOLVED.

Ren entered each under its own field, not as a list, not as consensus. Four noes, beside each other, none allowed to cancel the others.

The third vote body brightened toward the pane.

"Noes can stand," it said.

For a moment the chamber had something that was not answer and not paralysis. It had distributed refusal, which was harder to use and harder to sell.

Third-Voice's amber fan lifted weakly. "Yes."

Blue-white fan: "Positions carry different obligations."

Green-black flickered.

"Do not merge," Here said.

The chamber obeyed.

For twenty seconds.

Then the relay glass flashed:

COALITION VOTE: PRIVATE CORRIDOR STABILIZATION LEADING.

AUTOMATIC SUSPENSION: THIRTEEN POOLS.

SAFE-PASSAGE CONVOY: DOCK SEVEN EXIT INCOMPLETE.

The care-passage crescent surged toward the glass. The withdrawal cluster sharpened against it. Boundary witnesses darkened, and the private tooth flared with joy so naked that even Rusk recoiled.

"It wants us to choose fast," Ren said.

Oru-Kel answered, "It wants each body to carry only one truth."

The third vote body opened a seam. "No exchange."

Salt-Before-Shell turned toward it. "If no exchange, how does Parliament answer corridor?"

"Not by breaking me."

"Then what body carries withdrawal?"

"Yours."

The answer hit the withdrawal cluster like cold current.

Vessel-kin said, "What body carries care-passage?"

"Yours."

Oru-Kel: "Boundary warning?"

"Yours."

Here pulsed, quick and slow. "Division?"

The third body brightened toward the cracked brace. "Yours."

Rusk said, very quietly, "And the answer?"

The third vote body closed one seam and opened another toward Third-Voice.

"Not one body."

Everyone looked at Third-Voice.

Ren wished they would not.

Blue-white fan lifted. Amber followed. Green-black remained dim, trembling with the pressure of being seen as solution.

Third-Voice said, "No."

The room froze.

Salt-Before-Shell's limbs drew back. "Third?"

Blue-white: "We cannot be answer body."

Amber: "We are already overloaded."

Green-black did not speak.

Vessel-kin lowered their care limbs. "Then who holds continuity?"

No one answered.

That was the chamber's true wound. Not disagreement. Not even distrust. Continuity had been outsourced to bodies that could still break, to witnesses who could fade, to signatures that cut, to vote bodies that could refuse, to records that could be used, to human systems that priced fear, to old forms that saved hatchery medicine but could not decide the treaty.

Lael took one step inside the wet witness field and nearly collapsed.

Vessel-kin reached.

Lael raised one shaking hand. "Care, yes. Command, no."

Care touched her. Command did not.

She looked at Third-Voice. "If you do not hold continuity, do you vanish?"

Amber fan turned toward her. "Wrong question."

Lael breathed. "If you refuse to be answer body, what remains of Third-Voice?"

Blue-white: "Procedure."

Amber: "Relation."

Green-black flickered once, faint as a distant organism in dark water.

Ren waited.

The whole chamber waited.

Green-black said, "Pain."

The word entered human language with no ornament.

Third-Voice lowered as if the word had weight.

Blue-white: "We can release green-black to preserve function."

Amber: "We can continue with two."

Green-black did not object.

That was the horror.

Salt-Before-Shell moved toward them, then stopped because rushing to save a voice could become another use.

Here pulsed hard. "Do not repair by cutting."

The third vote body brightened. "Continuity that sacrifices dissent becomes clean body."

Ren wrote that before they could think better:

CONTINUITY THAT SACRIFICES DISSENT BECOMES CLEAN BODY.

The room accepted it with pain.

Third-Voice trembled.

Rusk looked at the relay glass, then away. For once he did not bring the timer into the center.

Oru-Kel darkened beside the tooth. "Older warning touches here too."

Blue-white fan: "Yes."

Amber fan: "If we cut green-black, we become passable path."

Green-black flickered again.

Not strong.

Present.

Third-Voice lifted all three fans by degrees so small Ren could hardly see them. The motion hurt. It hurt the body, hurt the room, hurt the wish for a clean answer.

"We choose painful continuity," Third-Voice said.

Three voices carried it unequally.

The private tooth dimmed.

Not because the crisis ended.

Because one clean path had refused to become passable.

Chapter 44: Third-Voice Chooses Painful Continuity

Painful continuity required witnesses who did not applaud it.

Third-Voice made that clear before anyone could turn endurance into virtue.

Blue-white fan lifted first. "Record condition."

Amber fan followed. "No praise."

Green-black flickered, dim and ragged. "No lesson."

Ren felt the line land in them like a command and then corrected themself. Not command. Boundary.

They wrote:

THIRD-VOICE CONTINUITY CONDITION: NO PRAISE, NO LESSON, NO USE OF PAIN AS PROOF THAT THREEFOLD WITNESSING IS SUSTAINABLE.

The multi-state witness held the line under BODY CHANGE and UNRESOLVED RELATION, with an edge toward EXTERNAL PRESSURE because every system outside would be eager to call Third-Voice's survival evidence that nothing needed to change.

Third-Voice lowered slightly in relief.

Then the body began the work.

It was not dramatic at first. No convulsion. No luminous crisis. Blue-white adjusted a current in the left basin. Amber opened a relational channel toward the care-passage crescent. Green-black, barely visible, remained present at the edge where withdrawal, boundary warning, and human record touched.

The cost appeared in delays.

Blue-white answered a procedural ripple half a breath late. Amber let a care signal pass too close to the withdrawal cluster before catching it. Green-black tried to mark a hidden center in Ren's record and failed to make color for it. Third-Voice's central body sagged, then righted itself, then sagged again.

Vessel-kin moved forward.

Third-Voice's amber fan said, "Support. Not replacement."

Vessel-kin stopped close enough to help and far enough not to take over.

"State support requested."

Blue-white: "Mineral current under base."

Amber: "Relational spacing around care and withdrawal."

Green-black flickered.

Ren waited.

Green-black made no word.

Here pulsed in the cracked brace. "Let weak ask slow."

Everyone waited.

The relay glass flashed in the background:

COALITION VOTE CONTINUES.

PRIVATE CORRIDOR SUPPORT: 61%.

No one brought it forward.

Green-black finally spoke. "Do not hide my failure."

Ren wrote the support condition:

GREEN-BLACK SUPPORT REQUEST: FAILURES REMAIN VISIBLE.

Vessel-kin placed the mineral current. Care-passage bodies opened relational spacing. Salt-Before-Shell withdrew two limbs that had been pressing too hard toward the center. Oru-Kel darkened near the tooth, not to shield Third-Voice from pressure but to keep the pressure from pretending to be the only clock.

Third-Voice steadied.

Not well.

Steadily enough.

Ren watched the supports become visible one by one.

The mineral current did not glow beneath Third-Voice like rescue. It registered as a thin gray brace under the central body, deliberately narrow, deliberately insufficient to hold more than weight. Vessel-kin marked it with a care tag that said:

SUPPORTING BASE STRESS ONLY. DOES NOT CARRY VOICE, DECISION, OR CONTINUITY.

The relational spacing around care and withdrawal was harder to see. It appeared as absence. Care-passage bodies stopped filling every gap with readiness. Withdrawal bodies stopped letting their sharp limbs point through Third-Voice to reach human glass. Amber did not ask them to trust each other. Amber only made enough room that their distrust did not pass through the same injured body at the same time.

Ren added:

RELATIONAL SPACING SUPPORTS LOAD DISTRIBUTION ONLY. DOES NOT INDICATE RECONCILIATION, COOLING OF WITHDRAWAL, OR ACCEPTANCE OF CARE-PASSAGE TERMS.

Salt-Before-Shell read the line and said, "Good. My limbs are still angry."

Vessel-kin answered, "And not using Third as path."

"For now."

"For now is recordable."

Ren wrote:

FOR NOW RECORDED. NO DURABILITY CLAIM.

Green-black flickered at that, a weak little line of approval or relief or simple continued existence. Ren did not name which.

The hardest support was Oru-Kel's darkness.

It did not touch Third-Voice. It did not touch the tooth. It made an interval in which pressure had to reveal direction before entering the center. Relay fear struck the interval and bent red. Private corridor urgency struck it and bent white. Public distortion struck it and broke into static. Each pressure still existed after passing through, but none could pretend to be neutral weather.

Oru-Kel said, "Darkness is not shelter. It is contrast."

Ren entered:

BOUNDARY CONTRAST SUPPORT: EXTERNAL PRESSURE MUST SHOW DIRECTION BEFORE TOUCHING CENTER. CONTRAST DOES NOT BLOCK PRESSURE OR MAKE CENTER SAFE.

Third-Voice's body steadied another fraction.

Not enough for comfort.

Enough to make comfort feel dishonest.

Lael watched from the wet witness field with tears floating at the edges of her eyes, held there by surface tension and discipline. "Outside, they will call this dysfunction."

Rusk said, "Outside, I might have."

She looked at him.

"Before," he added.

Salt-Before-Shell said, "Before is not absolution."

"No."

Ren wrote neither exchange. Some things were present without needing to become record. That, too, was progress.

The third vote body opened the seam facing Third-Voice. "Can vote begin?"

The chamber tightened.

Withdrawal.

The word did not need to be spoken. It had waited behind every corridor edge, every burned clause, every refusal, every safe-passage debt. Now the divided Parliament had bodies to carry incompatible obligations, a multi-state witness to show edges, and a Third-Voice that refused to become a clean continuity by cutting its weakest voice.

None of that made the vote safe.

It made the vote possible without immediate betrayal.

Blue-white fan lifted with difficulty. "Vote can begin if cost exchange precedes count."

Amber: "No body votes from abstraction."

Green-black, after a long delay: "No cost becomes leverage."

Ren wrote:

WITHDRAWAL VOTE CONDITION: COST EXCHANGE BEFORE COUNT. NO BODY VOTES FROM ABSTRACTION. COSTS MAY BE WITNESSED BUT NOT USED AS LEVERAGE TO FORCE POSITION.

Here pulsed.

"Pain not required to prove refusal."

Ren added it.

The third vote body brightened again, but remained outside the cradle. "I will not hold exchange."

Salt-Before-Shell's limbs tightened.

The body continued, "I will hold thresholds."

Third-Voice's amber fan lifted. "Explain."

"Each faction brings cost to edge. I mark when cost has been brought without making cost into vote. I do not carry positions inside. I do not merge."

Ren saw the elegance and distrusted it immediately.

"What prevents threshold from becoming gate?" they asked.

The third body turned a seam toward them. "Record."

"What prevents record from becoming gate?"

Here pulsed: "Us."

Keeps-Water-Calm said, "And refusal to let threshold prove maturity."

Ren added:

THRESHOLD HOLDING DOES NOT CERTIFY READINESS, MATURITY, STABILITY, OR LEGITIMACY. IT ONLY MARKS THAT COST HAS BEEN BROUGHT TO EDGE.

The third body accepted.

Rusk looked toward the relay glass. Private corridor support had climbed to 64%. He opened his mouth, then closed it.

Lael saw. "Say it as external pressure, not argument."

Rusk nodded. "External pressure: corridor vote likely passes before withdrawal count completes."

The multi-state witness took the line under EXTERNAL PRESSURE.

Salt-Before-Shell said, "Present. Not ruling."

"Present," Rusk agreed. "Not ruling."
