Care-passage sent a narrow stabilizing current behind the withdrawal push, not taking over, not softening its refusal. The care current held the human ship's local water from shearing while the withdrawal current bent the wake.

Ren wrote:

CARE-PASSAGE SUPPORTS RESCUE WITHOUT CLAIMING WITHDRAWAL ACTION AS TREATY CARE.

The third vote body accepted the line.

The protected minority basin remained warm.

The wake struck the edge of the service lane and split.

For one breath Kestrel Minor disappeared inside sensor noise.

Rusk made no sound. That was worse.

Lael's wet witness field flared around her throat. "Haro?"

The glass remained static.

Then:

Kestrel Minor hull contact minimal.

Crew telemetry alive.

Drive restart pending.

Salt-Before-Shell sagged.

No one thanked him.

No one praised him.

No one dared.

The withdrawal current still held, because the wake had not fully passed. The human ship's marker drifted along the edge of the curve, alive and uselessly fragile. Ledger Spar tumbled beyond it, the uncrewed test probe now sending corrupted telemetry in bursts.

Rusk said, "Ledger Spar is going to cross the lane after the wake."

Salt-Before-Shell turned toward him with pure exhaustion. "Your machine continues being problem."

"Yes."

"Can it be stopped?"

"Field operators lost stable control. They are trying to recover."

Oru-Kel darkened. "Control hunger again."

Vela-Short looked at the passive translation rack. "Could send another non-command pattern."

Rusk shook his head. "The probe is not in wake relation now. It is tumbling on inertial path. Pattern will not matter."

Silence.

Then Salt-Before-Shell said, "Can withdrawal push move ship more?"

Vessel-kin answered, "Not without tearing local care water."

Care-passage bodies trembled at the edge of depletion.

The human ship still had no drive.

Ren saw the next impossible choice forming and hated it.

Salt-Before-Shell saw it too.

"Human ship needs physical tug."

Rusk looked at him. "No tug can reach in time."

The protected minority basin warmed sharply.

Here pulsed. "Do not make death mouth."

No one moved.

Then one small withdrawal body detached from Salt-Before-Shell's cluster. It was not one of his limbs. It was a faction body Ren had barely noticed, shaped for current work, not speech. It moved into the care-passage lane and opened itself like a living drag anchor.

Salt-Before-Shell snapped, "No."

The body answered, not in human words.

Third-Voice translated with pain. "It can pull wake-torn water. It may not return unchanged."

Care-passage bodies moved to stop it.

The protected minority basin warmed again, not blocking, asking.

The small body turned one seam toward Salt-Before-Shell.

This time Third-Voice did not translate.

Salt-Before-Shell understood anyway.

His limbs lowered.

"Rescue without martyr story," he said.

Ren wrote:

WITHDRAWAL BODY VOLUNTEERS PHYSICAL CURRENT DRAG. RISK OF CHANGE. ACTION MAY NOT BE RECORDED AS MARTYRDOM, HUMAN DEBT, TREATY PROOF, OR WITHDRAWAL PURITY.

The body entered the current.

The service lane bent again.

Kestrel Minor moved.

Ledger Spar tumbled through the space where the human ship had been and vanished into the disturbed dark beyond the lane.

The glass updated:

Kestrel Minor clear.

Crew alive.

Withdrawal body status: changed / present.

The glass tried to add a fourth line and failed because Haro killed it before the full sentence appeared.

Ren saw only the first words:

GRATEFUL CREW STATEMENT--

Then blank.

Haro pressed both hands to the glass from the other side. His face was pale. He wrote with deliberate strokes:

CREW ALIVE. GRATITUDE HELD OUTSIDE CHAMBER UNLESS INVITED BY RECORD.

The protected minority basin warmed toward him.

Salt-Before-Shell did not look at Haro. "Good dry chain."

It was the closest thing to praise he could offer without making a hook.

Ren wrote:

CREW GRATITUDE MAY EXIST OUTSIDE RECORD. IT MAY NOT ENTER CHAMBER AS DEBT, PROOF, HERO STORY, OR SOFTENING OF WITHDRAWAL COST.

Rusk said, "Routeholder desks will use alive."

His voice was flat now, as if grief and shame had spent the surface of him and left only machinery.

The glass confirmed him:

ROUTEHOLDER DESKS: EMERGENCY RESPONSE DEMONSTRATES NEED FOR STANDBY VECTOR AUTHORITY.

CARRIER POOLS: HUMAN SHIP SURVIVAL REDUCES IMMEDIATE LIABILITY.

PRESS OFFICE: ORISON WITHDRAWAL FACTION AIDS HUMAN CREW.

Lael made a pained sound. "Already."

Ren wrote faster:

POST-RESCUE MISUSE: HUMAN SHIP SURVIVAL DOES NOT DEMONSTRATE NEED FOR STANDBY VECTOR AUTHORITY, REDUCE RESPONSIBILITY FOR PRIVATE TEST INITIATION, PROVE ORISON GOODWILL, OR CREATE PRESS-READY HERO NARRATIVE.

Third-Voice's amber fan lifted. "Add body changed."

Ren looked at the small withdrawal body.

It had returned, but returned was too simple a word. Its outer surface had lost the clean ridges of current-work shape and gained a rough translucent seam along one side where wake-torn water had passed through it. It moved with Salt-Before-Shell's cluster but not in rhythm. Present. Changed. Not lost. Not whole as before.

The body did not ask for attention.

That made attention necessary.

Ren wrote:

WITHDRAWAL BODY COST: RESCUE CHANGED BODY FORM. PRESENT DOES NOT MEAN UNHARMED. SURVIVAL DOES NOT ERASE COST.

Care-passage shifted toward it.

Salt-Before-Shell snapped, "Care not own."

Vessel-kin stopped. "Care asks permission to support changed body without making rescue treaty."

The changed body opened one small seam.

Salt-Before-Shell's limbs trembled. "It accepts care."

Ren wrote:

CHANGED WITHDRAWAL BODY ACCEPTS CARE-PASSAGE SUPPORT. ACCEPTANCE DOES NOT MAKE TREATY PROOF, GRATITUDE DEBT, OR WITHDRAWAL REVERSAL.

The care current touched the changed seam and did not close it. Closure would have been another lie. It cooled the burn, supported the body, and left the change visible.

Here pulsed, slow and uneven. "Changed remains changed."

"Yes," the third vote body said.

The private tooth flickered as if searching for any sweetness left in the event. Heroism had been denied. Gratitude denied. Authority denied. Survival denied as erasure. It found one possible food: purity.

Salt-Before-Shell found it too.

"Do not call us pure because one body paid," he said.

Ren entered:

RESCUE DOES NOT PURIFY WITHDRAWAL.

Lael added, weakly, "Nor does it purify humans."

Ren wrote:

RESCUE DOES NOT PURIFY HUMANS.

Rusk said, "Nor routeholders who caused need."

That one cost him. Ren saw it.

They wrote:

RESCUE DOES NOT PURIFY ROUTEHOLDER MACHINERY THAT CREATED THE HAZARD.

Oru-Kel darkened near the glass. "Nor warning."

Ren added:

RESCUE DOES NOT PURIFY BOUNDARY WARNING OR MAKE WAKE SAFE.

By the time they finished, the rescue had become heavier than celebration could carry.

Salt-Before-Shell closed every mouth plate.

He had saved a human ship.

The vote would not be allowed to use it.

Chapter 54: A Vote With Refusal Inside It

No one moved toward decision after the rescue.

That was the first mercy the chamber managed.

Kestrel Minor drifted beyond the lane with its crew alive, its hull carrying a shallow bruise where wake pressure had licked across plates never built for Orison water. Ledger Spar was gone from immediate sight, its hazard reduced to a bad line in the dark and a long audit waiting for human hands. The withdrawal body that had opened itself as drag anchor rested in a care-passage cradle, changed and present, not dead, not whole in the way it had been before the current.

The outer glass wanted a story. Its human habit was visible even after every prohibition. It arranged the rescue as sequence: danger, intervention, survival, consequence. It made narrative lanes because sensors did not know shame.

Ren ordered the display dimmed.

Deputy Haro did it without asking why.

Salt-Before-Shell remained at the basin rim. His mouth plates were shut so tightly that the translator offered only a soft pressure mark where speech might have been. Around him the withdrawal faction held a shape Ren had learned to read as guarded exhaustion. They had spent force. They had risked one of their own. They had broken none of their refusals, and now every other faction had to prove it understood that.

Rusk stood behind the witness rail with both hands visible.

He had not said thank you.

Ren respected him for that more than for any apology he had made.

Third-Voice pulsed from the central basin in three uneven colors. Its damaged harmonics made each phrase arrive with a little drag, as if the chamber had to carry the meaning the last handspan.

"Parliament cannot return to old vote."

Oru-Kel answered first. "Old vote already failed."

"Old vote failed because old vote made clean columns," Third-Voice said. "Accept. Refuse. Abstain. Delay. Clean columns cut living relation into dead storage."

Vela-Short's fingers tightened around a notation stylus. "We can add reservations."

Several Orison bodies darkened at once.

Vela raised one hand. "I know. Human word. Inadequate. I mean recorded constraints that alter the motion of the decision."

"Constraint is not decoration," Here said from the protected minority basin.

"No," Vela said. "Constraint is load-bearing."

Ren felt the sentence settle correctly. She wrote it before anyone could soften it:

CONSTRAINT IS LOAD-BEARING.

Salt-Before-Shell's closed plates opened by a fraction.

Not approval. Not forgiveness. But hearing.

Lael stepped to the edge of the witness floor. Her field had steadied after the rescue, though pale stress still glimmered around her throat. "What does a vote need to do that the old form could not?"

Third-Voice moved one limb through the water.

The basin showed four currents.

One current flowed toward the human corridor proposal, not as ownership now, not as the bypass Aven had attempted, but as a need to maintain contact without tearing Orison space. Another current flowed away from any human route, carrying the withdrawal refusal. A third current curved around both, care-passage work that would remain obligated to bodies before agreements. The fourth did not move like direction at all. It pulsed in place: protected minority memory, the heat of those who had almost been made symbol.

"Vote must show relation after decision," Third-Voice said. "Not only decision."

Oru-Kel's dorsal plates lifted. "If relation after decision includes refusal, humans will call treaty unstable."

Rusk said, "Some humans will."

Every visible eye turned toward him.

He did not step back. "The companies will call it unusable if refusal can still interrupt route planning. Some administrators will call it incomplete because it cannot be converted into a permanent access map. Some captains will dislike it because it asks them to read politics instead of coordinates."

"And you?" Salt-Before-Shell asked.

Rusk swallowed. "I will call it accurate."

The chamber held that sentence at a distance. It did not reward him. It did not reject him either.

Ren wrote:

HUMAN WITNESS ACKNOWLEDGES THAT ACCURACY MAY REDUCE HUMAN CONVENIENCE.

"Do not make your discomfort noble," Salt-Before-Shell said.

Rusk bowed his head once. "Understood."

Here warmed. "Vote form."

Third-Voice sent a new diagram into the basin. It was not a ballot. It was a braided record with separable strands. Each faction could enter a motion in one of five relations: joins, permits without joining, refuses and remains in protected relation, refuses and withdraws from implementation, or delays because the body required repair before speech. The strands did not collapse into majority. Instead, the final relation was determined by the pattern of risk: which bodies would bear cost, which waters would be touched, which refusals had to remain active to keep the decision from becoming harm.

Vela stared at the diagram with scholarly hunger and visible fear.

"This is not efficient," she said.

"Correct," Oru-Kel answered.

"It is not legible to standard treaty tables."

"Correct."

"It requires future meetings."

"Correct."

Lael looked at Ren. "It also prevents a single signature from pretending to settle what stays alive."

Ren nodded. Her hands had started to ache. She kept writing.

The proposed form received a working name from care-passage first: relation-vote-with-visible-refusal. It was too long in human terms. It was exactly long enough in Orison terms. The translation rack tried to shorten it to "qualified vote." Third-Voice struck the phrase from the glass so sharply that the letters scattered into white noise.

"No qualification," Third-Voice said. "Refusal is not smaller acceptance."

Salt-Before-Shell finally moved.

He crossed from the basin rim to the central witness floor, slow with spent current. The withdrawal faction parted around him without ceremony. When he reached the diagram, he placed one limb through the strand marked refuses and remains in protected relation.

"This strand must not be used to count us as agreeing."

"It will not," Lael said.

"This strand must not be used to count us as absent."

"It will not."

"This strand must not be used to say humans were forgiven."

Rusk answered before Lael could. "It will not."

Salt-Before-Shell's mouth plates clicked once. "You do not hold that promise alone."

"No," Rusk said. "I can only witness that I heard it."

Ren recorded the exchange in full.

Then the changed withdrawal body stirred in its care cradle.

The chamber turned.

It did not speak in mouth-sound. It shaped a small pressure around itself, a damaged current that touched the refusal strand and the care strand at once. Third-Voice reached toward it, then stopped, asking without words. The body pulsed again.

Third-Voice translated unevenly. "It says: do not make my change a bridge."

The protected minority basin warmed so fast that steam fogged the nearest glass.

Here spoke. "Yes."

The new vote form altered under that sentence. A mark was added: embodied cost cannot be converted into permission. Rescue, injury, repair, risk, and sacrifice could be entered as evidence of relation, but never as automatic consent. No body could be made into a bridge after being harmed.

Ren knew she was writing one of the central laws of the compact that might follow, though no compact had yet been drafted.

She wrote carefully:

EMBODIED COST MAY INFORM WITNESS. IT MAY NOT CREATE ACCESS.

Oru-Kel clicked approval. Care-passage repeated the line in a softer current. Even the pro-contact merchants did not object. They had seen the service lane. They had felt the wake. They knew what kind of lie objection would reveal.

Only the private delegation screens remained silent.

Deputy Haro checked one and said, "Aven's channel is still open."

Rusk's face hardened.

"Do they want to enter a statement?" Lael asked.

Haro listened to his earpiece, then shook his head. "They want confirmation that their lost probe will not be classified as hostile action if they provide its emergency logs."

Salt-Before-Shell made a sound like stone cracking under salt.

Ren did not look away from the page.

"Enter their request under human liability record," Lael said. "Not under Parliament vote."

"Done," Haro answered.

The chamber returned to the diagram.

Third-Voice asked for first relation entry.

Care-passage entered: permits limited corridor study only where living bodies can interrupt it.

Oru-Kel entered: joins warning structure, refuses speed claims, requires Pale Arc rhythm authority.

Here entered: remains in protected relation, requires minority heat before any route adjustment touching refuge zones.

The pro-contact merchants entered: permits narrow exchange lanes, accepts non-ownership language, protests delay. Their protest stayed visible. That mattered too. A vote that hid hunger would be no more honest than a vote that hid refusal.

Then Salt-Before-Shell entered the withdrawal relation.

Refuses human corridor. Remains in protected relation. Allows rescue obligations to exist without becoming treaty proof. Rejects forgiveness language. Requires every future human request to begin with harm history, not opportunity.

The strand darkened, then held.

It did not break the braid.

It did not merge.

The chamber waited for the form to reject the contradiction.

It did not.

The relation-vote held five visible positions in one decision-space. No majority swallowed them. No refusal destroyed the shared basin. The result was ugly by diplomatic standards, asymmetrical and difficult to teach. It looked less like law than a wound learning how not to close wrong.

Ren loved it and distrusted her love.

Third-Voice pulsed. "Provisional form accepted for compact drafting."

No applause followed.

The outer glass tried to name it anyway.

COMPACT TABLE SUGGESTION: QUALIFIED ACCEPTANCE WITH PROTECTED RESERVATIONS.

The chamber darkened so fast that the phrase looked embarrassed before Haro deleted it.

Vela-Short muttered, "I hate that I understand why it offered that."

"Then help kill it properly," Ren said.

Vela took the stylus without argument and wrote on a side pane:

NOT QUALIFIED ACCEPTANCE.

She paused, grimaced, and added:

NOT RESERVATION.

Ren continued:

NOT MINORITY APPENDIX.

Lael added from the wet field:

NOT UNSTABLE TREATY.

Rusk said:

NOT ROUTE PERMISSION WITH OBJECTIONS.

Salt-Before-Shell's mouth plates opened.

"Not a human yes wearing our no."

Ren wrote that one in full:

NOT A HUMAN YES WEARING ORISON NO.

The protected minority basin warmed with fierce approval.

Third-Voice let the rejection bundle settle before offering the export line:

RELATION-VOTE WITH VISIBLE REFUSAL IS A DECISION-SPACE THAT PRESERVES ACTIVE NON-CONSENT INSIDE LIMITED COORDINATION. IT CANNOT BE MAPPED TO ACCEPTANCE, ABSTENTION, RESERVATION, DEADLOCK, OR FAILURE WITHOUT MATERIAL DISTORTION.

The sentence was long enough to make every human system resent it.

Good.

Deputy Haro transmitted it to the dry chain and added no summary.

The dry chain responded:

STANDARD TABLE FIELD UNAVAILABLE.

Lael laughed once, a small exhausted sound.

"That may be the most honest thing the table has said."

Ren wrote:

STANDARD TABLE FIELD UNAVAILABLE.

Here pulsed. "Unavailable can be protection."

Oru-Kel replied, "Or excuse."

Both were true. Ren added:

UNAVAILABLE FIELD MUST NOT BE AUTOFILLED.

The third vote body accepted that as part of the provisional form.

The changed withdrawal body rested.

Salt-Before-Shell turned toward Ren. "Human witness."

She looked up.

"Write this plain."

Ren set down the formal stylus and opened a blank field beneath the record.

Salt-Before-Shell spoke slowly enough that no translation could pretend confusion.

"We remain against you. We remain near enough to stop you. We remain near enough to save you if saving does not become ownership. We do not forgive. We do not leave."

Ren wrote every word.

The basin accepted the line.

For the first time since the wake struck, the Parliament breathed without trying to become one body.

Chapter 55: Third-Voice Restored Unevenly

Third-Voice failed again before anyone could call it restored.

The failure was small enough that human systems almost missed it. The central basin kept its color. The translation rack did not alarm. The witness record held its line numbers and timestamp discipline. But the chamber knew. Every Orison body in the Parliament shifted before the diagnostic glass produced a single warning.

One of Third-Voice's three sound paths went silent.

Not broken this time. Withheld.

Ren watched the basin dim along one side and felt the room resist the old panic. No one rushed a repair body into the water. No one demanded a reboot. Care-passage moved near, then stopped at the boundary of request. Oru-Kel lowered his dorsal plates and waited. Salt-Before-Shell did not move at all.

Third-Voice pulsed once through the remaining two paths.

"I am not gone."

The sentence arrived crooked.

Deputy Haro checked his console anyway. "Translation variance at eleven percent."

Vela whispered, "Acceptable?"

Ren shook her head before she knew she had chosen an answer. "Not our word."

Third-Voice pulsed again. The silent path stayed dark.

"Not acceptable. Not failure. Different."

Here warmed the protected minority basin with a slow, cautious heat. "Different by injury?"

"Different by injury. Different by choice. Cannot sort clean."

That answer disturbed the chamber more than another collapse would have. Collapse had a protocol. Damage had care forms. Choice had political consequence. A voice that could not say whether its silence was wound or will required the Parliament to treat the ambiguity as real rather than solve it for administrative comfort.

Ren wrote:

THIRD-VOICE REPORTS PARTIAL SILENCE AS BOTH INJURY AND CHOICE, NOT CLEANLY SEPARABLE.

Lael read the line and nodded once.

Care-passage asked in color, "May repair approach?"

Third-Voice answered with two paths and one absence. "Approach edge. Do not close."

The care bodies came to the edge of the central basin. They carried repair salts, soft conductor threads, memory gel, and patient hands. The old Lael Shun would have read the procedure as technical intervention. The Lael standing beside Ren now watched it like diplomacy.

One care body extended a thread toward the silent path.

Third-Voice darkened.

The thread stopped.

"There," Third-Voice said. "That is too much."

The care body withdrew exactly half a handspan.

"There?" it asked.

"There."

No one pretended the exchange was efficient.

Rusk stood farther back than usual. After Ledger Spar, his body had learned that distance could be a form of participation. Ren could see him wanting to help and refusing the performance of usefulness. He was improving in ways that did not absolve him.

The repair continued by inches.

Each thread was offered, refused, shifted, offered again. Each salt flow was named before release. Each memory gel patch waited until Third-Voice pulsed consent through the paths that remained. The silent path never brightened. It did, however, stop collapsing inward. Its darkness became shaped instead of ragged.

Vela's stylus hovered.

"I need a term," she said softly.

Oru-Kel answered, "No."

She looked wounded, then understood. "Right. No term yet."

Ren nearly smiled. The chapter of the Parliament had changed people in small humiliating ways first. Those were the changes that lasted.

Third-Voice turned one sensor cluster toward Salt-Before-Shell.

"Withdrawal heard?"

Salt-Before-Shell opened one mouth plate. "Heard."

"Silent path may remain silent during compact."

"Then compact hears silence."

"Silence may interrupt."

"Then compact must stop."

"Silence may be mistaken for consent by humans."

Rusk spoke from the rail. "Then the human record will define silence as active non-consent unless Third-Voice names it otherwise."

Haro glanced at him, then at Lael.

Lael said, "Enter that as provisional human administrative rule for this chamber."

Ren wrote it:

THIRD-VOICE SILENCE SHALL NOT BE INTERPRETED AS CONSENT. HUMAN RECORD ACCEPTS ACTIVE NON-CONSENT UNLESS OTHERWISE STATED.

Salt-Before-Shell made no sign of gratitude. But one of his faction bodies eased its grip on the basin rim.

The repair team placed a conductor thread across the edge of the silent path. Not into it. Across the edge. A bridge that did not claim passage. The metaphor was dangerous; Ren rejected it before writing. No bridges. A boundary marker. A held seam. An invitation that remained outside the door.

Third-Voice accepted the thread.

The central basin changed.

The missing path did not return as sound. Instead it began sending pressure in short, irregular beats. The translation rack tried to map them into syllables and produced nonsense: if-stone, under-mouth, salt-left, no-green. Third-Voice cut the rack from that path with a flare of irritation.

"Not for words," it said.

Care-passage brightened with comprehension. "Pulse witness."

"Yes. Pulse witness. Carries stress. Carries refusal. Carries fatigue. Not speech."

Here warmed. "Body language inside translation."

"Close."

Ren put down the stylus again and flexed her fingers. The ache had become a second pulse under her skin.

"If it is not speech," she asked, "how do I record it?"

Third-Voice turned fully toward her. The two speaking paths braided around the silent pressure.

"As not speech."

Ren waited.

No further clarification came.

She laughed once, too tired to stop herself. The sound was small and human and inappropriate. Several Orison bodies shifted in alarm.

"Sorry," she said. "I understand."

She wrote:

THIRD PATH RESTORED AS PULSE WITNESS, NOT SPEECH. RECORD MUST NAME ITS PRESENCE WITHOUT TRANSLATING IT INTO WORDS.

The line felt insufficient. It was also the most honest thing available.

Vela finally lowered her stylus. "Our treaty archives cannot store a witness that is not text, image, audio, or certified sensor data."

"Then your treaty archives are too small," Oru-Kel said.

"Yes," Vela said.

She did not defend them. That mattered.

Haro opened a side channel to the archive technicians and began asking ugly practical questions. Could a treaty packet include a living pressure pattern? Could it include a nonverbal witness index? Could the official copy mark a section that must be re-heard in chamber conditions rather than read from a static file? The answers that came back were mostly no, followed by delays, followed by one frightened maybe.

Lael seized the maybe.

"Build from that," she ordered.

Third-Voice pulsed with two voices and one pressure beat.

The chamber settled into a different rhythm.

Ren had thought restoration would mean return: three paths where three paths had been, translation repaired, the Parliament's mediator made whole enough to carry everyone else again. That was the human temptation in every injury: to call healing successful when it became invisible.

Orison would not permit that lie.

The third path remained visibly changed. Its pressure beat interrupted speech when strain rose too high. It warmed when a clause tried to hide refusal. It slowed when humans named routes as if water were empty. It did not explain itself. It made explanation stop and wait.

After the fourth interruption, one of the pro-contact merchants snapped a color Ren did not know.

Third-Voice let the pressure beat answer.

The merchant dimmed immediately.

"It says the clause is hungry," Here translated from the protected basin.

The merchant curled inward. "It is accurate."

No punishment followed. The clause was rewritten.

Salt-Before-Shell watched the altered mediator with a suspicion that had lost one layer of contempt. "You are not neutral."

Third-Voice's two speech paths answered together. "Never was."

"You pretended better before."

"Yes."

Oru-Kel made a pleased clicking sound.

Third-Voice continued. "Old neutrality was service mask. Useful. Harmful. Damaged now."

"Do you mourn it?" Lael asked.

The basin held still for a long time.

The pressure path beat once.

"Yes."

No one corrected the grief.

Care-passage finished the boundary thread and withdrew. They left no seal, no certification mark, no final diagnostic. Instead they placed a small living indicator beside the central basin: a strip of responsive salt that would darken if the silent path was overrun by repair pressure, translation demand, or political force.

Haro asked, "Is that for your team?"

Care-passage answered, "For everyone who might forget."

Ren recorded that too.

Then Third-Voice requested the relation-vote form from the previous session. The braid appeared again: joins, permits without joining, refuses and remains in protected relation, refuses and withdraws from implementation, delays for repair before speech. A new mark formed beside it, made of pressure rather than color.

"Add damaged witness relation," Third-Voice said.

Vela leaned forward. "Who can use it?"

"Any body whose ability to speak is altered by the process being voted."

The protected minority basin warmed with fierce approval.

Lael's eyes closed for one breath. "That changes every compact procedure."

"Good," Salt-Before-Shell said.

Rusk looked at the floor.

Ren knew he was thinking of Kestrel Minor, of Ledger Spar, of all the human procedures that treated damage as evidence after decisions rather than a participant in them. She hoped the shame hurt. She hoped it became useful without becoming theater.

Third-Voice pulsed the new relation into the braid.

The vote form held.

It was less elegant now. More burdened. Harder to export, harder to explain, harder to abuse without leaving marks. The third path beat once in the middle of it, a pressure witness that no transcript could flatten.

Ren wrote the final line of the restoration record:

THIRD-VOICE RETURNS TO SERVICE UNEVENLY. UNEVENNESS IS PART OF SERVICE, NOT A DEFECT TO BE HIDDEN.

The central basin accepted the line.

Haro's archive channel returned with its frightened maybe.

ARCHIVE TECHNICIANS: NONVERBAL PRESSURE PATTERN CAN BE STORED AS SUPPLEMENTAL SENSOR APPENDIX, NOT PRIMARY TEXT.

Third-Voice's pressure path struck once, hard enough to ripple the basin.

"No appendix," Ren said before the rack could render anyone else's objection.

The technicians could not hear her, but Haro could. He wrote the objection on the dry pane:

NOT APPENDIX.

Lael added, "Not supplemental."

Vela added, "Not evidentiary attachment."

Rusk, after a pause, said, "Not optional review material."

Ren gathered the bundle:

DAMAGED WITNESS RELATION MUST BE STORED AS COEQUAL RECORD CONDITION. PRESSURE WITNESS IS NOT APPENDIX, SUPPLEMENT, ATTACHMENT, OPTIONAL REVIEW MATERIAL, OR TRANSLATOR NOTE.

The archive channel hesitated.

Then:

ARCHIVE TECHNICIANS: STANDARD PACKET CANNOT VALIDATE COEQUAL NON-TEXT CONDITION.

Salt-Before-Shell said, "Then packet fails."

Lael repeated it in human legal shape. "If the standard packet cannot validate the record condition, the standard packet is insufficient for this compact."

Ren wrote:

STANDARD PACKET INSUFFICIENT.

The phrase landed with surprising force. It did not solve storage. It changed the burden. The problem was no longer Third-Voice's altered path failing the archive. The archive was failing the relation it claimed to preserve.

Haro stared at the dry response, then typed a longer question with visible care.

Could a packet require chamber reactivation?

The answer took longer.

ARCHIVE TECHNICIANS: POSSIBLE AS RESTRICTED INTERPRETIVE CONDITION. RECORD WOULD NOT BE FULLY REVIEWABLE OUTSIDE CERTIFIED CHAMBER PLAYBACK.

Vela exhaled. "That is ugly."

Oru-Kel answered, "Ugly enough to be true?"

Vela looked at Third-Voice, at the pressure path, at Ren's exhausted hands. "Maybe."

Ren wrote:

CERTIFIED CHAMBER PLAYBACK REQUIRED FOR DAMAGED WITNESS RELATION. OUTSIDE REVIEW MAY READ INDEX BUT MAY NOT CLAIM FULL RECORD ACCESS WITHOUT REACTIVATING PRESSURE CONDITION.

Here warmed. "Reading not hearing."

Ren added:

READING IS NOT HEARING.

Third-Voice accepted the line with two colors and one pulse.

The pro-contact merchants did not like it. One of them asked, carefully this time, "If every future compact needs chamber playback, route negotiation slows."

The pressure path beat once.

Hungry clause.

The merchant corrected. "If this compact needs chamber playback, route negotiation slows. Cost named, not objection."

Ren wrote the cost.

No one let speed become proof.

Third-Voice spoke with two voices and one changed silence.

"Proceed to compact draft."

Chapter 56: The Shoals Compact Draft

The first compact draft began as a refusal to begin with routes.

That alone cost them forty-three minutes.

Human treaty systems expected scope, parties, definitions, authority, duration. Vela-Short placed those headings on a side display because some human archive would eventually need them, then darkened the panel until it became subordinate to the basin. Lael did not object. Rusk looked at the hidden headings with the expression of a man watching a useful tool become dangerous in public.

Third-Voice placed no heading in the central water.

Instead it released a memory current.

Dock Seven appeared without image. There were no bodies drawn, no dramatic reconstruction, no human-friendly grief sequence. The current carried pressure loss, delayed warning, blocked exit, cargo priority, and the silence after the last reachable crew signal. It moved through the chamber as condition rather than story.

Here warmed the protected minority basin.

Salt-Before-Shell opened all mouth plates.

"Begin there," he said.

Ren wrote:

THE COMPACT BEGINS WITH HARM HISTORY, NOT OPPORTUNITY.

Vela copied the line into the dormant human heading panel under preamble, then stopped herself and renamed the heading memory foundation. Ren saw the change and approved silently.

The draft's first clause took shape slowly.

No human vessel, company, research body, relief fleet, treaty office, or successor authority could request passage, exchange, refuge, mapping, salvage, communication priority, or emergency exception in Shoals water without attaching a harm history statement relevant to the request. The statement could not be ceremonial. It had to name prior damage, active uncertainty, bodies likely to bear risk, and procedures for stopping the request if harmed witnesses entered refusal.

Rusk said, "Successor authority needs stronger language."

Lael looked at him.

"Companies rename themselves," he said. "Consortia dissolve and reassemble. Flag registries shift. If the compact binds only named institutions, it will be evaded within a year."

Salt-Before-Shell angled toward him. "You know evasion mouth."

"Yes."

"Use it against itself."

Rusk nodded. "Any entity deriving operational benefit from a covered request inherits its obligations, whether or not it signed."

Vela's eyes widened. "That is going to make half the corridor lobby refuse recognition."

"Good," Oru-Kel said.

"Not good," Lael said. "Clarifying. We should know who intends evasion."

Ren wrote the clause. It felt like placing a stone in water and watching current reveal itself around the obstruction.

The second clause belonged to Orison.

The Shoals were not a single sovereign body, not a resource zone, not an ecological preserve administered by humans, not a cultural party represented by one speaker, and not a route problem. The compact would recognize Parliament relation as living procedure: faction, basin, witness, refusal, repair, care, warning, and silence. Humans could not demand a simplified counterpart for ease of enforcement.

Vela whispered, "Our law can barely hold that."

Third-Voice's pressure path beat once.

"Then law stretches or tears," Here said.

No one softened it.

The third clause nearly broke the room.

Emergency rescue.

Humans needed it named. Orison bodies needed it fenced. Kestrel Minor hung over the chamber, alive and uninvited, proof of care and danger both. If the compact created no rescue relation, humans would send ships anyway under the language of moral necessity. If the compact created a clean rescue obligation, Salt-Before-Shell's faction would see the human need become permanent leverage.

Care-passage proposed first.

"Living body in immediate danger may be aided before vote if delay would destroy body. Aid does not create access. Aid does not create gratitude debt. Aid does not reduce liability for why danger occurred."

Salt-Before-Shell answered, "Add: repeated emergency becomes pattern violation."

Rusk said, "Yes."

Deputy Haro entered the human equivalent. "No party may manufacture, tolerate, or predictably cause emergency conditions to obtain passage, mapping, repair, contact, or precedent."

The chamber warmed in several places.

Ren wrote:

RESCUE IS CARE UNDER LIMIT, NOT CORRIDOR BY CRISIS.

Third-Voice accepted the wording after the pressure path interrupted twice, once on care and once on crisis. The clause expanded to include third-party review by harmed witnesses after any emergency aid. The rescued body could survive without becoming argument.

The fourth clause was Oru-Kel's warning structure.

Pale Arc rhythms, boundary pulses, and nonhuman navigation patterns would not be treated as natural background to be modeled around human traffic. They would hold authority inside their own relation. When a warning rhythm entered the compact field, route planning stopped until the rhythm's meaning was heard by those able to hear it. Ignorance could not be used as permission.

"Humans will ask who certifies the rhythm," Vela said.

Oru-Kel's plates lifted. "The rhythm."

"They will not accept that."

"Then they are not ready to move."

Lael leaned over the draft. "We can create witness panels, but the panel cannot outrank the event."

That became the clause: witnesses could help humans receive warning; they could not convert warning into advisory data that humans remained free to override.

Rusk was quiet for a long time after that.

Ren knew why. Every private corridor model he had shown relied on override categories. Human systems loved warnings as long as warnings came with ranked exceptions.

The fifth clause belonged to refusal.

This was where the relation-vote became machinery. For any proposed action, each affected Orison relation could enter its position into the braid: joins, permits without joining, refuses and remains in protected relation, refuses and withdraws from implementation, delays for repair before speech, or damaged witness relation. No implementation could proceed while a damaged witness relation remained unheard. No refusal in protected relation could be counted as consent, absence, hostility, or breach. No permitting strand could be expanded beyond its named action.

Vela stared at the clause as if it might bite. "This will make the compact slow."

Here answered, "Fast killed."

The room held the two words.

Vela bowed her head. "Yes."

The sixth clause was Ren's, though she tried to avoid admitting it.

Records.

Static text would not be enough. The compact had to include live pressure witnesses, heat marks, repair-status indicators, minority basin responses, translation refusals, and explicit blanks where no safe translation existed. Human copies had to preserve the fact of unavailable meaning rather than replacing it with summary. Any summary had to be marked as operational convenience, not the compact itself.

"Human courts hate unavailable meaning," Haro said.

Ren did not look up. "They can learn to hate accurately."

Lael made a sound that might have been a laugh if the chamber had not been so tired.

Third-Voice's pressure path beat approval. Not speech. Approval was too simple. It was more like the draft had failed less badly than expected.

The seventh clause was liability.

Aven's name was not placed in the compact. That would have made the text too small. Instead the clause described unauthorized route testing, concealed probes, private wake generation, emergency manufacture, successor evasion, data laundering, and the use of rescue events as later access arguments. It required logs, restitution, hearing access for harmed bodies, and temporary suspension of related human requests when investigation showed pattern risk.

Salt-Before-Shell wanted suspension to be permanent.

Lael wanted review.

The chamber nearly returned to fracture.

Third-Voice let the pressure path interrupt them both.

Ren waited for speech.

None came.

Here translated from heat instead. "Do not make punishment pretend repair."

Salt-Before-Shell's plates closed.

Lael exhaled.

The clause changed: suspension would last until harmed relations accepted that risk had been altered, not until human authorities declared discipline complete. It was neither automatic forgiveness nor endless symbolic punishment. It required change that touched the risk itself.

Rusk said, "That is harder than a permanent ban."

Salt-Before-Shell looked at him. "Good."

The eighth clause was future contact.

The compact would not open the Shoals. It would not close them absolutely. It would establish narrow, revisable relation fields for communication, warning exchange, limited relief, non-extractive scholarship, and mutually requested repair knowledge. Each field required a separate relation-vote. None created precedent for the others. No field could be sold, inherited, securitized, or used as collateral.

Vela added, with visible satisfaction, "No route derivative instruments."

Most of the chamber did not understand the phrase.

Rusk did, and winced.

"Keep it," he said.

The ninth clause was duration.

Humans wanted dates.

Orison wanted cycles, repair states, warning seasons, body changes, and memory thresholds.

The compromise was not a compromise. The compact would be reviewed at intervals measured by both human time and Orison condition. If either measure arrived, review began. If harm changed sooner, review began. If silence entered damaged witness relation, review began. Expiration would not erase obligations already created by harm.

By then the central basin was crowded with clauses, currents, pressure beats, heat marks, and side annotations. It looked impossible.

Ren loved it less now. That was a good sign. A draft that could survive contact with use had to become inconvenient to its makers.

Lael asked for the text to be read back.

Third-Voice began.

Two speaking paths carried words. The third path interrupted with pressure whenever the words tried to become smoother than the relation underneath. Vela adjusted human phrasing. Oru-Kel rejected three verbs. Care-passage added limits around rescue touch. Here restored minority heat to clauses where the draft had cooled into abstraction. Salt-Before-Shell removed every hint that saving Kestrel Minor had changed withdrawal's stance.

Rusk contributed only when asked or when human evasion was hiding in a technical phrase.

At the end, the draft did not look like peace.

It looked like a way not to lie while remaining close enough to harm each other less.

Lael placed her hand over the human display but did not sign.

"This is not ready."

"No," Third-Voice said.

"But it is draft."

"Yes."

Salt-Before-Shell moved one limb through the refusal strand, not entering a new vote, only reminding everyone where he remained.

"Draft with teeth," he said.

Here warmed. "Draft with memory."

Oru-Kel clicked. "Draft with warning."

Care-passage dimmed and brightened. "Draft with hands restrained."

Rusk said, "Draft with consequences."

Ren looked at the impossible basin and wrote the sentence that would head the working copy:

THE SHOALS COMPACT DRAFT: A LIVING AGREEMENT FOR LIMITED RELATION UNDER MEMORY, REFUSAL, WARNING, CARE, AND REPAIR.

Third-Voice's changed silence beat once beneath it.

Then the dry chain asked the smallest question and exposed the largest wound.

PARTIES?

The word appeared alone on the outer glass. No threat, no pressure line, no carrier deadline. Just a field that every human treaty packet required before anything else could be stored.

Salt-Before-Shell closed his mouth plates.

Lael shut her eyes.

Vela whispered, "Of course."

Ren looked at the compact draft and saw the trap. If they wrote humans and Orison, the draft would create the simplified counterpart it had spent nine clauses refusing. If they wrote Parliament, the minority basin, damaged witness relations, care-passage, boundary warning, and withdrawal bodies became subfunctions of a named institution. If they wrote no parties, human archives would file the draft as unactionable philosophy until some emergency office replaced it with a usable lie.

Rusk said, "Covered participants?"

The pressure path struck once.

Hungry.

He corrected himself before anyone else did. "Too clean. It makes everyone a procedural object."

Here warmed. "Relation participants with named limits."

Vela tried it on the human panel:

RELATION PARTICIPANTS WITH NAMED LIMITS.

The phrase resisted storage. The field wanted party names, registration identifiers, jurisdiction, signature capacity. Vela watched the red errors multiply and did not delete the phrase.

Lael said, "The compact can name entry conditions instead of total parties."

Third-Voice's blue-white path brightened. "Say."

Lael spoke carefully. "Any human entity, successor, beneficiary, contractor, carrier, relief body, archive, court, military office, research body, or market instrument that seeks operational benefit from Shoals relation enters the compact only for the request it makes and the harms it inherits."

Rusk added, "And cannot transfer that relation as property."

Ren wrote:

HUMAN ENTRY CONDITION: NO HUMAN ENTITY ENTERS AS OWNER OF ACCESS. EACH ENTERS ONLY WITHIN A NAMED REQUEST, ITS HARM HISTORY, ITS BENEFICIARIES, ITS SUCCESSORS, ITS CONTRACTORS, ITS MARKET EFFECTS, AND ITS STOP CONDITIONS. RELATION MAY NOT BE SOLD, PLEDGED, SECURITIZED, ASSIGNED, OR TREATED AS ROUTE PROPERTY.

The chamber warmed in hard, cautious places.

Salt-Before-Shell said, "Orison entry condition."

The room became quieter.

Third-Voice did not answer first. Care-passage did not. Oru-Kel did not.

The protected minority basin warmed, not as answer but as warning: do not make us into a party.

Here finally spoke. "No Orison body enters all. Each relation enters by affectedness."

Vela frowned. "Affectedness is not a legal capacity."

"Then legal capacity is too small," Oru-Kel said.

Ren wrote:

ORISON ENTRY CONDITION: NO ORISON RELATION ENTERS AS TOTAL REPRESENTATIVE OF THE SHOALS. AFFECTED RELATIONS ENTER BY TOUCH, COST, WARNING, CARE, REFUSAL, REPAIR, MEMORY, SILENCE, OR CHOSEN PARTICIPATION. NO ENTRY BY ONE RELATION BINDS AN UNTOUCHED RELATION AS CONSENT.

Third-Voice's pressure path beat twice. The second beat hurt Ren's teeth.

Care-passage added, "Untouched may become touched later."

Ren added:

UNTOUCHED DOES NOT MEAN IRRELEVANT FOREVER; IT MEANS NOT YET ENTERED WITHOUT ITS OWN CONDITION.

The dry chain field still complained.

PARTIES REQUIRED.

Deputy Haro looked exhausted. "The packet will not validate."

Lael stared at the error. "Then the packet receives a failure note naming why validation fails."

Haro typed:

VALIDATION FAILURE: STANDARD PARTY FIELD CANNOT REPRESENT RELATION PARTICIPANTS WITH NAMED LIMITS WITHOUT MATERIAL DISTORTION.

The red errors remained. The chamber accepted them.

Ren realized the draft had acquired an honest scar before it even left the room.

They wrote:

ARCHIVE SCAR: STANDARD PARTY FIELD FAILS. FAILURE PRESERVED AS PART OF RECORD; DO NOT REPAIR BY SUBSTITUTING NEAREST PARTY CATEGORY.

The title held less elegantly now.

Better.

For once, the title held.

Chapter 57: No Signature Owns the Water

The signature problem arrived wearing a clerk's face.

His name was Pell, and he appeared on the east display with the flat patience of someone who had survived too many treaty rooms by believing in forms more than people. He was not hostile. That made him more dangerous. Hostility announced itself and could be answered. Procedure entered as furniture.

"For external recognition," Pell said, "the compact requires a signing authority."

No one in the chamber responded.

Pell continued because silence, in his world, meant the form had not yet been completed. "The human side can accept layered signatures from administrative, relief, scientific, and route safety offices. The Shoals side needs a counterpart signature or seal identifying the bound party."

Third-Voice's pressure path beat once.

The clerk looked down at data he could not interpret. "I am receiving an anomaly."

"You are receiving an objection," Lael said.

Pell blinked. "Understood. Please identify the objecting party."

The chamber changed temperature.

Ren closed her eyes for half a breath.

Lael's voice stayed level. "That is the objection."

Pell did not understand. He was trying. The effort showed in the small contractions around his eyes. He had likely been told this compact was unusual, politically delicate, culturally complex, biologically nonstandard. Those warnings had not prepared him for a room in which the request for a name could perform harm.

Vela stepped in before Salt-Before-Shell could make the exchange terminal.

"The compact cannot designate the Shoals as a singular bound party," she said. "It binds specific relations and procedures under Parliament process."

"A process cannot sign," Pell said.

Oru-Kel clicked. "Then your signing is too small."

Pell looked at Lael again, seeking the human who could translate the unreasonable thing into something fileable.

Lael did not rescue him.

Rusk spoke from the witness rail. "Pell, if we require a counterpart signature, we recreate the ownership premise the draft rejects."

"Recognition offices will ask who can be held accountable."

Here warmed the protected minority basin. "Those who act."

"I need a legal answer," Pell said.

Ren wrote the sentence before anyone else could turn it softer:

ACCOUNTABILITY FOLLOWS ACTION, NOT OWNERSHIP OF THE SHOALS.

Third-Voice accepted the line with two voices and one pressure beat.

The signature debate split into channels after that. Human officials wanted enforceable marks. Orison factions wanted no mark that could be mistaken for a body handing itself over. Lael wanted recognition strong enough to block private evasion. Salt-Before-Shell wanted every human page to begin with the statement that no signature owned the water. Oru-Kel wanted warning rhythms to outrank filing order. Vela wanted an archive format that would not be destroyed by the first court clerk who mistook living relation for corrupted attachment.

Ren wanted sleep.

She got clause work instead.

The first rejected solution was a Parliament seal.

It failed immediately. The visual mockup, produced by Pell's office without malice, showed a stylized basin circled by ten marks. It was elegant, simple, exportable, and false. The chamber recoiled from it as if it smelled of rot.

"It makes us emblem," Here said.

"It makes refusal decorative," Salt-Before-Shell added.

Pell deleted the mockup.

The second rejected solution was a rotating authorized witness list. That failed because names changed, bodies changed, relations changed, and human systems would inevitably treat omission as lack of standing. The third was a technical registry of compact participants. That failed because participation was not identity. The fourth was a jurisdictional map. No one let Pell finish explaining it.

"No maps as authority," Oru-Kel said.

"It was only--"

"No."

Pell stopped.

Ren respected him for that. Small mercy, but real.

Third-Voice finally proposed a form.

Not signature.

Trace.

The compact would carry human signatures only on human obligations. Beside them, instead of an Orison counterpart signature, the document would contain relation traces generated by the Parliament process at the time of adoption: heat marks from protected minority basins, pressure witness from Third-Voice's changed path, care-passage consent limits, warning rhythm references, refusal strands, and the explicit absence of any totalizing Shoals seal.

Pell stared at the diagram. "This is not a signature."

"Correct," Third-Voice said.

"Recognition systems will mark the compact incomplete."

"Then recognition systems lie."

Lael leaned toward the display. "Pell, can we create an instrument category for non-possessive counterpart trace?"

Pell looked physically pained.

"Not quickly."

"Can we create a provisional filing under emergency interspecies procedure?"

"That procedure is for temporary medical and quarantine arrangements."

Care-passage brightened with sudden interest.

Lael saw it too. "Does it require a singular counterpart signature?"

Pell read. His eyes moved fast. "It requires responsible human officers and attached nonhuman condition records."

Rusk's head lifted.

Vela whispered, "Condition records."

Salt-Before-Shell narrowed every visible seam. "Do not make us quarantine."

"No," Lael said. "We use the door without accepting its name."

Here warmed. "Dangerous."

"Yes."

Ren wrote:

HUMAN FILING MAY USE EXISTING EMERGENCY PROCEDURE ONLY IF THE COMPACT STATES THAT THE PROCEDURE NAME DOES NOT DEFINE ORISON STATUS.

Third-Voice's pressure path beat twice. Too smooth. Not enough.

Ren revised:

HUMAN FILING MAY USE EXISTING EMERGENCY PROCEDURE AS A TEMPORARY CARRIER. THE CARRIER DOES NOT NAME, CLASSIFY, CONTAIN, MEDICALIZE, QUARANTINE, OR OWN ORISON RELATION.

The pressure path quieted.

Pell looked as if his career had become a corridor with no walls. "That might be fileable."

"Might," Oru-Kel echoed with obvious dislike.

"Might is honest," Vela said.

The compact gained a filing clause: human signatures were admissions of human obligation, not acquisition of reciprocal property rights. Orison relation traces were binding conditions on the use of any human permission arising from the compact. The absence of a single Orison signature was not defect, gap, reservation, or delay. It was an operative term.

Pell repeated that last sentence slowly. "The absence is an operative term."

"Yes," Ren said.

"Our validators will reject it."

"Then attach a validator override."

"Those require authority."

Lael raised her hand. "Use mine."

Rusk said, "Use mine as technical liability witness."

Haro added, "Use mine for emergency procedure chain."

Vela hesitated, then said, "Use mine for archive exception."

Pell entered each name. The human side of the compact grew heavier, not with power but with exposure. That was the correct direction. Humans had built the systems that could not hold the relation. Humans would have to bear the awkwardness of making those systems stretch.

Salt-Before-Shell watched the names accumulate. "Many human marks."

"Yes," Lael said.

"No Orison mark."

"No owning mark."

"But relation trace."

"Yes."

He turned toward the central basin. "Show trace."

Third-Voice assembled it.

The relation trace did not look like a seal. It looked like weather held in a page: heat, pressure, interruption, refusal, warning, care limits, damaged witness, and space deliberately left unoccupied. It could not be printed correctly. It could only be referenced, stored, and reactivated under conditions the compact named.

Pell's display tried to thumbnail it and failed.

For the first time, the clerk smiled faintly. "That is going to upset document control."

"Good," said half the chamber in different ways.

The pro-contact merchants entered a protest. They wanted some mark that would reassure exchange partners that agreements were reliable. Their protest stayed visible. Under the new vote form, it could not be mocked or erased. The draft had to answer it.

Care-passage proposed language:

Reliability comes from named limits, not from pretending limits do not exist.

The merchants accepted that only after adding:

Partners may refuse relation if limits make exchange impossible.

Salt-Before-Shell surprised everyone by saying, "Keep."

Ren looked up.

He did not look back at her. "If humans can leave when relation too hard, they have less excuse to make relation false."

Rusk said quietly, "That may be the most enforceable sentence in the compact."

"Do not admire it," Salt-Before-Shell said.

Rusk shut his mouth.

The signature section became the longest part of the draft so far, which would have embarrassed old diplomats. It pleased Ren in a tired, bitter way. The place where treaties usually performed certainty had become the place where uncertainty was bound most explicitly.

Pell asked one final question.

"Who, then, can terminate the compact?"

The chamber went still.

Vela muttered, "There it is."

Human agreements loved termination clauses. They were exit hatches, threat tools, housekeeping. In the Shoals, termination could become abandonment, breach, or attempted erasure of harm history. No single Orison body could end the relation for all. No human office could declare obligations gone because policy changed.

Third-Voice let the question sit until it became uncomfortable enough to be useful.

Then the changed pressure path beat.

Here translated first. "Relation can close. Memory cannot."

Oru-Kel added, "Routes can end. Warnings remain."

Care-passage said, "Care fields can cease when bodies safe. Liability remains until repair changes risk."

Salt-Before-Shell said, "Refusal remains even if compact dies."

Lael shaped it into clause language:

Any party may cease its own future participation through the relation-vote process. No cessation erases harm history, accrued obligations, warning records, liability for prior action, or the standing of refusals already entered. The compact may become inactive. It cannot make itself never to have existed.

Pell typed for a long time.

"That is fileable," he said at last. "Ugly, but fileable."

Ren had never heard a better blessing from a clerk.

Third-Voice asked the chamber to review the signature trace one more time.

Human names stood on one side, each tied to a narrow obligation. Orison relation trace stood on the other, refusing to become a counterpart thing. Between them, no line said equality. No line said ownership. No line said peace.

There was only a binding field where action would have consequences.

Salt-Before-Shell touched the absence at the center of the trace.

"This empty place," he said. "Name it."

Ren waited for Third-Voice.

Third-Voice waited for her.

She understood, reluctantly.

She wrote:

NO SIGNATURE OWNS THE WATER.

The chamber accepted the line.

The press office saw it immediately and did what press offices did.

Pell's display flashed:

PUBLIC SUMMARY SUGGESTION: NO SIGNATURE OWNS THE WATER.

Ren said, "Absolutely not."

Pell looked startled. "It is the filed sentence."

"Filed is not public summary."

Lael's tired eyes sharpened. "If that becomes the headline, humans will treat it as elegant mutual respect and skip the machinery under it."

Rusk added, "Routeholder desks will treat it as non-ownership waiver while looking for operational loopholes."

Salt-Before-Shell's mouth plates opened in disgust. "Pretty words become empty bowl."

Ren wrote:

FILING SENTENCE IS NOT PUBLIC SLOGAN, WAIVER, MUTUAL-RESPECT SUMMARY, ROUTE DISCLAIMER, OR SUBSTITUTE FOR TRACE CONDITIONS.

Pell removed the summary suggestion.

The system generated another:

PUBLIC SUMMARY SUGGESTION: LIMITED RELATION COMPACT ESTABLISHES ACCOUNTABLE ACCESS FRAMEWORK.

This time even Vela groaned.

"Access framework?" she said. "It learned nothing."

Third-Voice's pressure path struck once.

Hungry.

Ren wrote before the room wasted more strength:

NO PUBLIC SUMMARY MAY USE ACCESS AS THE GOVERNING NOUN. THE COMPACT GOVERNS RELATION UNDER LIMIT; ACCESS IS ONLY A POSSIBLE, NARROW, REVOCABLE CONSEQUENCE OF SPECIFIC RELATION-VOTE CONDITIONS.

Pell stared at the sentence, then copied it into the filing constraints.

"Document control will ask for a public-facing description," he said.

Lael answered, "Then give them a warning label."

The chamber considered that.

Oru-Kel's plates lifted. "Warning label can be true."

Ren wrote:

PUBLIC DESCRIPTION, IF REQUIRED: THIS FILING RECORDS A LIMITED RELATION PROCESS WITH ACTIVE REFUSAL, HARM HISTORY, WARNING AUTHORITY, CARE LIMITS, DAMAGED WITNESS CONDITIONS, AND NO TRANSFERABLE ACCESS RIGHT.

The central basin accepted the line with no warmth, which was exactly right. It was not beautiful. It was hard to misuse quickly.

Pell attached it as the first visible sentence in the filing section, where every human office would have to trip over it before finding the forms beneath.

Chapter 58: Salt-Before-Shell Remains Apart

Salt-Before-Shell refused the draft three times before he let it continue.

The first refusal came after the signature section, when Lael asked whether the withdrawal faction would enter protected relation for compact adoption. The question was careful. It used the new form. It did not ask for agreement. It did not ask for forgiveness. It did not ask him to stand with anyone.

He refused anyway.

"Too soon."

The chamber accepted the refusal.

That changed its weight.

In the old vote form, refusal would have become obstruction, crisis, or leverage. In the new one it became visible relation: not assent, not absence, not attack. The draft paused around it without collapsing. Human displays showed a red interruption until Vela manually changed the color to a dark salt gray after three Orison bodies recoiled.

"Never use emergency red for refusal," Here said.

Vela corrected the archive standard immediately.

The second refusal came when care-passage proposed that withdrawal bodies might participate in future rescue review panels.

Salt-Before-Shell's plates opened like a wound.

"You want our rescue to become office."

"No," care-passage answered. "We want harmed refusal present when rescue becomes argument."

"Then name it without us."

"Cannot."

"Then do not have panel."

Care-passage dimmed. The chamber waited.

Ren expected Lael to intervene. She did not. The compact had taught her restraint by punishing every earlier elegance.

Finally the changed withdrawal body moved in its cradle.

Not far. It was still weak, still shaped differently from before the drag current. But it sent a small pressure across the basin edge. Third-Voice received it through the changed path and held the chamber still until meaning could arrive without being forced.

"It says," Third-Voice translated, "do not draft around the wound to spare the one who hates seeing it."

Salt-Before-Shell shut every mouth plate.

The sentence struck him harder than any human argument could have.

No one looked away. Looking away would have made pity. Pity would have made story. The changed body had forbidden that already.

Salt-Before-Shell remained closed for a long time.

Then he said, "Panel may call withdrawal relation. It may not require attendance. It may not punish absence. It may not cite absence as consent."

Care-passage accepted at once.

Ren wrote the amendment:

WITHDRAWAL RELATION MAY BE CALLED INTO RESCUE REVIEW BUT NOT COMPELLED, SUBSTITUTED, OR INTERPRETED THROUGH ABSENCE.

The third refusal came near the end of implementation.

Haro had assembled the human obligations list: route moratorium pending compact adoption, emergency filing carrier, liability disclosure for Ledger Spar, technical halt on private wake tests, archive exception requests, training requirements for captains entering any Shoals communication radius, and provisional recognition of relation traces.

It was the most human-looking part of the draft because humans had the most machinery to restrain.

Salt-Before-Shell studied it with distaste.

"This makes humans better at coming."

Lael answered carefully. "It makes humans easier to stop when they come wrong."

"Better stopping still begins with coming."

"Yes."

That yes mattered. Ren saw the chamber register it. Lael did not pretend regulation was absence. She did not pretend safer contact was no contact. She had learned at least that much.

Salt-Before-Shell entered refusal and withdraws from implementation for three compact fields: exchange lanes, non-extractive scholarship, and route safety training. The braid accepted the entries. The fields remained available to other relations under limits, but withdrawal would not build them, staff them, bless them, or be counted in their legitimacy.

Then he entered refuses and remains in protected relation for rescue review, harm history, warning authority, and liability suspension.

The distinction was sharp enough to draw blood.

Vela asked, "May I read back how the draft now sees withdrawal?"

"No," Salt-Before-Shell said.

Vela stopped.

Third-Voice's pressure path beat once.

Salt-Before-Shell looked toward it. "You think no is old reflex."

Third-Voice answered, "No. I think no is tired."

The chamber went still.

Salt-Before-Shell did not deny it.

After a moment he said to Vela, "Read."

Vela read without smoothing.

"The withdrawal faction refuses the compact's contact-expanding fields and withdraws from their implementation. The withdrawal faction remains in protected relation to fields governing harm history, rescue review, warning authority, refusal integrity, liability, and the non-ownership of Shoals water. Withdrawal participation may not be represented as compact endorsement. Withdrawal refusal may not be represented as abandonment of affected bodies."

Salt-Before-Shell listened with all plates open.

"Add: no forgiveness."

Vela added it.

"Add: no reconciliation ceremony."

Vela added it.

"Add: no human educational material may use our participation to teach that anger becomes cooperation."

Pell, still present on the side display, looked alarmed. "Educational material?"

Rusk closed his eyes briefly. "Yes. Add it."

Lael said, "Add it broadly. Public communication, training, press material, institutional reporting."

Ren wrote:

NO PUBLIC OR INSTITUTIONAL ACCOUNT MAY REPRESENT WITHDRAWAL PROTECTED RELATION AS FORGIVENESS, RECONCILIATION, MORAL CONVERSION, OR PROOF THAT HARMED PARTIES SHOULD BECOME COOPERATIVE.

The protected minority basin warmed hard enough to make the glass sweat.

Here said, "That clause should apply beyond withdrawal."

It did.

The compact's communication section grew teeth. Harmed relation could not be converted into moral lesson without consent. Survival could not be used as institutional redemption. Rescue could not become propaganda. Anger did not owe anyone a beautiful ending.

Ren felt something in her chest loosen and hurt at the same time.

Salt-Before-Shell turned toward Rusk.

"Your people will hate this."

"Some will."

"You?"

Rusk did not answer quickly.

"I will fail at it if I am not watched," he said.

That was the first answer Salt-Before-Shell seemed to find tolerable.

"Then be watched."

"I will."

"Do not enjoy being watched."

Rusk almost smiled and wisely did not. "I will not."

The chamber moved from refusal into maintenance. That was less dramatic and more important. Clauses were checked against each relation strand. Places where withdrawal remained apart had to be operationally real. If a future compact meeting concerned exchange lanes only, withdrawal could refuse notice. If a route training module cited Parliament legitimacy, it had to name which relations participated and which remained apart. If human authorities claimed compact adoption as Orison consent to contact, the relation trace would contradict them at the first line.

Pell kept saying, "This is unusual," until Haro muted him by accident or mercy.

Near the end, the changed withdrawal body asked to enter its own relation.

Care-passage hesitated. "You are still in repair."

The body pulsed.

Third-Voice translated, "Repair does not erase standing."

No one challenged that.

The body entered damaged witness relation to the rescue clause and protected relation to the communication clause. It entered no position on exchange, route training, scholarship, or future lanes. Its record included the statement it had already given:

DO NOT MAKE MY CHANGE A BRIDGE.

Ren watched Salt-Before-Shell read the line.

For one moment his plates moved as if grief might escape as sound.

It did not.

"Good," he said.

That was all.

Lael asked whether the draft could proceed to provisional adoption review.

Salt-Before-Shell did not answer for the withdrawal faction immediately. He crossed the chamber slowly, away from the central braid and toward the outer water where the glass showed the dark beyond Parliament lights. No one followed.

Ren understood then that apart was not only political. It was spatial, bodily, necessary. The compact could preserve relation, but it could not remove the need for distance from those who had made every closeness dangerous.

When Salt-Before-Shell returned, he carried a small quantity of dark salt in one limb.

He placed it beside the relation trace, not on it.

"Withdrawal remains apart," he said. "Apart in record. Apart in work. Apart in grief. Near in stopping harm. Near in warning. Near in rescue only when rescue does not become chain."

Third-Voice held the statement with care.

"Enter relation?" it asked.

Salt-Before-Shell opened all plates.

"Refuses and remains."

The braid accepted him.

It did not brighten.

It did not heal.

Vela started to mark the relation as present.

The protected minority basin warmed sharply.

She stopped before anyone spoke. "Present is too simple."

"Yes," Salt-Before-Shell said.

She tried again:

WITHDRAWAL RELATION: APART / NEAR ONLY UNDER NAMED HARM CONDITIONS.

The braid accepted the phrase, but Third-Voice's pressure path beat once.

"Operational," it said through the two speech paths.

Vela added an implementation table that looked ugly enough to be useful. Apart meant no default notice for contact-expanding meetings. Apart meant no obligation to review exchange training unless the training cited withdrawal or touched harm history. Apart meant no archive request could summon withdrawal testimony as background context. Apart meant rescue review could call, not compel. Apart meant human agencies had to mark decisions made without withdrawal participation as incomplete with respect to withdrawal, not blocked by withdrawal.

Ren wrote the governing line:

APARTNESS IS AN OPERATIVE CONDITION, NOT SYMBOLIC DISTANCE. SYSTEMS MUST RECORD WHEN WITHDRAWAL IS UNTOUCHED, CALLED, DECLINED, PRESENT UNDER LIMIT, OR NEAR UNDER HARM CONDITION.

Pell unmuted himself long enough to say, "That creates five new status states."

Haro muted him again.

Lael almost smiled.

Salt-Before-Shell did not, but one tired seam along his shoulder loosened.

"Five is not enough," Here said from the basin.

"No," Ren said. "But it is more than one."

The chamber accepted that as temporary, which was the only honest form of acceptance left.

It held.

Chapter 59: Oru-Kel Sends the Warning Forward

Oru-Kel refused to let the compact end inside the Shoals.

"If warning stops here," he said, "humans will call it local."

No one disputed him.

The chamber had seen that habit too many times in too many forms. Local anomaly. Regional hazard. Species-specific concern. Cultural objection. Environmental sensitivity. Each phrase was a small container built to keep a warning from touching the next profitable plan.

Oru-Kel moved to the outer basin and opened the Pale Arc record.

The water darkened.

This time the rhythm did not arrive as distant evidence. It entered with the authority the draft had just recognized: not advisory data, not myth, not navigational color, but warning with standing. The chamber lights dimmed to keep human eyes from making it spectacle. Ren felt the pattern through her feet before she could see it.

Slow arc.

Pressure fold.

Absence where travel wanted to make a line.

Then the second pulse, older and colder, the one Oru-Kel had carried since the boundary first spoke through him.

Lael drew a breath. "This is not only about the corridor."

"No," Oru-Kel said.

Vela's face had gone pale. "The same interference geometry appears in Ash Belt debris forecasts."

Rusk turned toward her. "How close?"

"Not identical. Related enough that I would not ignore it if I wanted to sleep again."

Third-Voice's pressure path beat once.

Ren wrote:

PALE ARC WARNING HAS EXTRA-SHOALS RELEVANCE. COMPACT RECORD MUST ROUTE IT FORWARD WITHOUT CONVERTING IT INTO HUMAN PROPERTY.

Oru-Kel accepted the first sentence and clicked doubt at the second.

"Forward to whom?" Lael asked.

That was the hard part.

Human systems loved destinations. Send warning to office, fleet, archive, agency, council. The Meridian Cycle had taught Ren that every destination became a filter, and every filter learned to protect itself. The Gate at Kestrel Falling had hidden urgency inside military caution. The Reef of Glass had turned survival into jurisdiction. The Orchard of Engines had made food political. The Ash Belt was already waiting somewhere ahead in the human map, full of people who would be told too late that debris could think in patterns humans had not named.

Oru-Kel did not know those books as books.

He knew the shape.

"Warning must move along relation, not chain of command," he said.

Vela looked at Ren. "Can we do that?"

Ren answered honestly. "Badly."

"Badly may be more accurate than cleanly," Lael said.

They built a warning packet that was not a packet.

First, the compact record would include the Pale Arc rhythm in protected form, requiring reactivation through trained witness conditions rather than static extraction. Second, human recipients could not separate the rhythm from the harm history, refusal clauses, and non-ownership language that gave it meaning. Third, any operational use of the warning had to preserve Orison standing: the rhythm could be heeded, but not mined, patented, simulated for route advantage, or stripped of relation.

Pell, still trapped in the side display by duty and perhaps curiosity, said, "That will make rapid response difficult."

Oru-Kel answered, "Rapid theft is not response."

Pell typed the line into his notes before realizing it was not a clause.

Ren almost liked him.

Haro opened channels to three human nodes: an intersystem hazard archive, a relief fleet coordination office, and a scientific warning desk that Vela trusted only because she had once seen it publish an inconvenient result without waiting for permission. Rusk added a fourth: a routeholder compliance office with enough enemies inside private shipping to leak obstruction if the warning was buried.

Lael added a fifth and did not explain it.

Ren saw the destination label anyway.

Moonwake civic listening post.

The name sat on the screen like a future door.

Third-Voice's pressure path beat hard enough to rattle the translation rack.

Here warmed. "Too far?"

Third-Voice answered with two voices. "Far warnings become stories. Stories become tools. Tools cut."

"Then why send?" Rusk asked.

Oru-Kel turned on him. "Because not sending also cuts."

That ended the objection.

The warning packet needed a carrier phrase, something human systems could route without pretending to understand. Vela proposed Technical Hazard Advisory. The basin rejected it. Haro proposed Interspecies Navigation Warning. Oru-Kel hated navigation. Pell proposed Compact-Attached Standing Notice. Nobody knew what that meant, including Pell.

Ren waited until the phrases exhausted themselves.

"Call it a carried warning," she said.

The chamber listened.

"Not an advisory. Not an alert. Not an asset. A warning carried by those not entitled to own it."

Oru-Kel's plates lifted.

Third-Voice accepted the wording.

The carried warning took shape:

PALE ARC CARRIED WARNING: BOUNDARY RHYTHMS OBSERVED IN SHOALS WATER INDICATE THAT HUMAN ROUTE, DEBRIS, WAKE, OR EXTRACTION SYSTEMS MAY DISTURB RELATIONAL PATTERNS BEYOND THE SHOALS. RECEIVING BODIES MUST HALT ASSUMPTIONS OF EMPTY SPACE, CONSULT HARM HISTORY, AND TREAT NONHUMAN WARNING AS STANDING CONDITION RATHER THAN OPTIONAL CONTEXT.

The pressure path interrupted on empty space.

Ren revised:

RECEIVING BODIES MUST HALT ASSUMPTIONS THAT APPARENTLY EMPTY SPACE IS AVAILABLE SPACE.

The pressure settled.

Oru-Kel added his own mark: a rhythm reference no human text could summarize. It curved through the packet like a dark vein. Vela attached translation limits. Lael attached obligations. Rusk attached liability language for any office that received the warning and suppressed it. Haro attached delivery receipts that could not be quietly deleted without leaving audit scars.

Salt-Before-Shell watched from apart.

"You send our chamber into human mouths," he said.

Oru-Kel answered, "I send warning through teeth."

"Teeth break things."

"So does silence."

The withdrawal leader considered that.

"Add refusal trace," he said.

Oru-Kel looked surprised.

Salt-Before-Shell bared one plate. "If warning goes without refusal, humans will call it help."

The chamber accepted this immediately.

A refusal trace joined the carried warning: the Shoals did not offer partnership by warning. The Shoals did not invite study by warning. The Shoals did not grant access by warning. The warning created obligation in the receiver, not entitlement.

Pell muttered, "This is the least convenient warning notice I have ever filed."

Lael said, "Good. Convenience is how it gets stolen."

The first delivery failed.

The hazard archive rejected the pressure attachment as unsupported format. Haro routed it again under emergency exception. It rejected the exception because the counterpart trace lacked a standard signature. Pell overrode the validator using Lael's authority, then Rusk's liability witness, then Vela's archive exception, then his own clerk credential at a level Ren suspected he was not supposed to use for interspecies compact materials.

"That may get reviewed," Pell said.

"Yes," Lael answered.

He sent it anyway.

The second delivery stalled at the relief fleet office until an operator opened a live line. She was older, with tired eyes and a scar across one cheek that pulled when she frowned.

"I am not authorized to accept nonstandard alien pressure data," she said.

Haro replied, "Are you authorized to ignore a carried warning attached to a compact liability notice?"

The operator read for six seconds.

"No," she said, and accepted it.

The third delivery vanished into the scientific warning desk and produced no immediate response. Vela cursed softly, then smiled when a receipt arrived from an individual researcher rather than the desk itself.

"It reached someone honest or reckless," she said.

"Difference?" Oru-Kel asked.

"Timing."

The fourth delivery, Rusk's compliance office, returned a request for clarification about commercial impact.

Rusk answered it himself:

Commercial impact is likely and irrelevant to the standing of the warning. Suppression or dilution increases liability.

He sent it before asking permission.

No one stopped him.

The fifth delivery, Moonwake, did not acknowledge for a long time.

The chamber waited.

Ren felt the whole book, though she would never call it that inside the record, lean toward the blank receipt line. Kestrel Falling, Glass Reef, Orchard, Basin, Belt, Bazaar, Shoals: each crisis had tried to remain itself and failed. They were not episodes. They were currents in the same dark water, touching before anyone had language for the touch.

At last the Moonwake listening post returned a narrow signal.

Not acceptance.

Not comprehension.

Only:

WARNING HEARD. CANNOT YET ANSWER. HOLDING SPACE.

Third-Voice's pressure path beat once.

Vela reached for the receipt field, then stopped. "If we record only heard, later systems may treat hearing as intake completion."

Oru-Kel's plates lifted. "Hearing is beginning."

Ren wrote:

WARNING HEARD DOES NOT MEAN WARNING PROCESSED, UNDERSTOOD, ACCEPTED, DISCHARGED, OR AVAILABLE FOR MODELING.

The Moonwake line remained open long enough for the sentence to transmit.

After seven seconds, the listening post replied:

CONFIRMED. HOLDING WITHOUT MODELING.

Rusk leaned forward. "Add no commercial derivative before the compliance office learns the phrase from someone worse."

Ren added:

NO RECEIVER MAY CONVERT THE CARRIED WARNING INTO PREDICTIVE PRODUCT, ROUTE OPTIMIZATION, INSURANCE FACTOR, SECURITY JUSTIFICATION, EXPLORATION CLAIM, OR COMMERCIAL DERIVATIVE WITHOUT VIOLATING THE WARNING'S STANDING CONDITIONS.

Pell looked up from his side display. "That is broader than most offices will accept."

Lael said, "It is exactly as broad as the theft will be."

The pressure path beat once, approving or at least failing to object.
