Haro attached the receiver obligations to all five delivery receipts. The hazard archive returned an automated complaint that non-modeling restrictions would reduce interoperability. Haro marked the complaint as evidence of attempted dilution and sent the mark back into the receipt chain.

The relief fleet operator read the new condition and said, "We can hold it as action constraint, not analysis product."

Care-passage brightened. "Good."

The scientific warning desk finally produced a second receipt, this one from an institutional account rather than the reckless individual.

ACCEPTED FOR REVIEW.

Vela added:

REVIEW MAY NOT REMOVE STANDING CONDITIONS.

The desk did not answer.

"It heard," Oru-Kel said. "It has not answered."

Ren recorded that distinction too.

Oru-Kel lowered his head.

"Enough?" Lael asked.

"No," he said.

Then, after a long moment:

"But carried."

Ren wrote the delivery record with care. The compact had not saved the future. It had refused to let the present pretend it ended at its own border.

Salt-Before-Shell moved back toward the outer dark.

"Now humans beyond us know we are inconvenient."

Rusk said, "Some will know."

"Make more know."

Lael looked at the carried warning receipts, then at the compact draft, then at the exhausted Parliament.

"We will."

Oru-Kel closed the Pale Arc record.

The rhythm did not leave.

It had entered the routes ahead.

Chapter 60: The Salt Parliament

The compact was not signed at dawn.

There was no dawn in the Parliament basin, only the long dimming and brightening of chamber light across water that remembered more kinds of time than humans could count. But the human clocks chose a morning, and because human reports needed a sentence, Pell's filing system would later say provisional adoption occurred at 06:13 station time.

Ren hated the neatness of it.

She left the time in the record anyway.

Accuracy was not the same as beauty.

The chamber gathered without ceremony. That was agreed first. No banners, no exchange of objects, no first photograph, no unity broadcast, no joint statement about a new era. Lael had drafted a public note so spare it looked almost rude:

The Shoals Compact has entered provisional relation. It creates limited obligations, preserves refusal, and does not open Shoals water.

Salt-Before-Shell removed the word entered and replaced it with begun.

The note became better.

Humans would dislike it. That also made it better.

Third-Voice occupied the central basin with two speaking paths and one changed pressure witness. Care-passage had placed the responsive salt strip in clear view. It had darkened twice during preparation and forced two delays, both because human systems tried to auto-summarize the relation trace into a filing abstract. Pell had personally disabled the summarizer after the second failure.

"I have never hated a convenience feature more," he said.

"Useful hatred," Oru-Kel answered.

Pell accepted that as praise, perhaps because he was tired.

Lael stood at the human rail. Haro stood beside her with the emergency filing chain open. Vela held the archive exception packet. Rusk stood behind them, not hidden, not central. Ren sat at the witness table with hands wrapped in compression cloth and the final record waiting.

Across the basin, the Orison relations held their positions.

Care-passage near the repair water.

Protected minority bodies around the warm basin.

Pro-contact merchants in restless color, their protest visible and still included.

Oru-Kel at the warning edge.

Salt-Before-Shell apart, dark salt beside him, withdrawal bodies arranged with space between them and everyone else.

The changed withdrawal body rested in its cradle, awake.

Third-Voice began the adoption review.

It did not read the entire compact. That would have flattered the words. Instead it passed through the living load points: harm history, emergency rescue under limit, warning authority, relation-vote with visible refusal, damaged witness, non-ownership signature trace, communication restraint, liability that followed action, carried warning, termination without erasure.

At each point, the pressure path beat or stayed still.

When it stayed still, the chamber waited anyway.

Ren wrote the waiting into the record.

Then came the relation entries.

Care-passage joined rescue limits, repair procedures, damaged witness protections, and communication restraint. It permitted without joining narrow exchange lanes and scholarship fields. It delayed for repair before speech on two technical appendices that had grown too human overnight.

Oru-Kel joined warning authority, carried warning, Pale Arc rhythm protection, and route halt conditions. He permitted without joining archive procedures. He refused any clause that let humans train around warnings by simulation alone.

The protected minority basin entered protected relation across the compact and damaged witness relation to all future route adjustments touching refuge zones. Here spoke one line:

"Warmth before motion."

Ren wrote it as operational principle.

The pro-contact merchants joined limited exchange, permitted scholarship, protested delay burdens, and accepted communication restraint after adding a note that honest hunger should remain visible. The Parliament let the note stand. Hunger hidden became theft. Hunger visible could be refused.

Then Salt-Before-Shell entered withdrawal relation exactly as revised.

Refuses contact-expanding fields.

Withdraws from their implementation.

Remains in protected relation to harm history, rescue review, warning authority, refusal integrity, liability, communication restraint, and non-ownership.

No forgiveness.

No reconciliation ceremony.

No use of anger as moral lesson.

The braid held.

No one applauded.

Lael entered the human obligations next. Her voice did not shake until the third line.

Human authorities accepted a route moratorium pending relation-vote review. Human emergency offices accepted that rescue did not create access. Human archives accepted non-possessive counterpart trace as operative term. Human signers accepted liability for successor entities deriving operational benefit. Human route offices accepted that warnings could halt motion without being converted into optional advisory data. Human public communications accepted limits on redemption narratives.

At the end, she added one line not in the prepared text.

"Human witnesses accept that this compact may make our systems look inadequate."

Third-Voice's pressure path beat once.

"Accepted," it said.

Rusk entered his liability witness. He did not make a speech. He attached the Ledger Spar logs, the private corridor model, the suppression chain, and the compliance warning he had sent forward. The compact took them without absolving him.

That seemed to steady him more than forgiveness would have.

Vela entered the archive exception and attached instructions for preserving unavailable meaning. She included three examples of things the archive must not do. The first was summarize pressure witness as sentiment. The second was render refusal in red emergency code. The third was crop silence.

"Crop silence?" Pell asked.

"Archivists crop everything eventually," Vela said.

Pell added the prohibition.

Haro entered the emergency filing carrier, the validator overrides, and the delivery receipts for the carried warning. Moonwake's line still read:

WARNING HEARD. CANNOT YET ANSWER. HOLDING SPACE.

Oru-Kel required it remain visible in the adoption record.

Then the chamber reached Ren.

"Human witness record," Third-Voice said.

Ren looked at the page. It was absurd to call it a page. It was text, pressure index, heat record, relation trace, missing translation, file exceptions, sensor disclaimers, and human language trying not to congratulate itself. Her hands hurt. Her mind felt rinsed in salt.

She had wanted, somewhere at the beginning of all this, to make a record good enough to be trusted.

Now she understood the record could only be good enough to be challenged correctly.

She stood.

"I witness that the compact is provisional, limited, and alive. I witness that refusal remains visible inside it. I witness that no rescue, injury, warning, or continued relation creates ownership. I witness that the Shoals have not become one party for human convenience. I witness that human systems are bound most strongly where they are least comfortable. I witness that this record is incomplete by design and must not be completed by force."

Her voice nearly failed.

She let it.

Third-Voice's pressure path held the failure without translating it.

Ren finished:

"I witness that the Parliament remains salt."

The chamber accepted the line.

Not as title.

As condition.

Pell executed the filing.

The first validator rejected it.

Everyone waited.

Pell overrode.

The second validator rejected the relation trace.

Pell overrode.

The third validator flagged the absence of counterpart signature as fatal.

Lael entered her authority. Haro entered the emergency chain. Vela entered archive exception. Rusk entered liability witness. The compact returned to the validator with the sentence in front:

NO SIGNATURE OWNS THE WATER.

The system stalled for twenty-seven seconds.

Then:

PROVISIONAL FILING ACCEPTED WITH EXCEPTIONS.

The exceptions list ran longer than the approval.

Care-passage brightened. "Accurate."

The human side exhaled too loudly.

The Orison side did not exhale at all.

Third-Voice asked whether any relation required immediate reopening.

The protected minority basin warmed, then cooled.

Oru-Kel's warning edge pulsed once toward the routes ahead.

The pro-contact merchants entered two future agenda items.

Care-passage scheduled repair review.

Salt-Before-Shell remained apart.

Then, without ceremony, he turned toward the changed withdrawal body.

"We leave," he said.

The body pulsed.

"Changed," Third-Voice translated.

"Yes," Salt-Before-Shell said.

"Present."

"Yes."

"Not bridge."

Salt-Before-Shell lowered one limb to the cradle edge. He did not touch without request. After a moment, the changed body extended a small current and met him.

"Not bridge," he said.

The withdrawal faction departed through a side waterway, not the ceremonial passage. Their dark salt remained beside the relation trace. No one moved it.

Lael watched them go.

"Did we succeed?" she asked.

Ren looked at the compact, the exceptions, the warnings, the refusal strands, the wounded mediator, the warmed minority basin, the human signatures standing where human discomfort belonged.

"No," she said.

Lael nodded slowly.

Ren added, "We began."

Third-Voice's two speech paths repeated the word in Orison forms Ren could not follow. The pressure path beat beneath them, not agreeing exactly, not refusing exactly, making the word carry more weight than hope.

Outside the chamber, human systems began to react. Messages stacked behind Haro's filters. Some were urgent. Some were angry. Some requested clarification in the thin, predatory tone of offices looking for loopholes. Pell's face vanished from the display and returned twice as new validators demanded his attention. Rusk received a notice from his former associates and deleted it unread after attaching it to the liability log.

Vela sent the archive packet and then sat on the floor.

Oru-Kel remained by the warning edge, listening past the Shoals.

Ren closed the witness record.

She did not mark it final.

The exception list kept growing after the acceptance line.

Pell's filing system named each exception in a polite administrative voice that made every wound sound like formatting:

NONSTANDARD COUNTERPART TRACE.

UNAVAILABLE PARTY FIELD.

LIVE PRESSURE CONDITION REQUIRED.

INCOMPLETE PUBLIC SUMMARY.

REFUSAL STRANDS REMAIN OPERATIVE.

DAMAGED WITNESS RELATION ACTIVE.

SIGNATURE ABSENCE OPERATIVE.

STANDARD ACCESS FIELD SUPPRESSED.

Ren copied the list into the chamber record and added:

EXCEPTIONS ARE NOT DEFECTS TO BE CURED WITHOUT RELATION-VOTE.

Pell, somewhere in the dry chain, saw the line and appended it to the filing notes before any validator could offer a repair wizard.

The first angry response arrived twelve seconds later.

ROUTEHOLDER COALITION: PROVISIONAL FILING CREATES UNCERTAINTY UNSUITABLE FOR COMMERCIAL RELIANCE.

Rusk laughed once, almost silently.

"Accurate," he said.

He entered the response into the liability log under evidence that the compact was already performing one of its functions.

The second response came from a public communications office:

REQUEST APPROVED SUMMARY FOR CIVILIAN REASSURANCE.

Lael looked at Ren.

Ren did not reopen the witness record. She opened a side pane and wrote:

NO REASSURANCE SUMMARY AVAILABLE. CIVILIANS MAY BE TOLD THAT LIMITED OBLIGATIONS HAVE BEGUN, REFUSAL REMAINS ACTIVE, SHOALS WATER IS NOT OPEN, AND WARNINGS CONTINUE.

Care-passage added, "Bodies needing care may ask through care channel."

Ren added it.

Salt-Before-Shell was already gone, but the dark salt beside the trace warmed faintly when the sentence did not mention gratitude.

The third response came from an oversight committee:

DOES PROVISIONAL RELATION INDICATE IMPROVED STABILITY?

Third-Voice's pressure path beat so hard the basin edge rippled.

Ren answered this one into the record, because it would return in a hundred forms if left hungry:

NO STABILITY CLAIM IS MADE. THE COMPACT CREATES NAMED WAYS TO STOP LYING WHILE INSTABILITY REMAINS.

Oru-Kel clicked approval without turning from the warning edge.

Haro transmitted it.

The committee did not answer.

That was not acceptance. It was only the next place pressure would gather.

Ren let that remain true.

The chamber lights dimmed into rest cycle. The compact stayed active in the basin as a living, ugly, load-bearing thing. It did not shine. It did not promise peace. It did not forgive the past or master the future.

It held relation without making difference disappear.

That had to be enough for the first tide.

Ren stepped away from the witness table and looked back once.

The Parliament remained divided.

The Parliament remained bound.

The Parliament remained salt.
